3311         /**
3312          * Produces a VarHandle giving access to a reflected field {@code f}
3313          * of type {@code T} declared in a class of type {@code R}.
3314          * The VarHandle's variable type is {@code T}.
3315          * If the field is non-static the VarHandle has one coordinate type,
3316          * {@code R}.  Otherwise, the field is static, and the VarHandle has no
3317          * coordinate types.
3318          * <p>
3319          * Access checking is performed immediately on behalf of the lookup
3320          * class, regardless of the value of the field's {@code accessible}
3321          * flag.
3322          * <p>
3323          * If the field is static, and if the returned VarHandle is operated
3324          * on, the field's declaring class will be initialized, if it has not
3325          * already been initialized.
3326          * <p>
3327          * Certain access modes of the returned VarHandle are unsupported under
3328          * the following conditions:
3329          * <ul>
3330          * <li>if the field is declared {@code final}, then the write, atomic
3331          *     update, numeric atomic update, and bitwise atomic update access
3332          *     modes are unsupported.
3333          * <li>if the field type is anything other than {@code byte},
3334          *     {@code short}, {@code char}, {@code int}, {@code long},
3335          *     {@code float}, or {@code double} then numeric atomic update
3336          *     access modes are unsupported.
3337          * <li>if the field type is anything other than {@code boolean},
3338          *     {@code byte}, {@code short}, {@code char}, {@code int} or
3339          *     {@code long} then bitwise atomic update access modes are
3340          *     unsupported.
3341          * </ul>
3342          * <p>
3343          * If the field is declared {@code volatile} then the returned VarHandle
3344          * will override access to the field (effectively ignore the
3345          * {@code volatile} declaration) in accordance to its specified
3346          * access modes.
3347          * <p>
3348          * If the field type is {@code float} or {@code double} then numeric
3349          * and atomic update access modes compare values using their bitwise
3350          * representation (see {@link Float#floatToRawIntBits} and
3351          * {@link Double#doubleToRawLongBits}, respectively).
3352          * @apiNote
3353          * Bitwise comparison of {@code float} values or {@code double} values,
3354          * as performed by the numeric and atomic update access modes, differ
3355          * from the primitive {@code ==} operator and the {@link Float#equals}
3356          * and {@link Double#equals} methods, specifically with respect to
3357          * comparing NaN values or comparing {@code -0.0} with {@code +0.0}.
3358          * Care should be taken when performing a compare and set or a compare
3359          * and exchange operation with such values since the operation may
3360          * unexpectedly fail.
3361          * There are many possible NaN values that are considered to be
3362          * {@code NaN} in Java, although no IEEE 754 floating-point operation
3363          * provided by Java can distinguish between them.  Operation failure can
3364          * occur if the expected or witness value is a NaN value and it is
3365          * transformed (perhaps in a platform specific manner) into another NaN
3366          * value, and thus has a different bitwise representation (see
3367          * {@link Float#intBitsToFloat} or {@link Double#longBitsToDouble} for more
3368          * details).
3369          * The values {@code -0.0} and {@code +0.0} have different bitwise
3370          * representations but are considered equal when using the primitive
3371          * {@code ==} operator.  Operation failure can occur if, for example, a
3372          * numeric algorithm computes an expected value to be say {@code -0.0}
3373          * and previously computed the witness value to be say {@code +0.0}.
3374          * @param f the reflected field, with a field of type {@code T}, and
3375          * a declaring class of type {@code R}
3376          * @return a VarHandle giving access to non-static fields or a static
3377          * field
3378          * @throws IllegalAccessException if access checking fails
3379          * @throws NullPointerException if the argument is null
3380          * @since 9
3381          */
3382         public VarHandle unreflectVarHandle(Field f) throws IllegalAccessException {
3383             MemberName getField = new MemberName(f, false);
3384             MemberName putField = new MemberName(f, true);
3385             return getFieldVarHandleNoSecurityManager(getField.getReferenceKind(), putField.getReferenceKind(),
3386                                                       f.getDeclaringClass(), getField, putField);
3387         }
3388 
3389         /**
3390          * Cracks a <a href="MethodHandleInfo.html#directmh">direct method handle</a>
3391          * created by this lookup object or a similar one.
3392          * Security and access checks are performed to ensure that this lookup object
3393          * is capable of reproducing the target method handle.
3394          * This means that the cracking may fail if target is a direct method handle
3395          * but was created by an unrelated lookup object.
3396          * This can happen if the method handle is <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#callsens">caller sensitive</a>
3397          * and was created by a lookup object for a different class.
3398          * @param target a direct method handle to crack into symbolic reference components
3399          * @return a symbolic reference which can be used to reconstruct this method handle from this lookup object
3400          * @throws    SecurityException if a security manager is present and it
3401          *                              <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#secmgr">refuses access</a>
3402          * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the target is not a direct method handle or if access checking fails
3403          * @throws    NullPointerException if the target is {@code null}
3404          * @see MethodHandleInfo
3405          * @since 1.8
3406          */
3407         public MethodHandleInfo revealDirect(MethodHandle target) {
3408             if (!target.isCrackable()) {
3409                 throw newIllegalArgumentException("not a direct method handle");
3410             }
3411             MemberName member = target.internalMemberName();
3412             Class<?> defc = member.getDeclaringClass();
3413             byte refKind = member.getReferenceKind();
3414             assert(MethodHandleNatives.refKindIsValid(refKind));
3415             if (refKind == REF_invokeSpecial && !target.isInvokeSpecial())
3416                 // Devirtualized method invocation is usually formally virtual.
3417                 // To avoid creating extra MemberName objects for this common case,
3418                 // we encode this extra degree of freedom using MH.isInvokeSpecial.
3419                 refKind = REF_invokeVirtual;
3420             if (refKind == REF_invokeVirtual && defc.isInterface())
3421                 // Symbolic reference is through interface but resolves to Object method (toString, etc.)
3422                 refKind = REF_invokeInterface;
3423             // Check SM permissions and member access before cracking.
3424             try {
3425                 checkAccess(refKind, defc, member);
3426                 checkSecurityManager(defc, member);
3427             } catch (IllegalAccessException ex) {
3428                 throw new IllegalArgumentException(ex);
3429             }
3430             if (allowedModes != TRUSTED && member.isCallerSensitive()) {
3431                 Class<?> callerClass = target.internalCallerClass();
3432                 if (!hasFullPrivilegeAccess() || callerClass != lookupClass())
3433                     throw new IllegalArgumentException("method handle is caller sensitive: "+callerClass);
3434             }
3435             // Produce the handle to the results.
3436             return new InfoFromMemberName(this, member, refKind);
3437         }
3438 
3439         /// Helper methods, all package-private.
3440 
3441         MemberName resolveOrFail(byte refKind, Class<?> refc, String name, Class<?> type) throws NoSuchFieldException, IllegalAccessException {
3442             checkSymbolicClass(refc);  // do this before attempting to resolve
3443             Objects.requireNonNull(name);
3444             Objects.requireNonNull(type);
3445             return IMPL_NAMES.resolveOrFail(refKind, new MemberName(refc, name, type, refKind), lookupClassOrNull(),
3446                                             NoSuchFieldException.class);
3447         }
3448 
3449         MemberName resolveOrFail(byte refKind, Class<?> refc, String name, MethodType type) throws NoSuchMethodException, IllegalAccessException {
3450             checkSymbolicClass(refc);  // do this before attempting to resolve
3451             Objects.requireNonNull(name);
3452             Objects.requireNonNull(type);
3453             checkMethodName(refKind, name);  // NPE check on name
3454             return IMPL_NAMES.resolveOrFail(refKind, new MemberName(refc, name, type, refKind), lookupClassOrNull(),
3455                                             NoSuchMethodException.class);
3456         }
3457 
3458         MemberName resolveOrFail(byte refKind, MemberName member) throws ReflectiveOperationException {
3459             checkSymbolicClass(member.getDeclaringClass());  // do this before attempting to resolve
3460             Objects.requireNonNull(member.getName());
3461             Objects.requireNonNull(member.getType());
3462             return IMPL_NAMES.resolveOrFail(refKind, member, lookupClassOrNull(),
3463                                             ReflectiveOperationException.class);
3464         }
3465 
3466         MemberName resolveOrNull(byte refKind, MemberName member) {
3467             // do this before attempting to resolve
3468             if (!isClassAccessible(member.getDeclaringClass())) {
3469                 return null;
3470             }
3471             Objects.requireNonNull(member.getName());
3472             Objects.requireNonNull(member.getType());
3473             return IMPL_NAMES.resolveOrNull(refKind, member, lookupClassOrNull());
3474         }
3475 
3476         void checkSymbolicClass(Class<?> refc) throws IllegalAccessException {
3477             if (!isClassAccessible(refc)) {
3478                 throw new MemberName(refc).makeAccessException("symbolic reference class is not accessible", this);
3479             }
3480         }
3481 
3482         boolean isClassAccessible(Class<?> refc) {
3483             Objects.requireNonNull(refc);
3484             Class<?> caller = lookupClassOrNull();
3485             return caller == null || VerifyAccess.isClassAccessible(refc, caller, prevLookupClass, allowedModes);
3486         }
3487 
3488         /** Check name for an illegal leading "&lt;" character. */
3489         void checkMethodName(byte refKind, String name) throws NoSuchMethodException {
3490             if (name.startsWith("<") && refKind != REF_newInvokeSpecial)
3491                 throw new NoSuchMethodException("illegal method name: "+name);
3492         }
3493 
3494 
3495         /**
3496          * Find my trustable caller class if m is a caller sensitive method.
3497          * If this lookup object has full privilege access, then the caller class is the lookupClass.
3498          * Otherwise, if m is caller-sensitive, throw IllegalAccessException.
3499          */
3500         Lookup findBoundCallerLookup(MemberName m) throws IllegalAccessException {
3501             if (MethodHandleNatives.isCallerSensitive(m) && !hasFullPrivilegeAccess()) {
3502                 // Only lookups with full privilege access are allowed to resolve caller-sensitive methods
3503                 throw new IllegalAccessException("Attempt to lookup caller-sensitive method using restricted lookup object");
3504             }
3505             return this;
3506         }
3507 
3508         /**
3509          * Returns {@code true} if this lookup has {@code PRIVATE} and {@code MODULE} access.
3510          * @return {@code true} if this lookup has {@code PRIVATE} and {@code MODULE} access.
3511          *
3512          * @deprecated This method was originally designed to test {@code PRIVATE} access
3513          * that implies full privilege access but {@code MODULE} access has since become
3514          * independent of {@code PRIVATE} access.  It is recommended to call
3515          * {@link #hasFullPrivilegeAccess()} instead.
3516          * @since 9
3517          */
3518         @Deprecated(since="14")
3519         public boolean hasPrivateAccess() {
3520             return hasFullPrivilegeAccess();
3521         }
3522 
3523         /**
3524          * Returns {@code true} if this lookup has <em>full privilege access</em>,
3525          * i.e. {@code PRIVATE} and {@code MODULE} access.
3526          * A {@code Lookup} object must have full privilege access in order to
3527          * access all members that are allowed to the {@linkplain #lookupClass() lookup class}.
3528          *
3529          * @return {@code true} if this lookup has full privilege access.
3530          * @since 14
3531          * @see <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#privacc">private and module access</a>
3532          */
3533         public boolean hasFullPrivilegeAccess() {
3534             return (allowedModes & (PRIVATE|MODULE)) == (PRIVATE|MODULE);
3535         }
3536 
3537         /**
3538          * Perform steps 1 and 2b <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#secmgr">access checks</a>
3539          * for ensureInitialzed, findClass or accessClass.
3540          */
3541         void checkSecurityManager(Class<?> refc) {
3542             if (allowedModes == TRUSTED)  return;
3543 
3544             SecurityManager smgr = System.getSecurityManager();
3545             if (smgr == null)  return;
3546 
3547             // Step 1:
3548             boolean fullPowerLookup = hasFullPrivilegeAccess();
3549             if (!fullPowerLookup ||
3550                 !VerifyAccess.classLoaderIsAncestor(lookupClass, refc)) {
3551                 ReflectUtil.checkPackageAccess(refc);
3552             }
3553 
3554             // Step 2b:
3555             if (!fullPowerLookup) {
3556                 smgr.checkPermission(SecurityConstants.GET_CLASSLOADER_PERMISSION);
3557             }
3558         }
3559 
3560         /**
3561          * Perform steps 1, 2a and 3 <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#secmgr">access checks</a>.
3562          * Determines a trustable caller class to compare with refc, the symbolic reference class.
3563          * If this lookup object has full privilege access, then the caller class is the lookupClass.
3564          */
3565         void checkSecurityManager(Class<?> refc, MemberName m) {
3566             Objects.requireNonNull(refc);
3567             Objects.requireNonNull(m);
3568 
3569             if (allowedModes == TRUSTED)  return;
3570 
3571             SecurityManager smgr = System.getSecurityManager();
3572             if (smgr == null)  return;
3573 
3574             // Step 1:
3575             boolean fullPowerLookup = hasFullPrivilegeAccess();
3576             if (!fullPowerLookup ||
3577                 !VerifyAccess.classLoaderIsAncestor(lookupClass, refc)) {
3578                 ReflectUtil.checkPackageAccess(refc);
3579             }
3580 








3581             // Step 2a:
3582             if (m.isPublic()) return;
3583             if (!fullPowerLookup) {
3584                 smgr.checkPermission(SecurityConstants.CHECK_MEMBER_ACCESS_PERMISSION);
3585             }
3586 
3587             // Step 3:
3588             Class<?> defc = m.getDeclaringClass();
3589             if (!fullPowerLookup && defc != refc) {
3590                 ReflectUtil.checkPackageAccess(defc);
3591             }
3592         }
3593 
3594         void checkMethod(byte refKind, Class<?> refc, MemberName m) throws IllegalAccessException {
3595             boolean wantStatic = (refKind == REF_invokeStatic);
3596             String message;
3597             if (m.isConstructor())
3598                 message = "expected a method, not a constructor";
3599             else if (!m.isMethod())
3600                 message = "expected a method";
3601             else if (wantStatic != m.isStatic())
3602                 message = wantStatic ? "expected a static method" : "expected a non-static method";
3603             else
3604                 { checkAccess(refKind, refc, m); return; }
3605             throw m.makeAccessException(message, this);
3606         }
3607 
3608         void checkField(byte refKind, Class<?> refc, MemberName m) throws IllegalAccessException {
3609             boolean wantStatic = !MethodHandleNatives.refKindHasReceiver(refKind);
3610             String message;
3611             if (wantStatic != m.isStatic())
3612                 message = wantStatic ? "expected a static field" : "expected a non-static field";
3613             else
3614                 { checkAccess(refKind, refc, m); return; }
3615             throw m.makeAccessException(message, this);
3616         }
3617 
3618         /** Check public/protected/private bits on the symbolic reference class and its member. */
3619         void checkAccess(byte refKind, Class<?> refc, MemberName m) throws IllegalAccessException {
3620             assert(m.referenceKindIsConsistentWith(refKind) &&
3621                    MethodHandleNatives.refKindIsValid(refKind) &&
3622                    (MethodHandleNatives.refKindIsField(refKind) == m.isField()));
3623             int allowedModes = this.allowedModes;
3624             if (allowedModes == TRUSTED)  return;
3625             int mods = m.getModifiers();
3626             if (Modifier.isProtected(mods) &&
3627                     refKind == REF_invokeVirtual &&
3628                     m.getDeclaringClass() == Object.class &&
3629                     m.getName().equals("clone") &&
3630                     refc.isArray()) {
3631                 // The JVM does this hack also.
3632                 // (See ClassVerifier::verify_invoke_instructions
3633                 // and LinkResolver::check_method_accessability.)
3634                 // Because the JVM does not allow separate methods on array types,
3635                 // there is no separate method for int[].clone.
3636                 // All arrays simply inherit Object.clone.
3637                 // But for access checking logic, we make Object.clone
3638                 // (normally protected) appear to be public.
3639                 // Later on, when the DirectMethodHandle is created,
3640                 // its leading argument will be restricted to the
3641                 // requested array type.
3642                 // N.B. The return type is not adjusted, because
3643                 // that is *not* the bytecode behavior.
3644                 mods ^= Modifier.PROTECTED | Modifier.PUBLIC;
3645             }
3646             if (Modifier.isProtected(mods) && refKind == REF_newInvokeSpecial) {
3647                 // cannot "new" a protected ctor in a different package
3648                 mods ^= Modifier.PROTECTED;
3649             }
3650             if (Modifier.isFinal(mods) &&
3651                     MethodHandleNatives.refKindIsSetter(refKind))
3652                 throw m.makeAccessException("unexpected set of a final field", this);
3653             int requestedModes = fixmods(mods);  // adjust 0 => PACKAGE
3654             if ((requestedModes & allowedModes) != 0) {
3655                 if (VerifyAccess.isMemberAccessible(refc, m.getDeclaringClass(),
3656                                                     mods, lookupClass(), previousLookupClass(), allowedModes))
3657                     return;
3658             } else {
3659                 // Protected members can also be checked as if they were package-private.
3660                 if ((requestedModes & PROTECTED) != 0 && (allowedModes & PACKAGE) != 0
3661                         && VerifyAccess.isSamePackage(m.getDeclaringClass(), lookupClass()))
3662                     return;
3663             }
3664             throw m.makeAccessException(accessFailedMessage(refc, m), this);
3665         }
3666 
3667         String accessFailedMessage(Class<?> refc, MemberName m) {
3668             Class<?> defc = m.getDeclaringClass();
3669             int mods = m.getModifiers();
3670             // check the class first:
3671             boolean classOK = (Modifier.isPublic(defc.getModifiers()) &&
3672                                (defc == refc ||
3673                                 Modifier.isPublic(refc.getModifiers())));
3674             if (!classOK && (allowedModes & PACKAGE) != 0) {
3675                 // ignore previous lookup class to check if default package access
3676                 classOK = (VerifyAccess.isClassAccessible(defc, lookupClass(), null, FULL_POWER_MODES) &&
3677                            (defc == refc ||
3678                             VerifyAccess.isClassAccessible(refc, lookupClass(), null, FULL_POWER_MODES)));
3679             }
3680             if (!classOK)
3681                 return "class is not public";
3682             if (Modifier.isPublic(mods))
3683                 return "access to public member failed";  // (how?, module not readable?)
3684             if (Modifier.isPrivate(mods))
3685                 return "member is private";
3686             if (Modifier.isProtected(mods))
3687                 return "member is protected";
3688             return "member is private to package";
3689         }
3690 
3691         private void checkSpecialCaller(Class<?> specialCaller, Class<?> refc) throws IllegalAccessException {
3692             int allowedModes = this.allowedModes;
3693             if (allowedModes == TRUSTED)  return;
3694             if ((lookupModes() & PRIVATE) == 0
3695                 || (specialCaller != lookupClass()
3696                        // ensure non-abstract methods in superinterfaces can be special-invoked
3697                     && !(refc != null && refc.isInterface() && refc.isAssignableFrom(specialCaller))))
3698                 throw new MemberName(specialCaller).
3699                     makeAccessException("no private access for invokespecial", this);
3700         }
3701 
3702         private boolean restrictProtectedReceiver(MemberName method) {
3703             // The accessing class only has the right to use a protected member
3704             // on itself or a subclass.  Enforce that restriction, from JVMS 5.4.4, etc.
3705             if (!method.isProtected() || method.isStatic()
3706                 || allowedModes == TRUSTED
3707                 || method.getDeclaringClass() == lookupClass()
3708                 || VerifyAccess.isSamePackage(method.getDeclaringClass(), lookupClass()))
3709                 return false;
3710             return true;
3711         }
3712         private MethodHandle restrictReceiver(MemberName method, DirectMethodHandle mh, Class<?> caller) throws IllegalAccessException {
3713             assert(!method.isStatic());
3714             // receiver type of mh is too wide; narrow to caller
3715             if (!method.getDeclaringClass().isAssignableFrom(caller)) {
3716                 throw method.makeAccessException("caller class must be a subclass below the method", caller);
3717             }
3718             MethodType rawType = mh.type();
3719             if (caller.isAssignableFrom(rawType.parameterType(0))) return mh; // no need to restrict; already narrow
3720             MethodType narrowType = rawType.changeParameterType(0, caller);
3721             assert(!mh.isVarargsCollector());  // viewAsType will lose varargs-ness
3722             assert(mh.viewAsTypeChecks(narrowType, true));
3723             return mh.copyWith(narrowType, mh.form);
3724         }
3725 
3726         /** Check access and get the requested method. */
3727         private MethodHandle getDirectMethod(byte refKind, Class<?> refc, MemberName method, Lookup callerLookup) throws IllegalAccessException {
3728             final boolean doRestrict    = true;
3729             final boolean checkSecurity = true;
3730             return getDirectMethodCommon(refKind, refc, method, checkSecurity, doRestrict, callerLookup);
3731         }
3732         /** Check access and get the requested method, for invokespecial with no restriction on the application of narrowing rules. */
3733         private MethodHandle getDirectMethodNoRestrictInvokeSpecial(Class<?> refc, MemberName method, Lookup callerLookup) throws IllegalAccessException {
3734             final boolean doRestrict    = false;
3735             final boolean checkSecurity = true;
3736             return getDirectMethodCommon(REF_invokeSpecial, refc, method, checkSecurity, doRestrict, callerLookup);
3737         }
3738         /** Check access and get the requested method, eliding security manager checks. */
3739         private MethodHandle getDirectMethodNoSecurityManager(byte refKind, Class<?> refc, MemberName method, Lookup callerLookup) throws IllegalAccessException {
3740             final boolean doRestrict    = true;
3741             final boolean checkSecurity = false;  // not needed for reflection or for linking CONSTANT_MH constants
3742             return getDirectMethodCommon(refKind, refc, method, checkSecurity, doRestrict, callerLookup);
3743         }
3744         /** Common code for all methods; do not call directly except from immediately above. */
3745         private MethodHandle getDirectMethodCommon(byte refKind, Class<?> refc, MemberName method,
3746                                                    boolean checkSecurity,
3747                                                    boolean doRestrict,
3748                                                    Lookup boundCaller) throws IllegalAccessException {
3749             checkMethod(refKind, refc, method);
3750             // Optionally check with the security manager; this isn't needed for unreflect* calls.
3751             if (checkSecurity)
3752                 checkSecurityManager(refc, method);
3753             assert(!method.isMethodHandleInvoke());
3754 
3755             if (refKind == REF_invokeSpecial &&
3756                 refc != lookupClass() &&
3757                 !refc.isInterface() &&
3758                 refc != lookupClass().getSuperclass() &&
3759                 refc.isAssignableFrom(lookupClass())) {
3760                 assert(!method.getName().equals("<init>"));  // not this code path
3761 
3762                 // Per JVMS 6.5, desc. of invokespecial instruction:
3763                 // If the method is in a superclass of the LC,
3764                 // and if our original search was above LC.super,
3765                 // repeat the search (symbolic lookup) from LC.super
3766                 // and continue with the direct superclass of that class,
3767                 // and so forth, until a match is found or no further superclasses exist.
3768                 // FIXME: MemberName.resolve should handle this instead.
3769                 Class<?> refcAsSuper = lookupClass();
3770                 MemberName m2;
3771                 do {
3772                     refcAsSuper = refcAsSuper.getSuperclass();
3773                     m2 = new MemberName(refcAsSuper,
3774                                         method.getName(),
3775                                         method.getMethodType(),
3776                                         REF_invokeSpecial);
3777                     m2 = IMPL_NAMES.resolveOrNull(refKind, m2, lookupClassOrNull());
3778                 } while (m2 == null &&         // no method is found yet
3779                          refc != refcAsSuper); // search up to refc
3780                 if (m2 == null)  throw new InternalError(method.toString());
3781                 method = m2;
3782                 refc = refcAsSuper;
3783                 // redo basic checks
3784                 checkMethod(refKind, refc, method);
3785             }
3786             DirectMethodHandle dmh = DirectMethodHandle.make(refKind, refc, method, lookupClass());
3787             MethodHandle mh = dmh;
3788             // Optionally narrow the receiver argument to lookupClass using restrictReceiver.
3789             if ((doRestrict && refKind == REF_invokeSpecial) ||
3790                     (MethodHandleNatives.refKindHasReceiver(refKind) && restrictProtectedReceiver(method))) {
3791                 mh = restrictReceiver(method, dmh, lookupClass());
3792             }
3793             mh = maybeBindCaller(method, mh, boundCaller);
3794             mh = mh.setVarargs(method);
3795             return mh;
3796         }
3797         private MethodHandle maybeBindCaller(MemberName method, MethodHandle mh, Lookup boundCaller)
3798                                              throws IllegalAccessException {
3799             if (boundCaller.allowedModes == TRUSTED || !MethodHandleNatives.isCallerSensitive(method))
3800                 return mh;
3801 
3802             // boundCaller must have full privilege access.
3803             // It should have been checked by findBoundCallerLookup. Safe to check this again.
3804             if (!boundCaller.hasFullPrivilegeAccess())
3805                 throw new IllegalAccessException("Attempt to lookup caller-sensitive method using restricted lookup object");
3806 
3807             MethodHandle cbmh = MethodHandleImpl.bindCaller(mh, boundCaller.lookupClass);
3808             // Note: caller will apply varargs after this step happens.
3809             return cbmh;
3810         }
3811 
3812         /** Check access and get the requested field. */
3813         private MethodHandle getDirectField(byte refKind, Class<?> refc, MemberName field) throws IllegalAccessException {
3814             final boolean checkSecurity = true;
3815             return getDirectFieldCommon(refKind, refc, field, checkSecurity);
3816         }
3817         /** Check access and get the requested field, eliding security manager checks. */
3818         private MethodHandle getDirectFieldNoSecurityManager(byte refKind, Class<?> refc, MemberName field) throws IllegalAccessException {
3819             final boolean checkSecurity = false;  // not needed for reflection or for linking CONSTANT_MH constants
3820             return getDirectFieldCommon(refKind, refc, field, checkSecurity);
3821         }
3822         /** Common code for all fields; do not call directly except from immediately above. */
3823         private MethodHandle getDirectFieldCommon(byte refKind, Class<?> refc, MemberName field,
3824                                                   boolean checkSecurity) throws IllegalAccessException {
3825             checkField(refKind, refc, field);
3826             // Optionally check with the security manager; this isn't needed for unreflect* calls.
3827             if (checkSecurity)
3828                 checkSecurityManager(refc, field);
3829             DirectMethodHandle dmh = DirectMethodHandle.make(refc, field);
3830             boolean doRestrict = (MethodHandleNatives.refKindHasReceiver(refKind) &&
3831                                     restrictProtectedReceiver(field));
3832             if (doRestrict)
3833                 return restrictReceiver(field, dmh, lookupClass());
3834             return dmh;
3835         }
3836         private VarHandle getFieldVarHandle(byte getRefKind, byte putRefKind,
3837                                             Class<?> refc, MemberName getField, MemberName putField)
3838                 throws IllegalAccessException {
3839             final boolean checkSecurity = true;
3840             return getFieldVarHandleCommon(getRefKind, putRefKind, refc, getField, putField, checkSecurity);
3841         }
3842         private VarHandle getFieldVarHandleNoSecurityManager(byte getRefKind, byte putRefKind,
3843                                                              Class<?> refc, MemberName getField, MemberName putField)
3844                 throws IllegalAccessException {
3845             final boolean checkSecurity = false;
3846             return getFieldVarHandleCommon(getRefKind, putRefKind, refc, getField, putField, checkSecurity);
3847         }
3848         private VarHandle getFieldVarHandleCommon(byte getRefKind, byte putRefKind,
3849                                                   Class<?> refc, MemberName getField, MemberName putField,
3850                                                   boolean checkSecurity) throws IllegalAccessException {
3851             assert getField.isStatic() == putField.isStatic();
3852             assert getField.isGetter() && putField.isSetter();
3853             assert MethodHandleNatives.refKindIsStatic(getRefKind) == MethodHandleNatives.refKindIsStatic(putRefKind);
3854             assert MethodHandleNatives.refKindIsGetter(getRefKind) && MethodHandleNatives.refKindIsSetter(putRefKind);
3855 
3856             checkField(getRefKind, refc, getField);
3857             if (checkSecurity)
3858                 checkSecurityManager(refc, getField);
3859 
3860             if (!putField.isFinal()) {
3861                 // A VarHandle does not support updates to final fields, any
3862                 // such VarHandle to a final field will be read-only and
3863                 // therefore the following write-based accessibility checks are
3864                 // only required for non-final fields
3865                 checkField(putRefKind, refc, putField);
3866                 if (checkSecurity)
3867                     checkSecurityManager(refc, putField);
3868             }
3869 
3870             boolean doRestrict = (MethodHandleNatives.refKindHasReceiver(getRefKind) &&
3871                                   restrictProtectedReceiver(getField));
3872             if (doRestrict) {
3873                 assert !getField.isStatic();
3874                 // receiver type of VarHandle is too wide; narrow to caller
3875                 if (!getField.getDeclaringClass().isAssignableFrom(lookupClass())) {
3876                     throw getField.makeAccessException("caller class must be a subclass below the method", lookupClass());
3877                 }
3878                 refc = lookupClass();
3879             }
3880             return VarHandles.makeFieldHandle(getField, refc, getField.getFieldType(),
3881                                               this.allowedModes == TRUSTED && !getField.isTrustedFinalField());
3882         }
3883         /** Check access and get the requested constructor. */
3884         private MethodHandle getDirectConstructor(Class<?> refc, MemberName ctor) throws IllegalAccessException {
3885             final boolean checkSecurity = true;
3886             return getDirectConstructorCommon(refc, ctor, checkSecurity);
3887         }
3888         /** Check access and get the requested constructor, eliding security manager checks. */
3889         private MethodHandle getDirectConstructorNoSecurityManager(Class<?> refc, MemberName ctor) throws IllegalAccessException {
3890             final boolean checkSecurity = false;  // not needed for reflection or for linking CONSTANT_MH constants
3891             return getDirectConstructorCommon(refc, ctor, checkSecurity);
3892         }
3893         /** Common code for all constructors; do not call directly except from immediately above. */
3894         private MethodHandle getDirectConstructorCommon(Class<?> refc, MemberName ctor,
3895                                                   boolean checkSecurity) throws IllegalAccessException {
3896             assert(ctor.isConstructor());
3897             checkAccess(REF_newInvokeSpecial, refc, ctor);
3898             // Optionally check with the security manager; this isn't needed for unreflect* calls.
3899             if (checkSecurity)
3900                 checkSecurityManager(refc, ctor);
3901             assert(!MethodHandleNatives.isCallerSensitive(ctor));  // maybeBindCaller not relevant here
3902             return DirectMethodHandle.make(ctor).setVarargs(ctor);
3903         }
3904 
3905         /** Hook called from the JVM (via MethodHandleNatives) to link MH constants:
3906          */
3907         /*non-public*/
3908         MethodHandle linkMethodHandleConstant(byte refKind, Class<?> defc, String name, Object type)
3909                 throws ReflectiveOperationException {
3910             if (!(type instanceof Class || type instanceof MethodType))
3911                 throw new InternalError("unresolved MemberName");
3912             MemberName member = new MemberName(refKind, defc, name, type);
3913             MethodHandle mh = LOOKASIDE_TABLE.get(member);
3914             if (mh != null) {
3915                 checkSymbolicClass(defc);
3916                 return mh;
3917             }
3918             if (defc == MethodHandle.class && refKind == REF_invokeVirtual) {
3919                 // Treat MethodHandle.invoke and invokeExact specially.
3920                 mh = findVirtualForMH(member.getName(), member.getMethodType());
3921                 if (mh != null) {
3922                     return mh;
3923                 }
3924             } else if (defc == VarHandle.class && refKind == REF_invokeVirtual) {
3925                 // Treat signature-polymorphic methods on VarHandle specially.
3926                 mh = findVirtualForVH(member.getName(), member.getMethodType());
3927                 if (mh != null) {
3928                     return mh;
3929                 }
3930             }
3931             MemberName resolved = resolveOrFail(refKind, member);
3932             mh = getDirectMethodForConstant(refKind, defc, resolved);
3933             if (mh instanceof DirectMethodHandle
3934                     && canBeCached(refKind, defc, resolved)) {
3935                 MemberName key = mh.internalMemberName();
3936                 if (key != null) {
3937                     key = key.asNormalOriginal();
3938                 }
3939                 if (member.equals(key)) {  // better safe than sorry
3940                     LOOKASIDE_TABLE.put(key, (DirectMethodHandle) mh);
3941                 }
3942             }
3943             return mh;
3944         }
3945         private boolean canBeCached(byte refKind, Class<?> defc, MemberName member) {
3946             if (refKind == REF_invokeSpecial) {
3947                 return false;
3948             }
3949             if (!Modifier.isPublic(defc.getModifiers()) ||
3950                     !Modifier.isPublic(member.getDeclaringClass().getModifiers()) ||
3951                     !member.isPublic() ||
3952                     member.isCallerSensitive()) {
3953                 return false;
3954             }
3955             ClassLoader loader = defc.getClassLoader();
3956             if (loader != null) {
3957                 ClassLoader sysl = ClassLoader.getSystemClassLoader();
3958                 boolean found = false;
3959                 while (sysl != null) {
3960                     if (loader == sysl) { found = true; break; }
3961                     sysl = sysl.getParent();
3962                 }
3963                 if (!found) {
3964                     return false;
3965                 }
3966             }
3967             try {
3968                 MemberName resolved2 = publicLookup().resolveOrNull(refKind,
3969                     new MemberName(refKind, defc, member.getName(), member.getType()));
3970                 if (resolved2 == null) {
3971                     return false;
3972                 }
3973                 checkSecurityManager(defc, resolved2);
3974             } catch (SecurityException ex) {
3975                 return false;
3976             }
3977             return true;
3978         }
3979         private MethodHandle getDirectMethodForConstant(byte refKind, Class<?> defc, MemberName member)
3980                 throws ReflectiveOperationException {
3981             if (MethodHandleNatives.refKindIsField(refKind)) {
3982                 return getDirectFieldNoSecurityManager(refKind, defc, member);
3983             } else if (MethodHandleNatives.refKindIsMethod(refKind)) {
3984                 return getDirectMethodNoSecurityManager(refKind, defc, member, findBoundCallerLookup(member));
3985             } else if (refKind == REF_newInvokeSpecial) {
3986                 return getDirectConstructorNoSecurityManager(defc, member);
3987             }
3988             // oops
3989             throw newIllegalArgumentException("bad MethodHandle constant #"+member);
3990         }
3991 
3992         static ConcurrentHashMap<MemberName, DirectMethodHandle> LOOKASIDE_TABLE = new ConcurrentHashMap<>();
3993     }

3995     /**
3996      * Produces a method handle constructing arrays of a desired type,
3997      * as if by the {@code anewarray} bytecode.
3998      * The return type of the method handle will be the array type.
3999      * The type of its sole argument will be {@code int}, which specifies the size of the array.
4000      *
4001      * <p> If the returned method handle is invoked with a negative
4002      * array size, a {@code NegativeArraySizeException} will be thrown.
4003      *
4004      * @param arrayClass an array type
4005      * @return a method handle which can create arrays of the given type
4006      * @throws NullPointerException if the argument is {@code null}
4007      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if {@code arrayClass} is not an array type
4008      * @see java.lang.reflect.Array#newInstance(Class, int)
4009      * @jvms 6.5 {@code anewarray} Instruction
4010      * @since 9
4011      */
4012     public static MethodHandle arrayConstructor(Class<?> arrayClass) throws IllegalArgumentException {
4013         if (!arrayClass.isArray()) {
4014             throw newIllegalArgumentException("not an array class: " + arrayClass.getName());
4015         }
4016         MethodHandle ani = MethodHandleImpl.getConstantHandle(MethodHandleImpl.MH_Array_newInstance).
4017                 bindTo(arrayClass.getComponentType());
4018         return ani.asType(ani.type().changeReturnType(arrayClass));
4019     }

4089     /**
4090      * Produces a VarHandle giving access to elements of an array of type
4091      * {@code arrayClass}.  The VarHandle's variable type is the component type
4092      * of {@code arrayClass} and the list of coordinate types is
4093      * {@code (arrayClass, int)}, where the {@code int} coordinate type
4094      * corresponds to an argument that is an index into an array.
4095      * <p>
4096      * Certain access modes of the returned VarHandle are unsupported under
4097      * the following conditions:
4098      * <ul>
4099      * <li>if the component type is anything other than {@code byte},
4100      *     {@code short}, {@code char}, {@code int}, {@code long},
4101      *     {@code float}, or {@code double} then numeric atomic update access
4102      *     modes are unsupported.
4103      * <li>if the component type is anything other than {@code boolean},
4104      *     {@code byte}, {@code short}, {@code char}, {@code int} or
4105      *     {@code long} then bitwise atomic update access modes are
4106      *     unsupported.
4107      * </ul>
4108      * <p>
4109      * If the component type is {@code float} or {@code double} then numeric
4110      * and atomic update access modes compare values using their bitwise
4111      * representation (see {@link Float#floatToRawIntBits} and
4112      * {@link Double#doubleToRawLongBits}, respectively).
4113      *
4114      * <p> When the returned {@code VarHandle} is invoked,
4115      * the array reference and array index are checked.
4116      * A {@code NullPointerException} will be thrown if the array reference
4117      * is {@code null} and an {@code ArrayIndexOutOfBoundsException} will be
4118      * thrown if the index is negative or if it is greater than or equal to
4119      * the length of the array.
4120      *
4121      * @apiNote
4122      * Bitwise comparison of {@code float} values or {@code double} values,
4123      * as performed by the numeric and atomic update access modes, differ
4124      * from the primitive {@code ==} operator and the {@link Float#equals}
4125      * and {@link Double#equals} methods, specifically with respect to
4126      * comparing NaN values or comparing {@code -0.0} with {@code +0.0}.
4127      * Care should be taken when performing a compare and set or a compare
4128      * and exchange operation with such values since the operation may
4129      * unexpectedly fail.
4130      * There are many possible NaN values that are considered to be
4131      * {@code NaN} in Java, although no IEEE 754 floating-point operation
4132      * provided by Java can distinguish between them.  Operation failure can
4133      * occur if the expected or witness value is a NaN value and it is
4134      * transformed (perhaps in a platform specific manner) into another NaN
4135      * value, and thus has a different bitwise representation (see
4136      * {@link Float#intBitsToFloat} or {@link Double#longBitsToDouble} for more
4137      * details).
4138      * The values {@code -0.0} and {@code +0.0} have different bitwise
4139      * representations but are considered equal when using the primitive
4140      * {@code ==} operator.  Operation failure can occur if, for example, a
4141      * numeric algorithm computes an expected value to be say {@code -0.0}
4142      * and previously computed the witness value to be say {@code +0.0}.
4143      * @param arrayClass the class of an array, of type {@code T[]}
4144      * @return a VarHandle giving access to elements of an array
4145      * @throws NullPointerException if the arrayClass is null
4146      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if arrayClass is not an array type
4147      * @since 9
4148      */
4149     public static VarHandle arrayElementVarHandle(Class<?> arrayClass) throws IllegalArgumentException {
4150         return VarHandles.makeArrayElementHandle(arrayClass);
4151     }
4152 
4153     /**
4154      * Produces a VarHandle giving access to elements of a {@code byte[]} array
4155      * viewed as if it were a different primitive array type, such as
4156      * {@code int[]} or {@code long[]}.
4157      * The VarHandle's variable type is the component type of
4158      * {@code viewArrayClass} and the list of coordinate types is
4159      * {@code (byte[], int)}, where the {@code int} coordinate type
4160      * corresponds to an argument that is an index into a {@code byte[]} array.
4161      * The returned VarHandle accesses bytes at an index in a {@code byte[]}
4162      * array, composing bytes to or from a value of the component type of
4163      * {@code viewArrayClass} according to the given endianness.
4164      * <p>
4165      * The supported component types (variables types) are {@code short},
4166      * {@code char}, {@code int}, {@code long}, {@code float} and
4167      * {@code double}.
4168      * <p>
4169      * Access of bytes at a given index will result in an
4170      * {@code IndexOutOfBoundsException} if the index is less than {@code 0}
4171      * or greater than the {@code byte[]} array length minus the size (in bytes)
4172      * of {@code T}.
4173      * <p>
4174      * Access of bytes at an index may be aligned or misaligned for {@code T},
4175      * with respect to the underlying memory address, {@code A} say, associated
4176      * with the array and index.
4177      * If access is misaligned then access for anything other than the
4178      * {@code get} and {@code set} access modes will result in an
4179      * {@code IllegalStateException}.  In such cases atomic access is only
4180      * guaranteed with respect to the largest power of two that divides the GCD
4181      * of {@code A} and the size (in bytes) of {@code T}.
4182      * If access is aligned then following access modes are supported and are
4183      * guaranteed to support atomic access:
4184      * <ul>
4185      * <li>read write access modes for all {@code T}, with the exception of
4186      *     access modes {@code get} and {@code set} for {@code long} and
4187      *     {@code double} on 32-bit platforms.
4188      * <li>atomic update access modes for {@code int}, {@code long},
4189      *     {@code float} or {@code double}.
4190      *     (Future major platform releases of the JDK may support additional
4191      *     types for certain currently unsupported access modes.)
4192      * <li>numeric atomic update access modes for {@code int} and {@code long}.
4193      *     (Future major platform releases of the JDK may support additional
4194      *     numeric types for certain currently unsupported access modes.)
4195      * <li>bitwise atomic update access modes for {@code int} and {@code long}.
4196      *     (Future major platform releases of the JDK may support additional
4197      *     numeric types for certain currently unsupported access modes.)
4198      * </ul>
4199      * <p>
4200      * Misaligned access, and therefore atomicity guarantees, may be determined
4201      * for {@code byte[]} arrays without operating on a specific array.  Given
4202      * an {@code index}, {@code T} and it's corresponding boxed type,
4203      * {@code T_BOX}, misalignment may be determined as follows:
4204      * <pre>{@code
4205      * int sizeOfT = T_BOX.BYTES;  // size in bytes of T
4206      * int misalignedAtZeroIndex = ByteBuffer.wrap(new byte[0]).
4207      *     alignmentOffset(0, sizeOfT);
4208      * int misalignedAtIndex = (misalignedAtZeroIndex + index) % sizeOfT;
4209      * boolean isMisaligned = misalignedAtIndex != 0;
4210      * }</pre>
4211      * <p>
4212      * If the variable type is {@code float} or {@code double} then atomic
4213      * update access modes compare values using their bitwise representation
4214      * (see {@link Float#floatToRawIntBits} and
4215      * {@link Double#doubleToRawLongBits}, respectively).
4216      * @param viewArrayClass the view array class, with a component type of
4217      * type {@code T}
4218      * @param byteOrder the endianness of the view array elements, as
4219      * stored in the underlying {@code byte} array
4220      * @return a VarHandle giving access to elements of a {@code byte[]} array
4221      * viewed as if elements corresponding to the components type of the view
4222      * array class
4223      * @throws NullPointerException if viewArrayClass or byteOrder is null
4224      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if viewArrayClass is not an array type
4225      * @throws UnsupportedOperationException if the component type of
4226      * viewArrayClass is not supported as a variable type
4227      * @since 9
4228      */
4229     public static VarHandle byteArrayViewVarHandle(Class<?> viewArrayClass,
4230                                      ByteOrder byteOrder) throws IllegalArgumentException {
4231         Objects.requireNonNull(byteOrder);
4232         return VarHandles.byteArrayViewHandle(viewArrayClass,
4233                                               byteOrder == ByteOrder.BIG_ENDIAN);
4234     }
4235 
4236     /**
4237      * Produces a VarHandle giving access to elements of a {@code ByteBuffer}
4238      * viewed as if it were an array of elements of a different primitive
4239      * component type to that of {@code byte}, such as {@code int[]} or
4240      * {@code long[]}.
4241      * The VarHandle's variable type is the component type of
4242      * {@code viewArrayClass} and the list of coordinate types is
4243      * {@code (ByteBuffer, int)}, where the {@code int} coordinate type
4244      * corresponds to an argument that is an index into a {@code byte[]} array.
4245      * The returned VarHandle accesses bytes at an index in a
4246      * {@code ByteBuffer}, composing bytes to or from a value of the component
4247      * type of {@code viewArrayClass} according to the given endianness.
4248      * <p>
4249      * The supported component types (variables types) are {@code short},
4250      * {@code char}, {@code int}, {@code long}, {@code float} and
4251      * {@code double}.
4252      * <p>
4253      * Access will result in a {@code ReadOnlyBufferException} for anything
4254      * other than the read access modes if the {@code ByteBuffer} is read-only.
4255      * <p>
4256      * Access of bytes at a given index will result in an
4257      * {@code IndexOutOfBoundsException} if the index is less than {@code 0}
4258      * or greater than the {@code ByteBuffer} limit minus the size (in bytes) of
4259      * {@code T}.
4260      * <p>
4261      * Access of bytes at an index may be aligned or misaligned for {@code T},
4262      * with respect to the underlying memory address, {@code A} say, associated
4263      * with the {@code ByteBuffer} and index.
4264      * If access is misaligned then access for anything other than the
4265      * {@code get} and {@code set} access modes will result in an
4266      * {@code IllegalStateException}.  In such cases atomic access is only
4267      * guaranteed with respect to the largest power of two that divides the GCD
4268      * of {@code A} and the size (in bytes) of {@code T}.
4269      * If access is aligned then following access modes are supported and are
4270      * guaranteed to support atomic access:
4271      * <ul>
4272      * <li>read write access modes for all {@code T}, with the exception of
4273      *     access modes {@code get} and {@code set} for {@code long} and
4274      *     {@code double} on 32-bit platforms.
4275      * <li>atomic update access modes for {@code int}, {@code long},
4276      *     {@code float} or {@code double}.
4277      *     (Future major platform releases of the JDK may support additional
4278      *     types for certain currently unsupported access modes.)
4279      * <li>numeric atomic update access modes for {@code int} and {@code long}.
4280      *     (Future major platform releases of the JDK may support additional
4281      *     numeric types for certain currently unsupported access modes.)
4282      * <li>bitwise atomic update access modes for {@code int} and {@code long}.
4283      *     (Future major platform releases of the JDK may support additional
4284      *     numeric types for certain currently unsupported access modes.)
4285      * </ul>
4286      * <p>
4287      * Misaligned access, and therefore atomicity guarantees, may be determined
4288      * for a {@code ByteBuffer}, {@code bb} (direct or otherwise), an
4289      * {@code index}, {@code T} and it's corresponding boxed type,
4290      * {@code T_BOX}, as follows:
4291      * <pre>{@code
4292      * int sizeOfT = T_BOX.BYTES;  // size in bytes of T
4293      * ByteBuffer bb = ...
4294      * int misalignedAtIndex = bb.alignmentOffset(index, sizeOfT);
4295      * boolean isMisaligned = misalignedAtIndex != 0;
4296      * }</pre>
4297      * <p>
4298      * If the variable type is {@code float} or {@code double} then atomic
4299      * update access modes compare values using their bitwise representation
4300      * (see {@link Float#floatToRawIntBits} and
4301      * {@link Double#doubleToRawLongBits}, respectively).
4302      * @param viewArrayClass the view array class, with a component type of
4303      * type {@code T}
4304      * @param byteOrder the endianness of the view array elements, as
4305      * stored in the underlying {@code ByteBuffer} (Note this overrides the
4306      * endianness of a {@code ByteBuffer})
4307      * @return a VarHandle giving access to elements of a {@code ByteBuffer}
4308      * viewed as if elements corresponding to the components type of the view
4309      * array class
4310      * @throws NullPointerException if viewArrayClass or byteOrder is null
4311      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if viewArrayClass is not an array type
4312      * @throws UnsupportedOperationException if the component type of
4313      * viewArrayClass is not supported as a variable type
4314      * @since 9
4315      */
4316     public static VarHandle byteBufferViewVarHandle(Class<?> viewArrayClass,
4317                                       ByteOrder byteOrder) throws IllegalArgumentException {
4318         Objects.requireNonNull(byteOrder);
4319         return VarHandles.makeByteBufferViewHandle(viewArrayClass,
4320                                                    byteOrder == ByteOrder.BIG_ENDIAN);
4321     }

4324     /// method handle invocation (reflective style)
4325 
4326     /**
4327      * Produces a method handle which will invoke any method handle of the
4328      * given {@code type}, with a given number of trailing arguments replaced by
4329      * a single trailing {@code Object[]} array.
4330      * The resulting invoker will be a method handle with the following
4331      * arguments:
4332      * <ul>
4333      * <li>a single {@code MethodHandle} target
4334      * <li>zero or more leading values (counted by {@code leadingArgCount})
4335      * <li>an {@code Object[]} array containing trailing arguments
4336      * </ul>
4337      * <p>
4338      * The invoker will invoke its target like a call to {@link MethodHandle#invoke invoke} with
4339      * the indicated {@code type}.
4340      * That is, if the target is exactly of the given {@code type}, it will behave
4341      * like {@code invokeExact}; otherwise it behave as if {@link MethodHandle#asType asType}
4342      * is used to convert the target to the required {@code type}.
4343      * <p>
4344      * The type of the returned invoker will not be the given {@code type}, but rather
4345      * will have all parameters except the first {@code leadingArgCount}
4346      * replaced by a single array of type {@code Object[]}, which will be
4347      * the final parameter.
4348      * <p>
4349      * Before invoking its target, the invoker will spread the final array, apply
4350      * reference casts as necessary, and unbox and widen primitive arguments.
4351      * If, when the invoker is called, the supplied array argument does
4352      * not have the correct number of elements, the invoker will throw
4353      * an {@link IllegalArgumentException} instead of invoking the target.
4354      * <p>
4355      * This method is equivalent to the following code (though it may be more efficient):
4356      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
4357 MethodHandle invoker = MethodHandles.invoker(type);
4358 int spreadArgCount = type.parameterCount() - leadingArgCount;
4359 invoker = invoker.asSpreader(Object[].class, spreadArgCount);
4360 return invoker;
4361      * }</pre></blockquote>
4362      * This method throws no reflective or security exceptions.
4363      * @param type the desired target type
4364      * @param leadingArgCount number of fixed arguments, to be passed unchanged to the target
4365      * @return a method handle suitable for invoking any method handle of the given type
4366      * @throws NullPointerException if {@code type} is null
4367      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if {@code leadingArgCount} is not in
4368      *                  the range from 0 to {@code type.parameterCount()} inclusive,
4369      *                  or if the resulting method handle's type would have
4370      *          <a href="MethodHandle.html#maxarity">too many parameters</a>
4371      */
4372     public static MethodHandle spreadInvoker(MethodType type, int leadingArgCount) {
4373         if (leadingArgCount < 0 || leadingArgCount > type.parameterCount())
4374             throw newIllegalArgumentException("bad argument count", leadingArgCount);
4375         type = type.asSpreaderType(Object[].class, leadingArgCount, type.parameterCount() - leadingArgCount);
4376         return type.invokers().spreadInvoker(leadingArgCount);
4377     }
4378 
4379     /**
4380      * Produces a special <em>invoker method handle</em> which can be used to
4381      * invoke any method handle of the given type, as if by {@link MethodHandle#invokeExact invokeExact}.
4382      * The resulting invoker will have a type which is
4383      * exactly equal to the desired type, except that it will accept
4384      * an additional leading argument of type {@code MethodHandle}.
4385      * <p>
4386      * This method is equivalent to the following code (though it may be more efficient):
4387      * {@code publicLookup().findVirtual(MethodHandle.class, "invokeExact", type)}
4388      *
4389      * <p style="font-size:smaller;">
4390      * <em>Discussion:</em>
4391      * Invoker method handles can be useful when working with variable method handles
4392      * of unknown types.
4393      * For example, to emulate an {@code invokeExact} call to a variable method
4394      * handle {@code M}, extract its type {@code T},
4395      * look up the invoker method {@code X} for {@code T},
4396      * and call the invoker method, as {@code X.invoke(T, A...)}.
4397      * (It would not work to call {@code X.invokeExact}, since the type {@code T}
4398      * is unknown.)
4399      * If spreading, collecting, or other argument transformations are required,
4400      * they can be applied once to the invoker {@code X} and reused on many {@code M}
4401      * method handle values, as long as they are compatible with the type of {@code X}.
4402      * <p style="font-size:smaller;">
4403      * <em>(Note:  The invoker method is not available via the Core Reflection API.
4404      * An attempt to call {@linkplain java.lang.reflect.Method#invoke java.lang.reflect.Method.invoke}
4405      * on the declared {@code invokeExact} or {@code invoke} method will raise an
4406      * {@link java.lang.UnsupportedOperationException UnsupportedOperationException}.)</em>
4407      * <p>
4408      * This method throws no reflective or security exceptions.
4409      * @param type the desired target type
4410      * @return a method handle suitable for invoking any method handle of the given type
4411      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the resulting method handle's type would have
4412      *          <a href="MethodHandle.html#maxarity">too many parameters</a>
4413      */
4414     public static MethodHandle exactInvoker(MethodType type) {
4415         return type.invokers().exactInvoker();
4416     }
4417 
4418     /**
4419      * Produces a special <em>invoker method handle</em> which can be used to
4420      * invoke any method handle compatible with the given type, as if by {@link MethodHandle#invoke invoke}.
4421      * The resulting invoker will have a type which is
4422      * exactly equal to the desired type, except that it will accept
4423      * an additional leading argument of type {@code MethodHandle}.
4424      * <p>
4425      * Before invoking its target, if the target differs from the expected type,
4426      * the invoker will apply reference casts as
4427      * necessary and box, unbox, or widen primitive values, as if by {@link MethodHandle#asType asType}.
4428      * Similarly, the return value will be converted as necessary.
4429      * If the target is a {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector variable arity method handle},
4430      * the required arity conversion will be made, again as if by {@link MethodHandle#asType asType}.
4431      * <p>
4432      * This method is equivalent to the following code (though it may be more efficient):
4433      * {@code publicLookup().findVirtual(MethodHandle.class, "invoke", type)}
4434      * <p style="font-size:smaller;">
4435      * <em>Discussion:</em>
4436      * A {@linkplain MethodType#genericMethodType general method type} is one which
4437      * mentions only {@code Object} arguments and return values.
4438      * An invoker for such a type is capable of calling any method handle
4439      * of the same arity as the general type.
4440      * <p style="font-size:smaller;">
4441      * <em>(Note:  The invoker method is not available via the Core Reflection API.
4442      * An attempt to call {@linkplain java.lang.reflect.Method#invoke java.lang.reflect.Method.invoke}
4443      * on the declared {@code invokeExact} or {@code invoke} method will raise an
4444      * {@link java.lang.UnsupportedOperationException UnsupportedOperationException}.)</em>
4445      * <p>
4446      * This method throws no reflective or security exceptions.
4447      * @param type the desired target type
4448      * @return a method handle suitable for invoking any method handle convertible to the given type
4449      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the resulting method handle's type would have
4450      *          <a href="MethodHandle.html#maxarity">too many parameters</a>
4451      */
4452     public static MethodHandle invoker(MethodType type) {
4453         return type.invokers().genericInvoker();
4454     }
4455 
4456     /**
4457      * Produces a special <em>invoker method handle</em> which can be used to
4458      * invoke a signature-polymorphic access mode method on any VarHandle whose
4459      * associated access mode type is compatible with the given type.
4460      * The resulting invoker will have a type which is exactly equal to the
4461      * desired given type, except that it will accept an additional leading
4462      * argument of type {@code VarHandle}.
4463      *
4464      * @param accessMode the VarHandle access mode
4465      * @param type the desired target type
4466      * @return a method handle suitable for invoking an access mode method of
4467      *         any VarHandle whose access mode type is of the given type.
4468      * @since 9
4469      */
4470     public static MethodHandle varHandleExactInvoker(VarHandle.AccessMode accessMode, MethodType type) {
4471         return type.invokers().varHandleMethodExactInvoker(accessMode);
4472     }
4473 
4474     /**
4475      * Produces a special <em>invoker method handle</em> which can be used to
4476      * invoke a signature-polymorphic access mode method on any VarHandle whose
4477      * associated access mode type is compatible with the given type.
4478      * The resulting invoker will have a type which is exactly equal to the
4479      * desired given type, except that it will accept an additional leading
4480      * argument of type {@code VarHandle}.
4481      * <p>
4482      * Before invoking its target, if the access mode type differs from the
4483      * desired given type, the invoker will apply reference casts as necessary
4484      * and box, unbox, or widen primitive values, as if by
4485      * {@link MethodHandle#asType asType}.  Similarly, the return value will be
4486      * converted as necessary.
4487      * <p>
4488      * This method is equivalent to the following code (though it may be more
4489      * efficient): {@code publicLookup().findVirtual(VarHandle.class, accessMode.name(), type)}
4490      *
4491      * @param accessMode the VarHandle access mode
4492      * @param type the desired target type
4493      * @return a method handle suitable for invoking an access mode method of
4494      *         any VarHandle whose access mode type is convertible to the given
4495      *         type.
4496      * @since 9
4497      */
4498     public static MethodHandle varHandleInvoker(VarHandle.AccessMode accessMode, MethodType type) {
4499         return type.invokers().varHandleMethodInvoker(accessMode);
4500     }
4501 
4502     /*non-public*/
4503     static MethodHandle basicInvoker(MethodType type) {
4504         return type.invokers().basicInvoker();
4505     }
4506 
4507      /// method handle modification (creation from other method handles)
4508 
4509     /**
4510      * Produces a method handle which adapts the type of the
4511      * given method handle to a new type by pairwise argument and return type conversion.
4512      * The original type and new type must have the same number of arguments.
4513      * The resulting method handle is guaranteed to report a type
4514      * which is equal to the desired new type.
4515      * <p>
4516      * If the original type and new type are equal, returns target.
4517      * <p>
4518      * The same conversions are allowed as for {@link MethodHandle#asType MethodHandle.asType},
4519      * and some additional conversions are also applied if those conversions fail.
4520      * Given types <em>T0</em>, <em>T1</em>, one of the following conversions is applied
4521      * if possible, before or instead of any conversions done by {@code asType}:
4522      * <ul>
4523      * <li>If <em>T0</em> and <em>T1</em> are references, and <em>T1</em> is an interface type,
4524      *     then the value of type <em>T0</em> is passed as a <em>T1</em> without a cast.
4525      *     (This treatment of interfaces follows the usage of the bytecode verifier.)
4526      * <li>If <em>T0</em> is boolean and <em>T1</em> is another primitive,
4527      *     the boolean is converted to a byte value, 1 for true, 0 for false.
4528      *     (This treatment follows the usage of the bytecode verifier.)
4529      * <li>If <em>T1</em> is boolean and <em>T0</em> is another primitive,
4530      *     <em>T0</em> is converted to byte via Java casting conversion (JLS 5.5),
4531      *     and the low order bit of the result is tested, as if by {@code (x & 1) != 0}.
4532      * <li>If <em>T0</em> and <em>T1</em> are primitives other than boolean,
4533      *     then a Java casting conversion (JLS 5.5) is applied.
4534      *     (Specifically, <em>T0</em> will convert to <em>T1</em> by
4535      *     widening and/or narrowing.)
4536      * <li>If <em>T0</em> is a reference and <em>T1</em> a primitive, an unboxing
4537      *     conversion will be applied at runtime, possibly followed
4538      *     by a Java casting conversion (JLS 5.5) on the primitive value,
4539      *     possibly followed by a conversion from byte to boolean by testing
4540      *     the low-order bit.
4541      * <li>If <em>T0</em> is a reference and <em>T1</em> a primitive,
4542      *     and if the reference is null at runtime, a zero value is introduced.
4543      * </ul>
4544      * @param target the method handle to invoke after arguments are retyped
4545      * @param newType the expected type of the new method handle
4546      * @return a method handle which delegates to the target after performing
4547      *           any necessary argument conversions, and arranges for any
4548      *           necessary return value conversions
4549      * @throws NullPointerException if either argument is null
4550      * @throws WrongMethodTypeException if the conversion cannot be made
4551      * @see MethodHandle#asType
4552      */
4553     public static MethodHandle explicitCastArguments(MethodHandle target, MethodType newType) {
4554         explicitCastArgumentsChecks(target, newType);
4555         // use the asTypeCache when possible:
4556         MethodType oldType = target.type();
4557         if (oldType == newType)  return target;
4558         if (oldType.explicitCastEquivalentToAsType(newType)) {
4559             return target.asFixedArity().asType(newType);
4560         }
4561         return MethodHandleImpl.makePairwiseConvert(target, newType, false);
4562     }
4563 
4564     private static void explicitCastArgumentsChecks(MethodHandle target, MethodType newType) {
4565         if (target.type().parameterCount() != newType.parameterCount()) {
4566             throw new WrongMethodTypeException("cannot explicitly cast " + target + " to " + newType);
4567         }
4568     }
4569 
4570     /**
4571      * Produces a method handle which adapts the calling sequence of the
4572      * given method handle to a new type, by reordering the arguments.
4573      * The resulting method handle is guaranteed to report a type
4574      * which is equal to the desired new type.
4575      * <p>
4576      * The given array controls the reordering.
4577      * Call {@code #I} the number of incoming parameters (the value
4578      * {@code newType.parameterCount()}, and call {@code #O} the number
4579      * of outgoing parameters (the value {@code target.type().parameterCount()}).
4580      * Then the length of the reordering array must be {@code #O},
4581      * and each element must be a non-negative number less than {@code #I}.
4582      * For every {@code N} less than {@code #O}, the {@code N}-th
4583      * outgoing argument will be taken from the {@code I}-th incoming
4584      * argument, where {@code I} is {@code reorder[N]}.
4585      * <p>
4586      * No argument or return value conversions are applied.
4587      * The type of each incoming argument, as determined by {@code newType},
4588      * must be identical to the type of the corresponding outgoing parameter
4589      * or parameters in the target method handle.
4590      * The return type of {@code newType} must be identical to the return
4591      * type of the original target.
4592      * <p>
4593      * The reordering array need not specify an actual permutation.
4594      * An incoming argument will be duplicated if its index appears
4595      * more than once in the array, and an incoming argument will be dropped
4596      * if its index does not appear in the array.
4597      * As in the case of {@link #dropArguments(MethodHandle,int,List) dropArguments},
4598      * incoming arguments which are not mentioned in the reordering array
4599      * may be of any type, as determined only by {@code newType}.
4600      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
4601 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.*;
4602 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodType.*;
4603 ...
4604 MethodType intfn1 = methodType(int.class, int.class);
4605 MethodType intfn2 = methodType(int.class, int.class, int.class);
4606 MethodHandle sub = ... (int x, int y) -> (x-y) ...;
4607 assert(sub.type().equals(intfn2));
4608 MethodHandle sub1 = permuteArguments(sub, intfn2, 0, 1);
4609 MethodHandle rsub = permuteArguments(sub, intfn2, 1, 0);
4610 assert((int)rsub.invokeExact(1, 100) == 99);
4611 MethodHandle add = ... (int x, int y) -> (x+y) ...;
4612 assert(add.type().equals(intfn2));
4613 MethodHandle twice = permuteArguments(add, intfn1, 0, 0);
4614 assert(twice.type().equals(intfn1));
4615 assert((int)twice.invokeExact(21) == 42);
4616      * }</pre></blockquote>
4617      * <p>
4618      * <em>Note:</em> The resulting adapter is never a {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector
4619      * variable-arity method handle}, even if the original target method handle was.
4620      * @param target the method handle to invoke after arguments are reordered
4621      * @param newType the expected type of the new method handle
4622      * @param reorder an index array which controls the reordering
4623      * @return a method handle which delegates to the target after it
4624      *           drops unused arguments and moves and/or duplicates the other arguments
4625      * @throws NullPointerException if any argument is null
4626      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the index array length is not equal to
4627      *                  the arity of the target, or if any index array element
4628      *                  not a valid index for a parameter of {@code newType},
4629      *                  or if two corresponding parameter types in
4630      *                  {@code target.type()} and {@code newType} are not identical,
4631      */
4632     public static MethodHandle permuteArguments(MethodHandle target, MethodType newType, int... reorder) {
4633         reorder = reorder.clone();  // get a private copy
4634         MethodType oldType = target.type();
4635         permuteArgumentChecks(reorder, newType, oldType);
4636         // first detect dropped arguments and handle them separately
4637         int[] originalReorder = reorder;
4638         BoundMethodHandle result = target.rebind();
4639         LambdaForm form = result.form;
4640         int newArity = newType.parameterCount();
4641         // Normalize the reordering into a real permutation,
4642         // by removing duplicates and adding dropped elements.
4643         // This somewhat improves lambda form caching, as well
4644         // as simplifying the transform by breaking it up into steps.
4645         for (int ddIdx; (ddIdx = findFirstDupOrDrop(reorder, newArity)) != 0; ) {
4646             if (ddIdx > 0) {
4647                 // We found a duplicated entry at reorder[ddIdx].
4648                 // Example:  (x,y,z)->asList(x,y,z)
4649                 // permuted by [1*,0,1] => (a0,a1)=>asList(a1,a0,a1)
4650                 // permuted by [0,1,0*] => (a0,a1)=>asList(a0,a1,a0)
4651                 // The starred element corresponds to the argument
4652                 // deleted by the dupArgumentForm transform.
4653                 int srcPos = ddIdx, dstPos = srcPos, dupVal = reorder[srcPos];
4654                 boolean killFirst = false;
4655                 for (int val; (val = reorder[--dstPos]) != dupVal; ) {
4656                     // Set killFirst if the dup is larger than an intervening position.
4657                     // This will remove at least one inversion from the permutation.
4658                     if (dupVal > val) killFirst = true;
4659                 }
4660                 if (!killFirst) {
4661                     srcPos = dstPos;
4662                     dstPos = ddIdx;
4663                 }
4664                 form = form.editor().dupArgumentForm(1 + srcPos, 1 + dstPos);
4665                 assert (reorder[srcPos] == reorder[dstPos]);
4666                 oldType = oldType.dropParameterTypes(dstPos, dstPos + 1);
4667                 // contract the reordering by removing the element at dstPos
4668                 int tailPos = dstPos + 1;
4669                 System.arraycopy(reorder, tailPos, reorder, dstPos, reorder.length - tailPos);
4670                 reorder = Arrays.copyOf(reorder, reorder.length - 1);
4671             } else {
4672                 int dropVal = ~ddIdx, insPos = 0;
4673                 while (insPos < reorder.length && reorder[insPos] < dropVal) {
4674                     // Find first element of reorder larger than dropVal.
4675                     // This is where we will insert the dropVal.
4676                     insPos += 1;
4677                 }
4678                 Class<?> ptype = newType.parameterType(dropVal);
4679                 form = form.editor().addArgumentForm(1 + insPos, BasicType.basicType(ptype));
4680                 oldType = oldType.insertParameterTypes(insPos, ptype);
4681                 // expand the reordering by inserting an element at insPos
4682                 int tailPos = insPos + 1;
4683                 reorder = Arrays.copyOf(reorder, reorder.length + 1);
4684                 System.arraycopy(reorder, insPos, reorder, tailPos, reorder.length - tailPos);
4685                 reorder[insPos] = dropVal;
4686             }
4687             assert (permuteArgumentChecks(reorder, newType, oldType));
4688         }
4689         assert (reorder.length == newArity);  // a perfect permutation
4690         // Note:  This may cache too many distinct LFs. Consider backing off to varargs code.
4691         form = form.editor().permuteArgumentsForm(1, reorder);
4692         if (newType == result.type() && form == result.internalForm())
4693             return result;
4694         return result.copyWith(newType, form);
4695     }
4696 
4697     /**
4698      * Return an indication of any duplicate or omission in reorder.
4699      * If the reorder contains a duplicate entry, return the index of the second occurrence.
