4700      * Otherwise, return ~(n), for the first n in [0..newArity-1] that is not present in reorder.
4701      * Otherwise, return zero.
4702      * If an element not in [0..newArity-1] is encountered, return reorder.length.
4703      */
4704     private static int findFirstDupOrDrop(int[] reorder, int newArity) {
4705         final int BIT_LIMIT = 63;  // max number of bits in bit mask
4706         if (newArity < BIT_LIMIT) {
4707             long mask = 0;
4708             for (int i = 0; i < reorder.length; i++) {
4709                 int arg = reorder[i];
4710                 if (arg >= newArity) {
4711                     return reorder.length;
4712                 }
4713                 long bit = 1L << arg;
4714                 if ((mask & bit) != 0) {
4715                     return i;  // >0 indicates a dup
4716                 }
4717                 mask |= bit;
4718             }
4719             if (mask == (1L << newArity) - 1) {
4720                 assert(Long.numberOfTrailingZeros(Long.lowestOneBit(~mask)) == newArity);
4721                 return 0;
4722             }
4723             // find first zero
4724             long zeroBit = Long.lowestOneBit(~mask);
4725             int zeroPos = Long.numberOfTrailingZeros(zeroBit);
4726             assert(zeroPos <= newArity);
4727             if (zeroPos == newArity) {
4728                 return 0;
4729             }
4730             return ~zeroPos;
4731         } else {
4732             // same algorithm, different bit set
4733             BitSet mask = new BitSet(newArity);
4734             for (int i = 0; i < reorder.length; i++) {
4735                 int arg = reorder[i];
4736                 if (arg >= newArity) {
4737                     return reorder.length;
4738                 }
4739                 if (mask.get(arg)) {
4740                     return i;  // >0 indicates a dup
4741                 }
4742                 mask.set(arg);
4743             }
4744             int zeroPos = mask.nextClearBit(0);
4745             assert(zeroPos <= newArity);
4746             if (zeroPos == newArity) {
4747                 return 0;
4748             }
4749             return ~zeroPos;
4750         }
4751     }
4752 
4753     static boolean permuteArgumentChecks(int[] reorder, MethodType newType, MethodType oldType) {
4754         if (newType.returnType() != oldType.returnType())
4755             throw newIllegalArgumentException("return types do not match",
4756                     oldType, newType);
4757         if (reorder.length == oldType.parameterCount()) {
4758             int limit = newType.parameterCount();
4759             boolean bad = false;
4760             for (int j = 0; j < reorder.length; j++) {
4761                 int i = reorder[j];
4762                 if (i < 0 || i >= limit) {
4763                     bad = true; break;
4764                 }
4765                 Class<?> src = newType.parameterType(i);
4766                 Class<?> dst = oldType.parameterType(j);
4767                 if (src != dst)
4768                     throw newIllegalArgumentException("parameter types do not match after reorder",
4769                             oldType, newType);
4770             }
4771             if (!bad)  return true;
4772         }
4773         throw newIllegalArgumentException("bad reorder array: "+Arrays.toString(reorder));
4774     }
4775 
4776     /**
4777      * Produces a method handle of the requested return type which returns the given
4778      * constant value every time it is invoked.
4779      * <p>
4780      * Before the method handle is returned, the passed-in value is converted to the requested type.
4781      * If the requested type is primitive, widening primitive conversions are attempted,
4782      * else reference conversions are attempted.
4783      * <p>The returned method handle is equivalent to {@code identity(type).bindTo(value)}.
4784      * @param type the return type of the desired method handle
4785      * @param value the value to return
4786      * @return a method handle of the given return type and no arguments, which always returns the given value
4787      * @throws NullPointerException if the {@code type} argument is null
4788      * @throws ClassCastException if the value cannot be converted to the required return type
4789      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the given type is {@code void.class}
4790      */
4791     public static MethodHandle constant(Class<?> type, Object value) {
4792         if (type.isPrimitive()) {
4793             if (type == void.class)
4794                 throw newIllegalArgumentException("void type");
4795             Wrapper w = Wrapper.forPrimitiveType(type);
4796             value = w.convert(value, type);
4797             if (w.zero().equals(value))
4798                 return zero(w, type);
4799             return insertArguments(identity(type), 0, value);
4800         } else {
4801             if (value == null)
4802                 return zero(Wrapper.OBJECT, type);
4803             return identity(type).bindTo(value);
4804         }
4805     }
4806 
4807     /**
4808      * Produces a method handle which returns its sole argument when invoked.
4809      * @param type the type of the sole parameter and return value of the desired method handle
4810      * @return a unary method handle which accepts and returns the given type
4811      * @throws NullPointerException if the argument is null
4812      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the given type is {@code void.class}
4813      */
4814     public static MethodHandle identity(Class<?> type) {
4815         Wrapper btw = (type.isPrimitive() ? Wrapper.forPrimitiveType(type) : Wrapper.OBJECT);
4816         int pos = btw.ordinal();
4817         MethodHandle ident = IDENTITY_MHS[pos];
4818         if (ident == null) {
4819             ident = setCachedMethodHandle(IDENTITY_MHS, pos, makeIdentity(btw.primitiveType()));
4820         }
4821         if (ident.type().returnType() == type)
4822             return ident;
4823         // something like identity(Foo.class); do not bother to intern these
4824         assert (btw == Wrapper.OBJECT);
4825         return makeIdentity(type);
4826     }
4827 
4828     /**
4829      * Produces a constant method handle of the requested return type which
4830      * returns the default value for that type every time it is invoked.
4831      * The resulting constant method handle will have no side effects.
4832      * <p>The returned method handle is equivalent to {@code empty(methodType(type))}.
4833      * It is also equivalent to {@code explicitCastArguments(constant(Object.class, null), methodType(type))},
4834      * since {@code explicitCastArguments} converts {@code null} to default values.
4835      * @param type the expected return type of the desired method handle
4836      * @return a constant method handle that takes no arguments
4837      *         and returns the default value of the given type (or void, if the type is void)
4838      * @throws NullPointerException if the argument is null
4839      * @see MethodHandles#constant
4840      * @see MethodHandles#empty
4841      * @see MethodHandles#explicitCastArguments
4842      * @since 9
4843      */
4844     public static MethodHandle zero(Class<?> type) {
4845         Objects.requireNonNull(type);
4846         return type.isPrimitive() ?  zero(Wrapper.forPrimitiveType(type), type) : zero(Wrapper.OBJECT, type);
4847     }
4848 
4849     private static MethodHandle identityOrVoid(Class<?> type) {
4850         return type == void.class ? zero(type) : identity(type);
4851     }
4852 
4853     /**
4854      * Produces a method handle of the requested type which ignores any arguments, does nothing,
4855      * and returns a suitable default depending on the return type.
4856      * That is, it returns a zero primitive value, a {@code null}, or {@code void}.
4857      * <p>The returned method handle is equivalent to
4858      * {@code dropArguments(zero(type.returnType()), 0, type.parameterList())}.
4859      *
4860      * @apiNote Given a predicate and target, a useful "if-then" construct can be produced as
4861      * {@code guardWithTest(pred, target, empty(target.type())}.
4862      * @param type the type of the desired method handle
4863      * @return a constant method handle of the given type, which returns a default value of the given return type
4864      * @throws NullPointerException if the argument is null
4865      * @see MethodHandles#zero
4866      * @see MethodHandles#constant
4867      * @since 9
4868      */
4869     public static  MethodHandle empty(MethodType type) {
4870         Objects.requireNonNull(type);
4871         return dropArguments(zero(type.returnType()), 0, type.parameterList());
4872     }
4873 
4874     private static final MethodHandle[] IDENTITY_MHS = new MethodHandle[Wrapper.COUNT];
4875     private static MethodHandle makeIdentity(Class<?> ptype) {
4876         MethodType mtype = methodType(ptype, ptype);
4877         LambdaForm lform = LambdaForm.identityForm(BasicType.basicType(ptype));
4878         return MethodHandleImpl.makeIntrinsic(mtype, lform, Intrinsic.IDENTITY);
4879     }
4880 
4881     private static MethodHandle zero(Wrapper btw, Class<?> rtype) {
4882         int pos = btw.ordinal();
4883         MethodHandle zero = ZERO_MHS[pos];
4884         if (zero == null) {
4885             zero = setCachedMethodHandle(ZERO_MHS, pos, makeZero(btw.primitiveType()));
4886         }
4887         if (zero.type().returnType() == rtype)
4888             return zero;
4889         assert(btw == Wrapper.OBJECT);
4890         return makeZero(rtype);
4891     }
4892     private static final MethodHandle[] ZERO_MHS = new MethodHandle[Wrapper.COUNT];
4893     private static MethodHandle makeZero(Class<?> rtype) {
4894         MethodType mtype = methodType(rtype);
4895         LambdaForm lform = LambdaForm.zeroForm(BasicType.basicType(rtype));
4896         return MethodHandleImpl.makeIntrinsic(mtype, lform, Intrinsic.ZERO);
4897     }
4898 
4899     private static synchronized MethodHandle setCachedMethodHandle(MethodHandle[] cache, int pos, MethodHandle value) {
4900         // Simulate a CAS, to avoid racy duplication of results.
4901         MethodHandle prev = cache[pos];
4902         if (prev != null) return prev;
4903         return cache[pos] = value;
4904     }
4905 
4906     /**
4907      * Provides a target method handle with one or more <em>bound arguments</em>
4908      * in advance of the method handle's invocation.
4909      * The formal parameters to the target corresponding to the bound
4910      * arguments are called <em>bound parameters</em>.
4911      * Returns a new method handle which saves away the bound arguments.
4912      * When it is invoked, it receives arguments for any non-bound parameters,
4913      * binds the saved arguments to their corresponding parameters,
4914      * and calls the original target.
4915      * <p>
4916      * The type of the new method handle will drop the types for the bound
4917      * parameters from the original target type, since the new method handle
4918      * will no longer require those arguments to be supplied by its callers.
4919      * <p>
4920      * Each given argument object must match the corresponding bound parameter type.
4921      * If a bound parameter type is a primitive, the argument object
4922      * must be a wrapper, and will be unboxed to produce the primitive value.
4923      * <p>
4924      * The {@code pos} argument selects which parameters are to be bound.
4925      * It may range between zero and <i>N-L</i> (inclusively),
4926      * where <i>N</i> is the arity of the target method handle
4927      * and <i>L</i> is the length of the values array.
4928      * <p>
4929      * <em>Note:</em> The resulting adapter is never a {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector
4930      * variable-arity method handle}, even if the original target method handle was.
4931      * @param target the method handle to invoke after the argument is inserted
4932      * @param pos where to insert the argument (zero for the first)
4933      * @param values the series of arguments to insert
4934      * @return a method handle which inserts an additional argument,
4935      *         before calling the original method handle
4936      * @throws NullPointerException if the target or the {@code values} array is null
4937      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if (@code pos) is less than {@code 0} or greater than
4938      *         {@code N - L} where {@code N} is the arity of the target method handle and {@code L}
4939      *         is the length of the values array.
4940      * @throws ClassCastException if an argument does not match the corresponding bound parameter
4941      *         type.
4942      * @see MethodHandle#bindTo
4943      */
4944     public static MethodHandle insertArguments(MethodHandle target, int pos, Object... values) {
4945         int insCount = values.length;
4946         Class<?>[] ptypes = insertArgumentsChecks(target, insCount, pos);
4947         if (insCount == 0)  return target;
4948         BoundMethodHandle result = target.rebind();
4949         for (int i = 0; i < insCount; i++) {
4950             Object value = values[i];
4951             Class<?> ptype = ptypes[pos+i];
4952             if (ptype.isPrimitive()) {
4953                 result = insertArgumentPrimitive(result, pos, ptype, value);
4954             } else {
4955                 value = ptype.cast(value);  // throw CCE if needed
4956                 result = result.bindArgumentL(pos, value);
4957             }
4958         }
4959         return result;
4960     }
4961 
4962     private static BoundMethodHandle insertArgumentPrimitive(BoundMethodHandle result, int pos,
4963                                                              Class<?> ptype, Object value) {
4964         Wrapper w = Wrapper.forPrimitiveType(ptype);
4965         // perform unboxing and/or primitive conversion
4966         value = w.convert(value, ptype);
4967         switch (w) {
4968         case INT:     return result.bindArgumentI(pos, (int)value);
4969         case LONG:    return result.bindArgumentJ(pos, (long)value);
4970         case FLOAT:   return result.bindArgumentF(pos, (float)value);
4971         case DOUBLE:  return result.bindArgumentD(pos, (double)value);
4972         default:      return result.bindArgumentI(pos, ValueConversions.widenSubword(value));
4973         }
4974     }
4975 
4976     private static Class<?>[] insertArgumentsChecks(MethodHandle target, int insCount, int pos) throws RuntimeException {
4977         MethodType oldType = target.type();
4978         int outargs = oldType.parameterCount();
4979         int inargs  = outargs - insCount;
4980         if (inargs < 0)
4981             throw newIllegalArgumentException("too many values to insert");
4982         if (pos < 0 || pos > inargs)
4983             throw newIllegalArgumentException("no argument type to append");
4984         return oldType.ptypes();
4985     }
4986 
4987     /**
4988      * Produces a method handle which will discard some dummy arguments
4989      * before calling some other specified <i>target</i> method handle.
4990      * The type of the new method handle will be the same as the target's type,
4991      * except it will also include the dummy argument types,
4992      * at some given position.
4993      * <p>
4994      * The {@code pos} argument may range between zero and <i>N</i>,
4995      * where <i>N</i> is the arity of the target.
4996      * If {@code pos} is zero, the dummy arguments will precede
4997      * the target's real arguments; if {@code pos} is <i>N</i>
4998      * they will come after.
4999      * <p>
5000      * <b>Example:</b>
5001      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5002 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.*;
5003 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodType.*;
5004 ...
5005 MethodHandle cat = lookup().findVirtual(String.class,
5006   "concat", methodType(String.class, String.class));
5007 assertEquals("xy", (String) cat.invokeExact("x", "y"));
5008 MethodType bigType = cat.type().insertParameterTypes(0, int.class, String.class);
5009 MethodHandle d0 = dropArguments(cat, 0, bigType.parameterList().subList(0,2));
5010 assertEquals(bigType, d0.type());
5011 assertEquals("yz", (String) d0.invokeExact(123, "x", "y", "z"));
5012      * }</pre></blockquote>
5013      * <p>
5014      * This method is also equivalent to the following code:
5015      * <blockquote><pre>
5016      * {@link #dropArguments(MethodHandle,int,Class...) dropArguments}{@code (target, pos, valueTypes.toArray(new Class[0]))}
5017      * </pre></blockquote>
5018      * @param target the method handle to invoke after the arguments are dropped
5019      * @param pos position of first argument to drop (zero for the leftmost)
5020      * @param valueTypes the type(s) of the argument(s) to drop
5021      * @return a method handle which drops arguments of the given types,
5022      *         before calling the original method handle
5023      * @throws NullPointerException if the target is null,
5024      *                              or if the {@code valueTypes} list or any of its elements is null
5025      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if any element of {@code valueTypes} is {@code void.class},
5026      *                  or if {@code pos} is negative or greater than the arity of the target,
5027      *                  or if the new method handle's type would have too many parameters
5028      */
5029     public static MethodHandle dropArguments(MethodHandle target, int pos, List<Class<?>> valueTypes) {
5030         return dropArguments0(target, pos, copyTypes(valueTypes.toArray()));
5031     }
5032 
5033     private static List<Class<?>> copyTypes(Object[] array) {
5034         return Arrays.asList(Arrays.copyOf(array, array.length, Class[].class));
5035     }
5036 
5037     private static MethodHandle dropArguments0(MethodHandle target, int pos, List<Class<?>> valueTypes) {
5038         MethodType oldType = target.type();  // get NPE
5039         int dropped = dropArgumentChecks(oldType, pos, valueTypes);
5040         MethodType newType = oldType.insertParameterTypes(pos, valueTypes);
5041         if (dropped == 0)  return target;
5042         BoundMethodHandle result = target.rebind();
5043         LambdaForm lform = result.form;
5044         int insertFormArg = 1 + pos;
5045         for (Class<?> ptype : valueTypes) {
5046             lform = lform.editor().addArgumentForm(insertFormArg++, BasicType.basicType(ptype));
5047         }
5048         result = result.copyWith(newType, lform);
5049         return result;
5050     }
5051 
5052     private static int dropArgumentChecks(MethodType oldType, int pos, List<Class<?>> valueTypes) {
5053         int dropped = valueTypes.size();
5054         MethodType.checkSlotCount(dropped);
5055         int outargs = oldType.parameterCount();
5056         int inargs  = outargs + dropped;
5057         if (pos < 0 || pos > outargs)
5058             throw newIllegalArgumentException("no argument type to remove"
5059                     + Arrays.asList(oldType, pos, valueTypes, inargs, outargs)
5060                     );
5061         return dropped;
5062     }
5063 
5064     /**
5065      * Produces a method handle which will discard some dummy arguments
5066      * before calling some other specified <i>target</i> method handle.
5067      * The type of the new method handle will be the same as the target's type,
5068      * except it will also include the dummy argument types,
5069      * at some given position.
5070      * <p>
5071      * The {@code pos} argument may range between zero and <i>N</i>,
5072      * where <i>N</i> is the arity of the target.
5073      * If {@code pos} is zero, the dummy arguments will precede
5074      * the target's real arguments; if {@code pos} is <i>N</i>
5075      * they will come after.
5076      * @apiNote
5077      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5078 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.*;
5079 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodType.*;
5080 ...
5081 MethodHandle cat = lookup().findVirtual(String.class,
5082   "concat", methodType(String.class, String.class));
5083 assertEquals("xy", (String) cat.invokeExact("x", "y"));
5084 MethodHandle d0 = dropArguments(cat, 0, String.class);
5085 assertEquals("yz", (String) d0.invokeExact("x", "y", "z"));
5086 MethodHandle d1 = dropArguments(cat, 1, String.class);
5087 assertEquals("xz", (String) d1.invokeExact("x", "y", "z"));
5088 MethodHandle d2 = dropArguments(cat, 2, String.class);
5089 assertEquals("xy", (String) d2.invokeExact("x", "y", "z"));
5090 MethodHandle d12 = dropArguments(cat, 1, int.class, boolean.class);
5091 assertEquals("xz", (String) d12.invokeExact("x", 12, true, "z"));
5092      * }</pre></blockquote>
5093      * <p>
5094      * This method is also equivalent to the following code:
5095      * <blockquote><pre>
5096      * {@link #dropArguments(MethodHandle,int,List) dropArguments}{@code (target, pos, Arrays.asList(valueTypes))}
5097      * </pre></blockquote>
5098      * @param target the method handle to invoke after the arguments are dropped
5099      * @param pos position of first argument to drop (zero for the leftmost)
5100      * @param valueTypes the type(s) of the argument(s) to drop
5101      * @return a method handle which drops arguments of the given types,
5102      *         before calling the original method handle
5103      * @throws NullPointerException if the target is null,
5104      *                              or if the {@code valueTypes} array or any of its elements is null
5105      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if any element of {@code valueTypes} is {@code void.class},
5106      *                  or if {@code pos} is negative or greater than the arity of the target,
5107      *                  or if the new method handle's type would have
5108      *                  <a href="MethodHandle.html#maxarity">too many parameters</a>
5109      */
5110     public static MethodHandle dropArguments(MethodHandle target, int pos, Class<?>... valueTypes) {
5111         return dropArguments0(target, pos, copyTypes(valueTypes));
5112     }
5113 
5114     // private version which allows caller some freedom with error handling
5115     private static MethodHandle dropArgumentsToMatch(MethodHandle target, int skip, List<Class<?>> newTypes, int pos,
5116                                       boolean nullOnFailure) {
5117         newTypes = copyTypes(newTypes.toArray());
5118         List<Class<?>> oldTypes = target.type().parameterList();
5119         int match = oldTypes.size();
5120         if (skip != 0) {
5121             if (skip < 0 || skip > match) {
5122                 throw newIllegalArgumentException("illegal skip", skip, target);
5123             }
5124             oldTypes = oldTypes.subList(skip, match);
5125             match -= skip;
5126         }
5127         List<Class<?>> addTypes = newTypes;
5128         int add = addTypes.size();
5129         if (pos != 0) {
5130             if (pos < 0 || pos > add) {
5131                 throw newIllegalArgumentException("illegal pos", pos, newTypes);
5132             }
5133             addTypes = addTypes.subList(pos, add);
5134             add -= pos;
5135             assert(addTypes.size() == add);
5136         }
5137         // Do not add types which already match the existing arguments.
5138         if (match > add || !oldTypes.equals(addTypes.subList(0, match))) {
5139             if (nullOnFailure) {
5140                 return null;
5141             }
5142             throw newIllegalArgumentException("argument lists do not match", oldTypes, newTypes);
5143         }
5144         addTypes = addTypes.subList(match, add);
5145         add -= match;
5146         assert(addTypes.size() == add);
5147         // newTypes:     (   P*[pos], M*[match], A*[add] )
5148         // target: ( S*[skip],        M*[match]  )
5149         MethodHandle adapter = target;
5150         if (add > 0) {
5151             adapter = dropArguments0(adapter, skip+ match, addTypes);
5152         }
5153         // adapter: (S*[skip],        M*[match], A*[add] )
5154         if (pos > 0) {
5155             adapter = dropArguments0(adapter, skip, newTypes.subList(0, pos));
5156         }
5157         // adapter: (S*[skip], P*[pos], M*[match], A*[add] )
5158         return adapter;
5159     }
5160 
5161     /**
5162      * Adapts a target method handle to match the given parameter type list. If necessary, adds dummy arguments. Some
5163      * leading parameters can be skipped before matching begins. The remaining types in the {@code target}'s parameter
5164      * type list must be a sub-list of the {@code newTypes} type list at the starting position {@code pos}. The
5165      * resulting handle will have the target handle's parameter type list, with any non-matching parameter types (before
5166      * or after the matching sub-list) inserted in corresponding positions of the target's original parameters, as if by
5167      * {@link #dropArguments(MethodHandle, int, Class[])}.
5168      * <p>
5169      * The resulting handle will have the same return type as the target handle.
5170      * <p>
5171      * In more formal terms, assume these two type lists:<ul>
5172      * <li>The target handle has the parameter type list {@code S..., M...}, with as many types in {@code S} as
5173      * indicated by {@code skip}. The {@code M} types are those that are supposed to match part of the given type list,
5174      * {@code newTypes}.
5175      * <li>The {@code newTypes} list contains types {@code P..., M..., A...}, with as many types in {@code P} as
5176      * indicated by {@code pos}. The {@code M} types are precisely those that the {@code M} types in the target handle's
5177      * parameter type list are supposed to match. The types in {@code A} are additional types found after the matching
5178      * sub-list.
5179      * </ul>
5180      * Given these assumptions, the result of an invocation of {@code dropArgumentsToMatch} will have the parameter type
5181      * list {@code S..., P..., M..., A...}, with the {@code P} and {@code A} types inserted as if by
5182      * {@link #dropArguments(MethodHandle, int, Class[])}.
5183      *
5184      * @apiNote
5185      * Two method handles whose argument lists are "effectively identical" (i.e., identical in a common prefix) may be
5186      * mutually converted to a common type by two calls to {@code dropArgumentsToMatch}, as follows:
5187      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5188 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.*;
5189 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodType.*;
5190 ...
5191 ...
5192 MethodHandle h0 = constant(boolean.class, true);
5193 MethodHandle h1 = lookup().findVirtual(String.class, "concat", methodType(String.class, String.class));
5194 MethodType bigType = h1.type().insertParameterTypes(1, String.class, int.class);
5195 MethodHandle h2 = dropArguments(h1, 0, bigType.parameterList());
5196 if (h1.type().parameterCount() < h2.type().parameterCount())
5197     h1 = dropArgumentsToMatch(h1, 0, h2.type().parameterList(), 0);  // lengthen h1
5198 else
5199     h2 = dropArgumentsToMatch(h2, 0, h1.type().parameterList(), 0);    // lengthen h2
5200 MethodHandle h3 = guardWithTest(h0, h1, h2);
5201 assertEquals("xy", h3.invoke("x", "y", 1, "a", "b", "c"));
5202      * }</pre></blockquote>
5203      * @param target the method handle to adapt
5204      * @param skip number of targets parameters to disregard (they will be unchanged)
5205      * @param newTypes the list of types to match {@code target}'s parameter type list to
5206      * @param pos place in {@code newTypes} where the non-skipped target parameters must occur
5207      * @return a possibly adapted method handle
5208      * @throws NullPointerException if either argument is null
5209      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if any element of {@code newTypes} is {@code void.class},
5210      *         or if {@code skip} is negative or greater than the arity of the target,
5211      *         or if {@code pos} is negative or greater than the newTypes list size,
5212      *         or if {@code newTypes} does not contain the {@code target}'s non-skipped parameter types at position
5213      *         {@code pos}.
5214      * @since 9
5215      */
5216     public static MethodHandle dropArgumentsToMatch(MethodHandle target, int skip, List<Class<?>> newTypes, int pos) {
5217         Objects.requireNonNull(target);
5218         Objects.requireNonNull(newTypes);
5219         return dropArgumentsToMatch(target, skip, newTypes, pos, false);
5220     }
5221 
5222     /**
5223      * Adapts a target method handle by pre-processing
5224      * one or more of its arguments, each with its own unary filter function,
5225      * and then calling the target with each pre-processed argument
5226      * replaced by the result of its corresponding filter function.
5227      * <p>
5228      * The pre-processing is performed by one or more method handles,
5229      * specified in the elements of the {@code filters} array.
5230      * The first element of the filter array corresponds to the {@code pos}
5231      * argument of the target, and so on in sequence.
5232      * The filter functions are invoked in left to right order.
5233      * <p>
5234      * Null arguments in the array are treated as identity functions,
5235      * and the corresponding arguments left unchanged.
5236      * (If there are no non-null elements in the array, the original target is returned.)
5237      * Each filter is applied to the corresponding argument of the adapter.
5238      * <p>
5239      * If a filter {@code F} applies to the {@code N}th argument of
5240      * the target, then {@code F} must be a method handle which
5241      * takes exactly one argument.  The type of {@code F}'s sole argument
5242      * replaces the corresponding argument type of the target
5243      * in the resulting adapted method handle.
5244      * The return type of {@code F} must be identical to the corresponding
5245      * parameter type of the target.
5246      * <p>
5247      * It is an error if there are elements of {@code filters}
5248      * (null or not)
5249      * which do not correspond to argument positions in the target.
5250      * <p><b>Example:</b>
5251      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5252 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.*;
5253 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodType.*;
5254 ...
5255 MethodHandle cat = lookup().findVirtual(String.class,
5256   "concat", methodType(String.class, String.class));
5257 MethodHandle upcase = lookup().findVirtual(String.class,
5258   "toUpperCase", methodType(String.class));
5259 assertEquals("xy", (String) cat.invokeExact("x", "y"));
5260 MethodHandle f0 = filterArguments(cat, 0, upcase);
5261 assertEquals("Xy", (String) f0.invokeExact("x", "y")); // Xy
5262 MethodHandle f1 = filterArguments(cat, 1, upcase);
5263 assertEquals("xY", (String) f1.invokeExact("x", "y")); // xY
5264 MethodHandle f2 = filterArguments(cat, 0, upcase, upcase);
5265 assertEquals("XY", (String) f2.invokeExact("x", "y")); // XY
5266      * }</pre></blockquote>
5267      * <p>Here is pseudocode for the resulting adapter. In the code, {@code T}
5268      * denotes the return type of both the {@code target} and resulting adapter.
5269      * {@code P}/{@code p} and {@code B}/{@code b} represent the types and values
5270      * of the parameters and arguments that precede and follow the filter position
5271      * {@code pos}, respectively. {@code A[i]}/{@code a[i]} stand for the types and
5272      * values of the filtered parameters and arguments; they also represent the
5273      * return types of the {@code filter[i]} handles. The latter accept arguments
5274      * {@code v[i]} of type {@code V[i]}, which also appear in the signature of
5275      * the resulting adapter.
5276      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5277      * T target(P... p, A[i]... a[i], B... b);
5278      * A[i] filter[i](V[i]);
5279      * T adapter(P... p, V[i]... v[i], B... b) {
5280      *   return target(p..., filter[i](v[i])..., b...);
5281      * }
5282      * }</pre></blockquote>
5283      * <p>
5284      * <em>Note:</em> The resulting adapter is never a {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector
5285      * variable-arity method handle}, even if the original target method handle was.
5286      *
5287      * @param target the method handle to invoke after arguments are filtered
5288      * @param pos the position of the first argument to filter
5289      * @param filters method handles to call initially on filtered arguments
5290      * @return method handle which incorporates the specified argument filtering logic
5291      * @throws NullPointerException if the target is null
5292      *                              or if the {@code filters} array is null
5293      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if a non-null element of {@code filters}
5294      *          does not match a corresponding argument type of target as described above,
5295      *          or if the {@code pos+filters.length} is greater than {@code target.type().parameterCount()},
5296      *          or if the resulting method handle's type would have
5297      *          <a href="MethodHandle.html#maxarity">too many parameters</a>
5298      */
5299     public static MethodHandle filterArguments(MethodHandle target, int pos, MethodHandle... filters) {
5300         // In method types arguments start at index 0, while the LF
5301         // editor have the MH receiver at position 0 - adjust appropriately.
5302         final int MH_RECEIVER_OFFSET = 1;
5303         filterArgumentsCheckArity(target, pos, filters);
5304         MethodHandle adapter = target;
5305 
5306         // keep track of currently matched filters, as to optimize repeated filters
5307         int index = 0;
5308         int[] positions = new int[filters.length];
5309         MethodHandle filter = null;
5310 
5311         // process filters in reverse order so that the invocation of
5312         // the resulting adapter will invoke the filters in left-to-right order
5313         for (int i = filters.length - 1; i >= 0; --i) {
5314             MethodHandle newFilter = filters[i];
5315             if (newFilter == null) continue;  // ignore null elements of filters
5316 
5317             // flush changes on update
5318             if (filter != newFilter) {
5319                 if (filter != null) {
5320                     if (index > 1) {
5321                         adapter = filterRepeatedArgument(adapter, filter, Arrays.copyOf(positions, index));
5322                     } else {
5323                         adapter = filterArgument(adapter, positions[0] - 1, filter);
5324                     }
5325                 }
5326                 filter = newFilter;
5327                 index = 0;
5328             }
5329 
5330             filterArgumentChecks(target, pos + i, newFilter);
5331             positions[index++] = pos + i + MH_RECEIVER_OFFSET;
5332         }
5333         if (index > 1) {
5334             adapter = filterRepeatedArgument(adapter, filter, Arrays.copyOf(positions, index));
5335         } else if (index == 1) {
5336             adapter = filterArgument(adapter, positions[0] - 1, filter);
5337         }
5338         return adapter;
5339     }
5340 
5341     private static MethodHandle filterRepeatedArgument(MethodHandle adapter, MethodHandle filter, int[] positions) {
5342         MethodType targetType = adapter.type();
5343         MethodType filterType = filter.type();
5344         BoundMethodHandle result = adapter.rebind();
5345         Class<?> newParamType = filterType.parameterType(0);
5346 
5347         Class<?>[] ptypes = targetType.ptypes().clone();
5348         for (int pos : positions) {
5349             ptypes[pos - 1] = newParamType;
5350         }
5351         MethodType newType = MethodType.makeImpl(targetType.rtype(), ptypes, true);
5352 
5353         LambdaForm lform = result.editor().filterRepeatedArgumentForm(BasicType.basicType(newParamType), positions);
5354         return result.copyWithExtendL(newType, lform, filter);
5355     }
5356 
5357     /*non-public*/
5358     static MethodHandle filterArgument(MethodHandle target, int pos, MethodHandle filter) {
5359         filterArgumentChecks(target, pos, filter);
5360         MethodType targetType = target.type();
5361         MethodType filterType = filter.type();
5362         BoundMethodHandle result = target.rebind();
5363         Class<?> newParamType = filterType.parameterType(0);
5364         LambdaForm lform = result.editor().filterArgumentForm(1 + pos, BasicType.basicType(newParamType));
5365         MethodType newType = targetType.changeParameterType(pos, newParamType);
5366         result = result.copyWithExtendL(newType, lform, filter);
5367         return result;
5368     }
5369 
5370     private static void filterArgumentsCheckArity(MethodHandle target, int pos, MethodHandle[] filters) {
5371         MethodType targetType = target.type();
5372         int maxPos = targetType.parameterCount();
5373         if (pos + filters.length > maxPos)
5374             throw newIllegalArgumentException("too many filters");
5375     }
5376 
5377     private static void filterArgumentChecks(MethodHandle target, int pos, MethodHandle filter) throws RuntimeException {
5378         MethodType targetType = target.type();
5379         MethodType filterType = filter.type();
5380         if (filterType.parameterCount() != 1
5381             || filterType.returnType() != targetType.parameterType(pos))
5382             throw newIllegalArgumentException("target and filter types do not match", targetType, filterType);
5383     }
5384 
5385     /**
5386      * Adapts a target method handle by pre-processing
5387      * a sub-sequence of its arguments with a filter (another method handle).
5388      * The pre-processed arguments are replaced by the result (if any) of the
5389      * filter function.
5390      * The target is then called on the modified (usually shortened) argument list.
5391      * <p>
5392      * If the filter returns a value, the target must accept that value as
5393      * its argument in position {@code pos}, preceded and/or followed by
5394      * any arguments not passed to the filter.
5395      * If the filter returns void, the target must accept all arguments
5396      * not passed to the filter.
5397      * No arguments are reordered, and a result returned from the filter
5398      * replaces (in order) the whole subsequence of arguments originally
5399      * passed to the adapter.
5400      * <p>
5401      * The argument types (if any) of the filter
5402      * replace zero or one argument types of the target, at position {@code pos},
5403      * in the resulting adapted method handle.
5404      * The return type of the filter (if any) must be identical to the
5405      * argument type of the target at position {@code pos}, and that target argument
5406      * is supplied by the return value of the filter.
5407      * <p>
5408      * In all cases, {@code pos} must be greater than or equal to zero, and
5409      * {@code pos} must also be less than or equal to the target's arity.
5410      * <p><b>Example:</b>
5411      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5412 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.*;
5413 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodType.*;
5414 ...
5415 MethodHandle deepToString = publicLookup()
5416   .findStatic(Arrays.class, "deepToString", methodType(String.class, Object[].class));
5417 
5418 MethodHandle ts1 = deepToString.asCollector(String[].class, 1);
5419 assertEquals("[strange]", (String) ts1.invokeExact("strange"));
5420 
5421 MethodHandle ts2 = deepToString.asCollector(String[].class, 2);
5422 assertEquals("[up, down]", (String) ts2.invokeExact("up", "down"));
5423 
5424 MethodHandle ts3 = deepToString.asCollector(String[].class, 3);
5425 MethodHandle ts3_ts2 = collectArguments(ts3, 1, ts2);
5426 assertEquals("[top, [up, down], strange]",
5427              (String) ts3_ts2.invokeExact("top", "up", "down", "strange"));
5428 
5429 MethodHandle ts3_ts2_ts1 = collectArguments(ts3_ts2, 3, ts1);
5430 assertEquals("[top, [up, down], [strange]]",
5431              (String) ts3_ts2_ts1.invokeExact("top", "up", "down", "strange"));
5432 
5433 MethodHandle ts3_ts2_ts3 = collectArguments(ts3_ts2, 1, ts3);
5434 assertEquals("[top, [[up, down, strange], charm], bottom]",
5435              (String) ts3_ts2_ts3.invokeExact("top", "up", "down", "strange", "charm", "bottom"));
5436      * }</pre></blockquote>
5437      * <p>Here is pseudocode for the resulting adapter. In the code, {@code T}
5438      * represents the return type of the {@code target} and resulting adapter.
5439      * {@code V}/{@code v} stand for the return type and value of the
5440      * {@code filter}, which are also found in the signature and arguments of
5441      * the {@code target}, respectively, unless {@code V} is {@code void}.
5442      * {@code A}/{@code a} and {@code C}/{@code c} represent the parameter types
5443      * and values preceding and following the collection position, {@code pos},
5444      * in the {@code target}'s signature. They also turn up in the resulting
5445      * adapter's signature and arguments, where they surround
5446      * {@code B}/{@code b}, which represent the parameter types and arguments
5447      * to the {@code filter} (if any).
5448      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5449      * T target(A...,V,C...);
5450      * V filter(B...);
5451      * T adapter(A... a,B... b,C... c) {
5452      *   V v = filter(b...);
5453      *   return target(a...,v,c...);
5454      * }
5455      * // and if the filter has no arguments:
5456      * T target2(A...,V,C...);
5457      * V filter2();
5458      * T adapter2(A... a,C... c) {
5459      *   V v = filter2();
5460      *   return target2(a...,v,c...);
5461      * }
5462      * // and if the filter has a void return:
5463      * T target3(A...,C...);
5464      * void filter3(B...);
5465      * T adapter3(A... a,B... b,C... c) {
5466      *   filter3(b...);
5467      *   return target3(a...,c...);
5468      * }
5469      * }</pre></blockquote>
5470      * <p>
5471      * A collection adapter {@code collectArguments(mh, 0, coll)} is equivalent to
5472      * one which first "folds" the affected arguments, and then drops them, in separate
5473      * steps as follows:
5474      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5475      * mh = MethodHandles.dropArguments(mh, 1, coll.type().parameterList()); //step 2
5476      * mh = MethodHandles.foldArguments(mh, coll); //step 1
5477      * }</pre></blockquote>
5478      * If the target method handle consumes no arguments besides than the result
5479      * (if any) of the filter {@code coll}, then {@code collectArguments(mh, 0, coll)}
5480      * is equivalent to {@code filterReturnValue(coll, mh)}.
5481      * If the filter method handle {@code coll} consumes one argument and produces
5482      * a non-void result, then {@code collectArguments(mh, N, coll)}
5483      * is equivalent to {@code filterArguments(mh, N, coll)}.
5484      * Other equivalences are possible but would require argument permutation.
5485      * <p>
5486      * <em>Note:</em> The resulting adapter is never a {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector
5487      * variable-arity method handle}, even if the original target method handle was.
5488      *
5489      * @param target the method handle to invoke after filtering the subsequence of arguments
5490      * @param pos the position of the first adapter argument to pass to the filter,
5491      *            and/or the target argument which receives the result of the filter
5492      * @param filter method handle to call on the subsequence of arguments
5493      * @return method handle which incorporates the specified argument subsequence filtering logic
5494      * @throws NullPointerException if either argument is null
5495      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the return type of {@code filter}
5496      *          is non-void and is not the same as the {@code pos} argument of the target,
5497      *          or if {@code pos} is not between 0 and the target's arity, inclusive,
5498      *          or if the resulting method handle's type would have
5499      *          <a href="MethodHandle.html#maxarity">too many parameters</a>
5500      * @see MethodHandles#foldArguments
5501      * @see MethodHandles#filterArguments
5502      * @see MethodHandles#filterReturnValue
5503      */
5504     public static MethodHandle collectArguments(MethodHandle target, int pos, MethodHandle filter) {
5505         MethodType newType = collectArgumentsChecks(target, pos, filter);
5506         MethodType collectorType = filter.type();
5507         BoundMethodHandle result = target.rebind();
5508         LambdaForm lform;
5509         if (collectorType.returnType().isArray() && filter.intrinsicName() == Intrinsic.NEW_ARRAY) {
5510             lform = result.editor().collectArgumentArrayForm(1 + pos, filter);
5511             if (lform != null) {
5512                 return result.copyWith(newType, lform);
5513             }
5514         }
5515         lform = result.editor().collectArgumentsForm(1 + pos, collectorType.basicType());
5516         return result.copyWithExtendL(newType, lform, filter);
5517     }
5518 
5519     private static MethodType collectArgumentsChecks(MethodHandle target, int pos, MethodHandle filter) throws RuntimeException {
5520         MethodType targetType = target.type();
5521         MethodType filterType = filter.type();
5522         Class<?> rtype = filterType.returnType();
5523         List<Class<?>> filterArgs = filterType.parameterList();
5524         if (rtype == void.class) {
5525             return targetType.insertParameterTypes(pos, filterArgs);
5526         }
5527         if (rtype != targetType.parameterType(pos)) {
5528             throw newIllegalArgumentException("target and filter types do not match", targetType, filterType);
5529         }
5530         return targetType.dropParameterTypes(pos, pos+1).insertParameterTypes(pos, filterArgs);
5531     }
5532 
5533     /**
5534      * Adapts a target method handle by post-processing
5535      * its return value (if any) with a filter (another method handle).
5536      * The result of the filter is returned from the adapter.
5537      * <p>
5538      * If the target returns a value, the filter must accept that value as
5539      * its only argument.
5540      * If the target returns void, the filter must accept no arguments.
5541      * <p>
5542      * The return type of the filter
5543      * replaces the return type of the target
5544      * in the resulting adapted method handle.
5545      * The argument type of the filter (if any) must be identical to the
5546      * return type of the target.
5547      * <p><b>Example:</b>
5548      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5549 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.*;
5550 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodType.*;
5551 ...
5552 MethodHandle cat = lookup().findVirtual(String.class,
5553   "concat", methodType(String.class, String.class));
5554 MethodHandle length = lookup().findVirtual(String.class,
5555   "length", methodType(int.class));
5556 System.out.println((String) cat.invokeExact("x", "y")); // xy
5557 MethodHandle f0 = filterReturnValue(cat, length);
5558 System.out.println((int) f0.invokeExact("x", "y")); // 2
5559      * }</pre></blockquote>
5560      * <p>Here is pseudocode for the resulting adapter. In the code,
5561      * {@code T}/{@code t} represent the result type and value of the
5562      * {@code target}; {@code V}, the result type of the {@code filter}; and
5563      * {@code A}/{@code a}, the types and values of the parameters and arguments
5564      * of the {@code target} as well as the resulting adapter.
5565      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5566      * T target(A...);
5567      * V filter(T);
5568      * V adapter(A... a) {
5569      *   T t = target(a...);
5570      *   return filter(t);
5571      * }
5572      * // and if the target has a void return:
5573      * void target2(A...);
5574      * V filter2();
5575      * V adapter2(A... a) {
5576      *   target2(a...);
5577      *   return filter2();
5578      * }
5579      * // and if the filter has a void return:
5580      * T target3(A...);
5581      * void filter3(V);
5582      * void adapter3(A... a) {
5583      *   T t = target3(a...);
5584      *   filter3(t);
5585      * }
5586      * }</pre></blockquote>
5587      * <p>
5588      * <em>Note:</em> The resulting adapter is never a {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector
5589      * variable-arity method handle}, even if the original target method handle was.
5590      * @param target the method handle to invoke before filtering the return value
5591      * @param filter method handle to call on the return value
5592      * @return method handle which incorporates the specified return value filtering logic
5593      * @throws NullPointerException if either argument is null
5594      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the argument list of {@code filter}
5595      *          does not match the return type of target as described above
5596      */
5597     public static MethodHandle filterReturnValue(MethodHandle target, MethodHandle filter) {
5598         MethodType targetType = target.type();
5599         MethodType filterType = filter.type();
5600         filterReturnValueChecks(targetType, filterType);
5601         BoundMethodHandle result = target.rebind();
5602         BasicType rtype = BasicType.basicType(filterType.returnType());
5603         LambdaForm lform = result.editor().filterReturnForm(rtype, false);
5604         MethodType newType = targetType.changeReturnType(filterType.returnType());
5605         result = result.copyWithExtendL(newType, lform, filter);
5606         return result;
5607     }
5608 
5609     private static void filterReturnValueChecks(MethodType targetType, MethodType filterType) throws RuntimeException {
5610         Class<?> rtype = targetType.returnType();
5611         int filterValues = filterType.parameterCount();
5612         if (filterValues == 0
5613                 ? (rtype != void.class)
5614                 : (rtype != filterType.parameterType(0) || filterValues != 1))
5615             throw newIllegalArgumentException("target and filter types do not match", targetType, filterType);
5616     }
5617 
5618     /**
5619      * Filter the return value of a target method handle with a filter function. The filter function is
5620      * applied to the return value of the original handle; if the filter specifies more than one parameters,
5621      * then any remaining parameter is appended to the adapter handle. In other words, the adaptation works
5622      * as follows:
5623      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5624      * T target(A...)
5625      * V filter(B... , T)
5626      * V adapter(A... a, B... b) {
5627      *     T t = target(a...);
5628      *     return filter(b..., t);
5629      * }</pre></blockquote>
5630      * <p>
5631      * If the filter handle is a unary function, then this method behaves like {@link #filterReturnValue(MethodHandle, MethodHandle)}.
5632      *
5633      * @param target the target method handle
5634      * @param filter the filter method handle
5635      * @return the adapter method handle
5636      */
5637     /* package */ static MethodHandle collectReturnValue(MethodHandle target, MethodHandle filter) {
5638         MethodType targetType = target.type();
5639         MethodType filterType = filter.type();
5640         BoundMethodHandle result = target.rebind();
5641         LambdaForm lform = result.editor().collectReturnValueForm(filterType.basicType());
5642         MethodType newType = targetType.changeReturnType(filterType.returnType());
5643         if (filterType.parameterList().size() > 1) {
5644             for (int i = 0 ; i < filterType.parameterList().size() - 1 ; i++) {
5645                 newType = newType.appendParameterTypes(filterType.parameterType(i));
5646             }
5647         }
5648         result = result.copyWithExtendL(newType, lform, filter);
5649         return result;
5650     }
5651 
5652     /**
5653      * Adapts a target method handle by pre-processing
5654      * some of its arguments, and then calling the target with
5655      * the result of the pre-processing, inserted into the original
5656      * sequence of arguments.
5657      * <p>
5658      * The pre-processing is performed by {@code combiner}, a second method handle.
5659      * Of the arguments passed to the adapter, the first {@code N} arguments
5660      * are copied to the combiner, which is then called.
5661      * (Here, {@code N} is defined as the parameter count of the combiner.)
5662      * After this, control passes to the target, with any result
5663      * from the combiner inserted before the original {@code N} incoming
5664      * arguments.
5665      * <p>
5666      * If the combiner returns a value, the first parameter type of the target
5667      * must be identical with the return type of the combiner, and the next
5668      * {@code N} parameter types of the target must exactly match the parameters
5669      * of the combiner.
5670      * <p>
5671      * If the combiner has a void return, no result will be inserted,
5672      * and the first {@code N} parameter types of the target
5673      * must exactly match the parameters of the combiner.
5674      * <p>
5675      * The resulting adapter is the same type as the target, except that the
5676      * first parameter type is dropped,
5677      * if it corresponds to the result of the combiner.
5678      * <p>
5679      * (Note that {@link #dropArguments(MethodHandle,int,List) dropArguments} can be used to remove any arguments
5680      * that either the combiner or the target does not wish to receive.
5681      * If some of the incoming arguments are destined only for the combiner,
5682      * consider using {@link MethodHandle#asCollector asCollector} instead, since those
5683      * arguments will not need to be live on the stack on entry to the
5684      * target.)
5685      * <p><b>Example:</b>
5686      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5687 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.*;
5688 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodType.*;
5689 ...
5690 MethodHandle trace = publicLookup().findVirtual(java.io.PrintStream.class,
5691   "println", methodType(void.class, String.class))
5692     .bindTo(System.out);
5693 MethodHandle cat = lookup().findVirtual(String.class,
5694   "concat", methodType(String.class, String.class));
5695 assertEquals("boojum", (String) cat.invokeExact("boo", "jum"));
5696 MethodHandle catTrace = foldArguments(cat, trace);
5697 // also prints "boo":
5698 assertEquals("boojum", (String) catTrace.invokeExact("boo", "jum"));
5699      * }</pre></blockquote>
5700      * <p>Here is pseudocode for the resulting adapter. In the code, {@code T}
5701      * represents the result type of the {@code target} and resulting adapter.
5702      * {@code V}/{@code v} represent the type and value of the parameter and argument
5703      * of {@code target} that precedes the folding position; {@code V} also is
5704      * the result type of the {@code combiner}. {@code A}/{@code a} denote the
5705      * types and values of the {@code N} parameters and arguments at the folding
5706      * position. {@code B}/{@code b} represent the types and values of the
5707      * {@code target} parameters and arguments that follow the folded parameters
5708      * and arguments.
5709      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5710      * // there are N arguments in A...
5711      * T target(V, A[N]..., B...);
5712      * V combiner(A...);
5713      * T adapter(A... a, B... b) {
5714      *   V v = combiner(a...);
5715      *   return target(v, a..., b...);
5716      * }
5717      * // and if the combiner has a void return:
5718      * T target2(A[N]..., B...);
5719      * void combiner2(A...);
5720      * T adapter2(A... a, B... b) {
5721      *   combiner2(a...);
5722      *   return target2(a..., b...);
5723      * }
5724      * }</pre></blockquote>
5725      * <p>
5726      * <em>Note:</em> The resulting adapter is never a {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector
5727      * variable-arity method handle}, even if the original target method handle was.
5728      * @param target the method handle to invoke after arguments are combined
5729      * @param combiner method handle to call initially on the incoming arguments
5730      * @return method handle which incorporates the specified argument folding logic
5731      * @throws NullPointerException if either argument is null
5732      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if {@code combiner}'s return type
5733      *          is non-void and not the same as the first argument type of
5734      *          the target, or if the initial {@code N} argument types
5735      *          of the target
5736      *          (skipping one matching the {@code combiner}'s return type)
5737      *          are not identical with the argument types of {@code combiner}
5738      */
5739     public static MethodHandle foldArguments(MethodHandle target, MethodHandle combiner) {
5740         return foldArguments(target, 0, combiner);
5741     }
5742 
5743     /**
5744      * Adapts a target method handle by pre-processing some of its arguments, starting at a given position, and then
5745      * calling the target with the result of the pre-processing, inserted into the original sequence of arguments just
5746      * before the folded arguments.
5747      * <p>
5748      * This method is closely related to {@link #foldArguments(MethodHandle, MethodHandle)}, but allows to control the
5749      * position in the parameter list at which folding takes place. The argument controlling this, {@code pos}, is a
5750      * zero-based index. The aforementioned method {@link #foldArguments(MethodHandle, MethodHandle)} assumes position
5751      * 0.
5752      *
5753      * @apiNote Example:
5754      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5755     import static java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.*;
5756     import static java.lang.invoke.MethodType.*;
5757     ...
5758     MethodHandle trace = publicLookup().findVirtual(java.io.PrintStream.class,
5759     "println", methodType(void.class, String.class))
5760     .bindTo(System.out);
5761     MethodHandle cat = lookup().findVirtual(String.class,
5762     "concat", methodType(String.class, String.class));
5763     assertEquals("boojum", (String) cat.invokeExact("boo", "jum"));
5764     MethodHandle catTrace = foldArguments(cat, 1, trace);
5765     // also prints "jum":
5766     assertEquals("boojum", (String) catTrace.invokeExact("boo", "jum"));
5767      * }</pre></blockquote>
5768      * <p>Here is pseudocode for the resulting adapter. In the code, {@code T}
5769      * represents the result type of the {@code target} and resulting adapter.
5770      * {@code V}/{@code v} represent the type and value of the parameter and argument
5771      * of {@code target} that precedes the folding position; {@code V} also is
5772      * the result type of the {@code combiner}. {@code A}/{@code a} denote the
5773      * types and values of the {@code N} parameters and arguments at the folding
5774      * position. {@code Z}/{@code z} and {@code B}/{@code b} represent the types
5775      * and values of the {@code target} parameters and arguments that precede and
5776      * follow the folded parameters and arguments starting at {@code pos},
5777      * respectively.
5778      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5779      * // there are N arguments in A...
5780      * T target(Z..., V, A[N]..., B...);
5781      * V combiner(A...);
5782      * T adapter(Z... z, A... a, B... b) {
5783      *   V v = combiner(a...);
5784      *   return target(z..., v, a..., b...);
5785      * }
5786      * // and if the combiner has a void return:
5787      * T target2(Z..., A[N]..., B...);
5788      * void combiner2(A...);
5789      * T adapter2(Z... z, A... a, B... b) {
5790      *   combiner2(a...);
5791      *   return target2(z..., a..., b...);
5792      * }
5793      * }</pre></blockquote>
5794      * <p>
5795      * <em>Note:</em> The resulting adapter is never a {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector
5796      * variable-arity method handle}, even if the original target method handle was.
5797      *
5798      * @param target the method handle to invoke after arguments are combined
5799      * @param pos the position at which to start folding and at which to insert the folding result; if this is {@code
5800      *            0}, the effect is the same as for {@link #foldArguments(MethodHandle, MethodHandle)}.
5801      * @param combiner method handle to call initially on the incoming arguments
5802      * @return method handle which incorporates the specified argument folding logic
5803      * @throws NullPointerException if either argument is null
5804      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if either of the following two conditions holds:
5805      *          (1) {@code combiner}'s return type is non-{@code void} and not the same as the argument type at position
5806      *              {@code pos} of the target signature;
5807      *          (2) the {@code N} argument types at position {@code pos} of the target signature (skipping one matching
5808      *              the {@code combiner}'s return type) are not identical with the argument types of {@code combiner}.
5809      *
5810      * @see #foldArguments(MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
5811      * @since 9
5812      */
5813     public static MethodHandle foldArguments(MethodHandle target, int pos, MethodHandle combiner) {
5814         MethodType targetType = target.type();
5815         MethodType combinerType = combiner.type();
5816         Class<?> rtype = foldArgumentChecks(pos, targetType, combinerType);
5817         BoundMethodHandle result = target.rebind();
5818         boolean dropResult = rtype == void.class;
5819         LambdaForm lform = result.editor().foldArgumentsForm(1 + pos, dropResult, combinerType.basicType());
5820         MethodType newType = targetType;
5821         if (!dropResult) {
5822             newType = newType.dropParameterTypes(pos, pos + 1);
5823         }
5824         result = result.copyWithExtendL(newType, lform, combiner);
5825         return result;
5826     }
5827 
5828     private static Class<?> foldArgumentChecks(int foldPos, MethodType targetType, MethodType combinerType) {
5829         int foldArgs   = combinerType.parameterCount();
5830         Class<?> rtype = combinerType.returnType();
5831         int foldVals = rtype == void.class ? 0 : 1;
5832         int afterInsertPos = foldPos + foldVals;
5833         boolean ok = (targetType.parameterCount() >= afterInsertPos + foldArgs);
5834         if (ok) {
5835             for (int i = 0; i < foldArgs; i++) {
5836                 if (combinerType.parameterType(i) != targetType.parameterType(i + afterInsertPos)) {
5837                     ok = false;
5838                     break;
5839                 }
5840             }
5841         }
5842         if (ok && foldVals != 0 && combinerType.returnType() != targetType.parameterType(foldPos))
5843             ok = false;
5844         if (!ok)
5845             throw misMatchedTypes("target and combiner types", targetType, combinerType);
5846         return rtype;
5847     }
5848 
5849     /**
5850      * Adapts a target method handle by pre-processing some of its arguments, then calling the target with the result
5851      * of the pre-processing replacing the argument at the given position.
5852      *
5853      * @param target the method handle to invoke after arguments are combined
5854      * @param position the position at which to start folding and at which to insert the folding result; if this is {@code
5855      *            0}, the effect is the same as for {@link #foldArguments(MethodHandle, MethodHandle)}.
5856      * @param combiner method handle to call initially on the incoming arguments
5857      * @param argPositions indexes of the target to pick arguments sent to the combiner from
5858      * @return method handle which incorporates the specified argument folding logic
5859      * @throws NullPointerException if either argument is null
5860      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if either of the following two conditions holds:
5861      *          (1) {@code combiner}'s return type is not the same as the argument type at position
5862      *              {@code pos} of the target signature;
5863      *          (2) the {@code N} argument types at positions {@code argPositions[1...N]} of the target signature are
5864      *              not identical with the argument types of {@code combiner}.
5865      */
5866     /*non-public*/
5867     static MethodHandle filterArgumentsWithCombiner(MethodHandle target, int position, MethodHandle combiner, int ... argPositions) {
5868         return argumentsWithCombiner(true, target, position, combiner, argPositions);
5869     }
5870 
5871     /**
5872      * Adapts a target method handle by pre-processing some of its arguments, calling the target with the result of
5873      * the pre-processing inserted into the original sequence of arguments at the given position.
5874      *
5875      * @param target the method handle to invoke after arguments are combined
5876      * @param position the position at which to start folding and at which to insert the folding result; if this is {@code
5877      *            0}, the effect is the same as for {@link #foldArguments(MethodHandle, MethodHandle)}.
5878      * @param combiner method handle to call initially on the incoming arguments
5879      * @param argPositions indexes of the target to pick arguments sent to the combiner from
5880      * @return method handle which incorporates the specified argument folding logic
5881      * @throws NullPointerException if either argument is null
5882      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if either of the following two conditions holds:
5883      *          (1) {@code combiner}'s return type is non-{@code void} and not the same as the argument type at position
5884      *              {@code pos} of the target signature;
5885      *          (2) the {@code N} argument types at positions {@code argPositions[1...N]} of the target signature
5886      *              (skipping {@code position} where the {@code combiner}'s return will be folded in) are not identical
5887      *              with the argument types of {@code combiner}.
5888      */
5889     /*non-public*/
5890     static MethodHandle foldArgumentsWithCombiner(MethodHandle target, int position, MethodHandle combiner, int ... argPositions) {
5891         return argumentsWithCombiner(false, target, position, combiner, argPositions);
5892     }
5893 
5894     private static MethodHandle argumentsWithCombiner(boolean filter, MethodHandle target, int position, MethodHandle combiner, int ... argPositions) {
5895         MethodType targetType = target.type();
5896         MethodType combinerType = combiner.type();
5897         Class<?> rtype = argumentsWithCombinerChecks(position, filter, targetType, combinerType, argPositions);
5898         BoundMethodHandle result = target.rebind();
5899 
5900         MethodType newType = targetType;
5901         LambdaForm lform;
5902         if (filter) {
5903             lform = result.editor().filterArgumentsForm(1 + position, combinerType.basicType(), argPositions);
5904         } else {
5905             boolean dropResult = rtype == void.class;
5906             lform = result.editor().foldArgumentsForm(1 + position, dropResult, combinerType.basicType(), argPositions);
5907             if (!dropResult) {
5908                 newType = newType.dropParameterTypes(position, position + 1);
5909             }
5910         }
5911         result = result.copyWithExtendL(newType, lform, combiner);
5912         return result;
5913     }
5914 
5915     private static Class<?> argumentsWithCombinerChecks(int position, boolean filter, MethodType targetType, MethodType combinerType, int ... argPos) {
5916         int combinerArgs = combinerType.parameterCount();
5917         if (argPos.length != combinerArgs) {
5918             throw newIllegalArgumentException("combiner and argument map must be equal size", combinerType, argPos.length);
5919         }
5920         Class<?> rtype = combinerType.returnType();
5921 
5922         for (int i = 0; i < combinerArgs; i++) {
5923             int arg = argPos[i];
5924             if (arg < 0 || arg > targetType.parameterCount()) {
5925                 throw newIllegalArgumentException("arg outside of target parameterRange", targetType, arg);
5926             }
5927             if (combinerType.parameterType(i) != targetType.parameterType(arg)) {
5928                 throw newIllegalArgumentException("target argument type at position " + arg
5929                         + " must match combiner argument type at index " + i + ": " + targetType
5930                         + " -> " + combinerType + ", map: " + Arrays.toString(argPos));
5931             }
5932         }
5933         if (filter && combinerType.returnType() != targetType.parameterType(position)) {
5934             throw misMatchedTypes("target and combiner types", targetType, combinerType);
5935         }
5936         return rtype;
5937     }
5938 
5939     /**
5940      * Makes a method handle which adapts a target method handle,
5941      * by guarding it with a test, a boolean-valued method handle.
5942      * If the guard fails, a fallback handle is called instead.
5943      * All three method handles must have the same corresponding
5944      * argument and return types, except that the return type
5945      * of the test must be boolean, and the test is allowed
5946      * to have fewer arguments than the other two method handles.
5947      * <p>
5948      * Here is pseudocode for the resulting adapter. In the code, {@code T}
5949      * represents the uniform result type of the three involved handles;
5950      * {@code A}/{@code a}, the types and values of the {@code target}
5951      * parameters and arguments that are consumed by the {@code test}; and
5952      * {@code B}/{@code b}, those types and values of the {@code target}
5953      * parameters and arguments that are not consumed by the {@code test}.
5954      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5955      * boolean test(A...);
5956      * T target(A...,B...);
5957      * T fallback(A...,B...);
5958      * T adapter(A... a,B... b) {
5959      *   if (test(a...))
5960      *     return target(a..., b...);
5961      *   else
5962      *     return fallback(a..., b...);
5963      * }
5964      * }</pre></blockquote>
5965      * Note that the test arguments ({@code a...} in the pseudocode) cannot
5966      * be modified by execution of the test, and so are passed unchanged
5967      * from the caller to the target or fallback as appropriate.
5968      * @param test method handle used for test, must return boolean
5969      * @param target method handle to call if test passes
5970      * @param fallback method handle to call if test fails
5971      * @return method handle which incorporates the specified if/then/else logic
5972      * @throws NullPointerException if any argument is null
5973      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if {@code test} does not return boolean,
5974      *          or if all three method types do not match (with the return
5975      *          type of {@code test} changed to match that of the target).
5976      */
5977     public static MethodHandle guardWithTest(MethodHandle test,
5978                                MethodHandle target,
5979                                MethodHandle fallback) {
5980         MethodType gtype = test.type();
5981         MethodType ttype = target.type();
5982         MethodType ftype = fallback.type();
5983         if (!ttype.equals(ftype))
5984             throw misMatchedTypes("target and fallback types", ttype, ftype);
5985         if (gtype.returnType() != boolean.class)
5986             throw newIllegalArgumentException("guard type is not a predicate "+gtype);
5987         List<Class<?>> targs = ttype.parameterList();
5988         test = dropArgumentsToMatch(test, 0, targs, 0, true);
5989         if (test == null) {
5990             throw misMatchedTypes("target and test types", ttype, gtype);
5991         }
5992         return MethodHandleImpl.makeGuardWithTest(test, target, fallback);
5993     }
5994 
5995     static <T> RuntimeException misMatchedTypes(String what, T t1, T t2) {
5996         return newIllegalArgumentException(what + " must match: " + t1 + " != " + t2);
5997     }
5998 
5999     /**
6000      * Makes a method handle which adapts a target method handle,
6001      * by running it inside an exception handler.
6002      * If the target returns normally, the adapter returns that value.
6003      * If an exception matching the specified type is thrown, the fallback
6004      * handle is called instead on the exception, plus the original arguments.
6005      * <p>
6006      * The target and handler must have the same corresponding
6007      * argument and return types, except that handler may omit trailing arguments
6008      * (similarly to the predicate in {@link #guardWithTest guardWithTest}).
6009      * Also, the handler must have an extra leading parameter of {@code exType} or a supertype.
6010      * <p>
6011      * Here is pseudocode for the resulting adapter. In the code, {@code T}
6012      * represents the return type of the {@code target} and {@code handler},
6013      * and correspondingly that of the resulting adapter; {@code A}/{@code a},
6014      * the types and values of arguments to the resulting handle consumed by
6015      * {@code handler}; and {@code B}/{@code b}, those of arguments to the
6016      * resulting handle discarded by {@code handler}.
6017      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6018      * T target(A..., B...);
6019      * T handler(ExType, A...);
6020      * T adapter(A... a, B... b) {
6021      *   try {
6022      *     return target(a..., b...);
6023      *   } catch (ExType ex) {
6024      *     return handler(ex, a...);
6025      *   }
6026      * }
6027      * }</pre></blockquote>
6028      * Note that the saved arguments ({@code a...} in the pseudocode) cannot
6029      * be modified by execution of the target, and so are passed unchanged
6030      * from the caller to the handler, if the handler is invoked.
6031      * <p>
6032      * The target and handler must return the same type, even if the handler
6033      * always throws.  (This might happen, for instance, because the handler
6034      * is simulating a {@code finally} clause).
6035      * To create such a throwing handler, compose the handler creation logic
6036      * with {@link #throwException throwException},
6037      * in order to create a method handle of the correct return type.
6038      * @param target method handle to call
6039      * @param exType the type of exception which the handler will catch
6040      * @param handler method handle to call if a matching exception is thrown
6041      * @return method handle which incorporates the specified try/catch logic
6042      * @throws NullPointerException if any argument is null
6043      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if {@code handler} does not accept
6044      *          the given exception type, or if the method handle types do
6045      *          not match in their return types and their
6046      *          corresponding parameters
6047      * @see MethodHandles#tryFinally(MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
6048      */
6049     public static MethodHandle catchException(MethodHandle target,
6050                                 Class<? extends Throwable> exType,
6051                                 MethodHandle handler) {
6052         MethodType ttype = target.type();
6053         MethodType htype = handler.type();
6054         if (!Throwable.class.isAssignableFrom(exType))
6055             throw new ClassCastException(exType.getName());
6056         if (htype.parameterCount() < 1 ||
6057             !htype.parameterType(0).isAssignableFrom(exType))
6058             throw newIllegalArgumentException("handler does not accept exception type "+exType);
6059         if (htype.returnType() != ttype.returnType())
6060             throw misMatchedTypes("target and handler return types", ttype, htype);
6061         handler = dropArgumentsToMatch(handler, 1, ttype.parameterList(), 0, true);
6062         if (handler == null) {
6063             throw misMatchedTypes("target and handler types", ttype, htype);
6064         }
6065         return MethodHandleImpl.makeGuardWithCatch(target, exType, handler);
6066     }
6067 
6068     /**
6069      * Produces a method handle which will throw exceptions of the given {@code exType}.
6070      * The method handle will accept a single argument of {@code exType},
6071      * and immediately throw it as an exception.
6072      * The method type will nominally specify a return of {@code returnType}.
6073      * The return type may be anything convenient:  It doesn't matter to the
6074      * method handle's behavior, since it will never return normally.
6075      * @param returnType the return type of the desired method handle
6076      * @param exType the parameter type of the desired method handle
6077      * @return method handle which can throw the given exceptions
6078      * @throws NullPointerException if either argument is null
6079      */
6080     public static MethodHandle throwException(Class<?> returnType, Class<? extends Throwable> exType) {
6081         if (!Throwable.class.isAssignableFrom(exType))
6082             throw new ClassCastException(exType.getName());
6083         return MethodHandleImpl.throwException(methodType(returnType, exType));
6084     }
6085 
6086     /**
6087      * Constructs a method handle representing a loop with several loop variables that are updated and checked upon each
6088      * iteration. Upon termination of the loop due to one of the predicates, a corresponding finalizer is run and
6089      * delivers the loop's result, which is the return value of the resulting handle.
6090      * <p>
6091      * Intuitively, every loop is formed by one or more "clauses", each specifying a local <em>iteration variable</em> and/or a loop
6092      * exit. Each iteration of the loop executes each clause in order. A clause can optionally update its iteration
6093      * variable; it can also optionally perform a test and conditional loop exit. In order to express this logic in
6094      * terms of method handles, each clause will specify up to four independent actions:<ul>
6095      * <li><em>init:</em> Before the loop executes, the initialization of an iteration variable {@code v} of type {@code V}.
6096      * <li><em>step:</em> When a clause executes, an update step for the iteration variable {@code v}.
6097      * <li><em>pred:</em> When a clause executes, a predicate execution to test for loop exit.
6098      * <li><em>fini:</em> If a clause causes a loop exit, a finalizer execution to compute the loop's return value.
6099      * </ul>
6100      * The full sequence of all iteration variable types, in clause order, will be notated as {@code (V...)}.
6101      * The values themselves will be {@code (v...)}.  When we speak of "parameter lists", we will usually
6102      * be referring to types, but in some contexts (describing execution) the lists will be of actual values.
6103      * <p>
6104      * Some of these clause parts may be omitted according to certain rules, and useful default behavior is provided in
6105      * this case. See below for a detailed description.
