6106      * <p>
6107      * <em>Parameters optional everywhere:</em>
6108      * Each clause function is allowed but not required to accept a parameter for each iteration variable {@code v}.
6109      * As an exception, the init functions cannot take any {@code v} parameters,
6110      * because those values are not yet computed when the init functions are executed.
6111      * Any clause function may neglect to take any trailing subsequence of parameters it is entitled to take.
6112      * In fact, any clause function may take no arguments at all.
6113      * <p>
6114      * <em>Loop parameters:</em>
6115      * A clause function may take all the iteration variable values it is entitled to, in which case
6116      * it may also take more trailing parameters. Such extra values are called <em>loop parameters</em>,
6117      * with their types and values notated as {@code (A...)} and {@code (a...)}.
6118      * These become the parameters of the resulting loop handle, to be supplied whenever the loop is executed.
6119      * (Since init functions do not accept iteration variables {@code v}, any parameter to an
6120      * init function is automatically a loop parameter {@code a}.)
6121      * As with iteration variables, clause functions are allowed but not required to accept loop parameters.
6122      * These loop parameters act as loop-invariant values visible across the whole loop.
6123      * <p>
6124      * <em>Parameters visible everywhere:</em>
6125      * Each non-init clause function is permitted to observe the entire loop state, because it can be passed the full
6126      * list {@code (v... a...)} of current iteration variable values and incoming loop parameters.
6127      * The init functions can observe initial pre-loop state, in the form {@code (a...)}.
6128      * Most clause functions will not need all of this information, but they will be formally connected to it
6129      * as if by {@link #dropArguments}.
6130      * <a id="astar"></a>
6131      * More specifically, we shall use the notation {@code (V*)} to express an arbitrary prefix of a full
6132      * sequence {@code (V...)} (and likewise for {@code (v*)}, {@code (A*)}, {@code (a*)}).
6133      * In that notation, the general form of an init function parameter list
6134      * is {@code (A*)}, and the general form of a non-init function parameter list is {@code (V*)} or {@code (V... A*)}.
6135      * <p>
6136      * <em>Checking clause structure:</em>
6137      * Given a set of clauses, there is a number of checks and adjustments performed to connect all the parts of the
6138      * loop. They are spelled out in detail in the steps below. In these steps, every occurrence of the word "must"
6139      * corresponds to a place where {@link IllegalArgumentException} will be thrown if the required constraint is not
6140      * met by the inputs to the loop combinator.
6141      * <p>
6142      * <em>Effectively identical sequences:</em>
6143      * <a id="effid"></a>
6144      * A parameter list {@code A} is defined to be <em>effectively identical</em> to another parameter list {@code B}
6145      * if {@code A} and {@code B} are identical, or if {@code A} is shorter and is identical with a proper prefix of {@code B}.
6146      * When speaking of an unordered set of parameter lists, we say they the set is "effectively identical"
6147      * as a whole if the set contains a longest list, and all members of the set are effectively identical to
6148      * that longest list.
6149      * For example, any set of type sequences of the form {@code (V*)} is effectively identical,
6150      * and the same is true if more sequences of the form {@code (V... A*)} are added.
6151      * <p>
6152      * <em>Step 0: Determine clause structure.</em><ol type="a">
6153      * <li>The clause array (of type {@code MethodHandle[][]}) must be non-{@code null} and contain at least one element.
6154      * <li>The clause array may not contain {@code null}s or sub-arrays longer than four elements.
6155      * <li>Clauses shorter than four elements are treated as if they were padded by {@code null} elements to length
6156      * four. Padding takes place by appending elements to the array.
6157      * <li>Clauses with all {@code null}s are disregarded.
6158      * <li>Each clause is treated as a four-tuple of functions, called "init", "step", "pred", and "fini".
6159      * </ol>
6160      * <p>
6161      * <em>Step 1A: Determine iteration variable types {@code (V...)}.</em><ol type="a">
6162      * <li>The iteration variable type for each clause is determined using the clause's init and step return types.
6163      * <li>If both functions are omitted, there is no iteration variable for the corresponding clause ({@code void} is
6164      * used as the type to indicate that). If one of them is omitted, the other's return type defines the clause's
6165      * iteration variable type. If both are given, the common return type (they must be identical) defines the clause's
6166      * iteration variable type.
6167      * <li>Form the list of return types (in clause order), omitting all occurrences of {@code void}.
6168      * <li>This list of types is called the "iteration variable types" ({@code (V...)}).
6169      * </ol>
6170      * <p>
6171      * <em>Step 1B: Determine loop parameters {@code (A...)}.</em><ul>
6172      * <li>Examine and collect init function parameter lists (which are of the form {@code (A*)}).
6173      * <li>Examine and collect the suffixes of the step, pred, and fini parameter lists, after removing the iteration variable types.
6174      * (They must have the form {@code (V... A*)}; collect the {@code (A*)} parts only.)
6175      * <li>Do not collect suffixes from step, pred, and fini parameter lists that do not begin with all the iteration variable types.
6176      * (These types will be checked in step 2, along with all the clause function types.)
6177      * <li>Omitted clause functions are ignored.  (Equivalently, they are deemed to have empty parameter lists.)
6178      * <li>All of the collected parameter lists must be effectively identical.
6179      * <li>The longest parameter list (which is necessarily unique) is called the "external parameter list" ({@code (A...)}).
6180      * <li>If there is no such parameter list, the external parameter list is taken to be the empty sequence.
6181      * <li>The combined list consisting of iteration variable types followed by the external parameter types is called
6182      * the "internal parameter list".
6183      * </ul>
6184      * <p>
6185      * <em>Step 1C: Determine loop return type.</em><ol type="a">
6186      * <li>Examine fini function return types, disregarding omitted fini functions.
6187      * <li>If there are no fini functions, the loop return type is {@code void}.
6188      * <li>Otherwise, the common return type {@code R} of the fini functions (their return types must be identical) defines the loop return
6189      * type.
6190      * </ol>
6191      * <p>
6192      * <em>Step 1D: Check other types.</em><ol type="a">
6193      * <li>There must be at least one non-omitted pred function.
6194      * <li>Every non-omitted pred function must have a {@code boolean} return type.
6195      * </ol>
6196      * <p>
6197      * <em>Step 2: Determine parameter lists.</em><ol type="a">
6198      * <li>The parameter list for the resulting loop handle will be the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
6199      * <li>The parameter list for init functions will be adjusted to the external parameter list.
6200      * (Note that their parameter lists are already effectively identical to this list.)
6201      * <li>The parameter list for every non-omitted, non-init (step, pred, and fini) function must be
6202      * effectively identical to the internal parameter list {@code (V... A...)}.
6203      * </ol>
6204      * <p>
6205      * <em>Step 3: Fill in omitted functions.</em><ol type="a">
6206      * <li>If an init function is omitted, use a {@linkplain #empty default value} for the clause's iteration variable
6207      * type.
6208      * <li>If a step function is omitted, use an {@linkplain #identity identity function} of the clause's iteration
6209      * variable type; insert dropped argument parameters before the identity function parameter for the non-{@code void}
6210      * iteration variables of preceding clauses. (This will turn the loop variable into a local loop invariant.)
6211      * <li>If a pred function is omitted, use a constant {@code true} function. (This will keep the loop going, as far
6212      * as this clause is concerned.  Note that in such cases the corresponding fini function is unreachable.)
6213      * <li>If a fini function is omitted, use a {@linkplain #empty default value} for the
6214      * loop return type.
6215      * </ol>
6216      * <p>
6217      * <em>Step 4: Fill in missing parameter types.</em><ol type="a">
6218      * <li>At this point, every init function parameter list is effectively identical to the external parameter list {@code (A...)},
6219      * but some lists may be shorter. For every init function with a short parameter list, pad out the end of the list.
6220      * <li>At this point, every non-init function parameter list is effectively identical to the internal parameter
6221      * list {@code (V... A...)}, but some lists may be shorter. For every non-init function with a short parameter list,
6222      * pad out the end of the list.
6223      * <li>Argument lists are padded out by {@linkplain #dropArgumentsToMatch(MethodHandle, int, List, int) dropping unused trailing arguments}.
6224      * </ol>
6225      * <p>
6226      * <em>Final observations.</em><ol type="a">
6227      * <li>After these steps, all clauses have been adjusted by supplying omitted functions and arguments.
6228      * <li>All init functions have a common parameter type list {@code (A...)}, which the final loop handle will also have.
6229      * <li>All fini functions have a common return type {@code R}, which the final loop handle will also have.
6230      * <li>All non-init functions have a common parameter type list {@code (V... A...)}, of
6231      * (non-{@code void}) iteration variables {@code V} followed by loop parameters.
6232      * <li>Each pair of init and step functions agrees in their return type {@code V}.
6233      * <li>Each non-init function will be able to observe the current values {@code (v...)} of all iteration variables.
6234      * <li>Every function will be able to observe the incoming values {@code (a...)} of all loop parameters.
6235      * </ol>
6236      * <p>
6237      * <em>Example.</em> As a consequence of step 1A above, the {@code loop} combinator has the following property:
6238      * <ul>
6239      * <li>Given {@code N} clauses {@code Cn = {null, Sn, Pn}} with {@code n = 1..N}.
6240      * <li>Suppose predicate handles {@code Pn} are either {@code null} or have no parameters.
6241      * (Only one {@code Pn} has to be non-{@code null}.)
6242      * <li>Suppose step handles {@code Sn} have signatures {@code (B1..BX)Rn}, for some constant {@code X>=N}.
6243      * <li>Suppose {@code Q} is the count of non-void types {@code Rn}, and {@code (V1...VQ)} is the sequence of those types.
6244      * <li>It must be that {@code Vn == Bn} for {@code n = 1..min(X,Q)}.
6245      * <li>The parameter types {@code Vn} will be interpreted as loop-local state elements {@code (V...)}.
6246      * <li>Any remaining types {@code BQ+1..BX} (if {@code Q<X}) will determine
6247      * the resulting loop handle's parameter types {@code (A...)}.
6248      * </ul>
6249      * In this example, the loop handle parameters {@code (A...)} were derived from the step functions,
6250      * which is natural if most of the loop computation happens in the steps.  For some loops,
6251      * the burden of computation might be heaviest in the pred functions, and so the pred functions
6252      * might need to accept the loop parameter values.  For loops with complex exit logic, the fini
6253      * functions might need to accept loop parameters, and likewise for loops with complex entry logic,
6254      * where the init functions will need the extra parameters.  For such reasons, the rules for
6255      * determining these parameters are as symmetric as possible, across all clause parts.
6256      * In general, the loop parameters function as common invariant values across the whole
6257      * loop, while the iteration variables function as common variant values, or (if there is
6258      * no step function) as internal loop invariant temporaries.
6259      * <p>
6260      * <em>Loop execution.</em><ol type="a">
6261      * <li>When the loop is called, the loop input values are saved in locals, to be passed to
6262      * every clause function. These locals are loop invariant.
6263      * <li>Each init function is executed in clause order (passing the external arguments {@code (a...)})
6264      * and the non-{@code void} values are saved (as the iteration variables {@code (v...)}) into locals.
6265      * These locals will be loop varying (unless their steps behave as identity functions, as noted above).
6266      * <li>All function executions (except init functions) will be passed the internal parameter list, consisting of
6267      * the non-{@code void} iteration values {@code (v...)} (in clause order) and then the loop inputs {@code (a...)}
6268      * (in argument order).
6269      * <li>The step and pred functions are then executed, in clause order (step before pred), until a pred function
6270      * returns {@code false}.
6271      * <li>The non-{@code void} result from a step function call is used to update the corresponding value in the
6272      * sequence {@code (v...)} of loop variables.
6273      * The updated value is immediately visible to all subsequent function calls.
6274      * <li>If a pred function returns {@code false}, the corresponding fini function is called, and the resulting value
6275      * (of type {@code R}) is returned from the loop as a whole.
6276      * <li>If all the pred functions always return true, no fini function is ever invoked, and the loop cannot exit
6277      * except by throwing an exception.
6278      * </ol>
6279      * <p>
6280      * <em>Usage tips.</em>
6281      * <ul>
6282      * <li>Although each step function will receive the current values of <em>all</em> the loop variables,
6283      * sometimes a step function only needs to observe the current value of its own variable.
6284      * In that case, the step function may need to explicitly {@linkplain #dropArguments drop all preceding loop variables}.
6285      * This will require mentioning their types, in an expression like {@code dropArguments(step, 0, V0.class, ...)}.
6286      * <li>Loop variables are not required to vary; they can be loop invariant.  A clause can create
6287      * a loop invariant by a suitable init function with no step, pred, or fini function.  This may be
6288      * useful to "wire" an incoming loop argument into the step or pred function of an adjacent loop variable.
6289      * <li>If some of the clause functions are virtual methods on an instance, the instance
6290      * itself can be conveniently placed in an initial invariant loop "variable", using an initial clause
6291      * like {@code new MethodHandle[]{identity(ObjType.class)}}.  In that case, the instance reference
6292      * will be the first iteration variable value, and it will be easy to use virtual
6293      * methods as clause parts, since all of them will take a leading instance reference matching that value.
6294      * </ul>
6295      * <p>
6296      * Here is pseudocode for the resulting loop handle. As above, {@code V} and {@code v} represent the types
6297      * and values of loop variables; {@code A} and {@code a} represent arguments passed to the whole loop;
6298      * and {@code R} is the common result type of all finalizers as well as of the resulting loop.
6299      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6300      * V... init...(A...);
6301      * boolean pred...(V..., A...);
6302      * V... step...(V..., A...);
6303      * R fini...(V..., A...);
6304      * R loop(A... a) {
6305      *   V... v... = init...(a...);
6306      *   for (;;) {
6307      *     for ((v, p, s, f) in (v..., pred..., step..., fini...)) {
6308      *       v = s(v..., a...);
6309      *       if (!p(v..., a...)) {
6310      *         return f(v..., a...);
6311      *       }
6312      *     }
6313      *   }
6314      * }
6315      * }</pre></blockquote>
6316      * Note that the parameter type lists {@code (V...)} and {@code (A...)} have been expanded
6317      * to their full length, even though individual clause functions may neglect to take them all.
6318      * As noted above, missing parameters are filled in as if by {@link #dropArgumentsToMatch(MethodHandle, int, List, int)}.
6319      *
6320      * @apiNote Example:
6321      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6322      * // iterative implementation of the factorial function as a loop handle
6323      * static int one(int k) { return 1; }
6324      * static int inc(int i, int acc, int k) { return i + 1; }
6325      * static int mult(int i, int acc, int k) { return i * acc; }
6326      * static boolean pred(int i, int acc, int k) { return i < k; }
6327      * static int fin(int i, int acc, int k) { return acc; }
6328      * // assume MH_one, MH_inc, MH_mult, MH_pred, and MH_fin are handles to the above methods
6329      * // null initializer for counter, should initialize to 0
6330      * MethodHandle[] counterClause = new MethodHandle[]{null, MH_inc};
6331      * MethodHandle[] accumulatorClause = new MethodHandle[]{MH_one, MH_mult, MH_pred, MH_fin};
6332      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.loop(counterClause, accumulatorClause);
6333      * assertEquals(120, loop.invoke(5));
6334      * }</pre></blockquote>
6335      * The same example, dropping arguments and using combinators:
6336      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6337      * // simplified implementation of the factorial function as a loop handle
6338      * static int inc(int i) { return i + 1; } // drop acc, k
6339      * static int mult(int i, int acc) { return i * acc; } //drop k
6340      * static boolean cmp(int i, int k) { return i < k; }
6341      * // assume MH_inc, MH_mult, and MH_cmp are handles to the above methods
6342      * // null initializer for counter, should initialize to 0
6343      * MethodHandle MH_one = MethodHandles.constant(int.class, 1);
6344      * MethodHandle MH_pred = MethodHandles.dropArguments(MH_cmp, 1, int.class); // drop acc
6345      * MethodHandle MH_fin = MethodHandles.dropArguments(MethodHandles.identity(int.class), 0, int.class); // drop i
6346      * MethodHandle[] counterClause = new MethodHandle[]{null, MH_inc};
6347      * MethodHandle[] accumulatorClause = new MethodHandle[]{MH_one, MH_mult, MH_pred, MH_fin};
6348      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.loop(counterClause, accumulatorClause);
6349      * assertEquals(720, loop.invoke(6));
6350      * }</pre></blockquote>
6351      * A similar example, using a helper object to hold a loop parameter:
6352      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6353      * // instance-based implementation of the factorial function as a loop handle
6354      * static class FacLoop {
6355      *   final int k;
6356      *   FacLoop(int k) { this.k = k; }
6357      *   int inc(int i) { return i + 1; }
6358      *   int mult(int i, int acc) { return i * acc; }
6359      *   boolean pred(int i) { return i < k; }
6360      *   int fin(int i, int acc) { return acc; }
6361      * }
6362      * // assume MH_FacLoop is a handle to the constructor
6363      * // assume MH_inc, MH_mult, MH_pred, and MH_fin are handles to the above methods
6364      * // null initializer for counter, should initialize to 0
6365      * MethodHandle MH_one = MethodHandles.constant(int.class, 1);
6366      * MethodHandle[] instanceClause = new MethodHandle[]{MH_FacLoop};
6367      * MethodHandle[] counterClause = new MethodHandle[]{null, MH_inc};
6368      * MethodHandle[] accumulatorClause = new MethodHandle[]{MH_one, MH_mult, MH_pred, MH_fin};
6369      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.loop(instanceClause, counterClause, accumulatorClause);
6370      * assertEquals(5040, loop.invoke(7));
6371      * }</pre></blockquote>
6372      *
6373      * @param clauses an array of arrays (4-tuples) of {@link MethodHandle}s adhering to the rules described above.
6374      *
6375      * @return a method handle embodying the looping behavior as defined by the arguments.
6376      *
6377      * @throws IllegalArgumentException in case any of the constraints described above is violated.
6378      *
6379      * @see MethodHandles#whileLoop(MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
6380      * @see MethodHandles#doWhileLoop(MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
6381      * @see MethodHandles#countedLoop(MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
6382      * @see MethodHandles#iteratedLoop(MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
6383      * @since 9
6384      */
6385     public static MethodHandle loop(MethodHandle[]... clauses) {
6386         // Step 0: determine clause structure.
6387         loopChecks0(clauses);
6388 
6389         List<MethodHandle> init = new ArrayList<>();
6390         List<MethodHandle> step = new ArrayList<>();
6391         List<MethodHandle> pred = new ArrayList<>();
6392         List<MethodHandle> fini = new ArrayList<>();
6393 
6394         Stream.of(clauses).filter(c -> Stream.of(c).anyMatch(Objects::nonNull)).forEach(clause -> {
6395             init.add(clause[0]); // all clauses have at least length 1
6396             step.add(clause.length <= 1 ? null : clause[1]);
6397             pred.add(clause.length <= 2 ? null : clause[2]);
6398             fini.add(clause.length <= 3 ? null : clause[3]);
6399         });
6400 
6401         assert Stream.of(init, step, pred, fini).map(List::size).distinct().count() == 1;
6402         final int nclauses = init.size();
6403 
6404         // Step 1A: determine iteration variables (V...).
6405         final List<Class<?>> iterationVariableTypes = new ArrayList<>();
6406         for (int i = 0; i < nclauses; ++i) {
6407             MethodHandle in = init.get(i);
6408             MethodHandle st = step.get(i);
6409             if (in == null && st == null) {
6410                 iterationVariableTypes.add(void.class);
6411             } else if (in != null && st != null) {
6412                 loopChecks1a(i, in, st);
6413                 iterationVariableTypes.add(in.type().returnType());
6414             } else {
6415                 iterationVariableTypes.add(in == null ? st.type().returnType() : in.type().returnType());
6416             }
6417         }
6418         final List<Class<?>> commonPrefix = iterationVariableTypes.stream().filter(t -> t != void.class).
6419                 collect(Collectors.toList());
6420 
6421         // Step 1B: determine loop parameters (A...).
6422         final List<Class<?>> commonSuffix = buildCommonSuffix(init, step, pred, fini, commonPrefix.size());
6423         loopChecks1b(init, commonSuffix);
6424 
6425         // Step 1C: determine loop return type.
6426         // Step 1D: check other types.
6427         // local variable required here; see JDK-8223553
6428         Stream<Class<?>> cstream = fini.stream().filter(Objects::nonNull).map(MethodHandle::type)
6429                 .map(MethodType::returnType);
6430         final Class<?> loopReturnType = cstream.findFirst().orElse(void.class);
6431         loopChecks1cd(pred, fini, loopReturnType);
6432 
6433         // Step 2: determine parameter lists.
6434         final List<Class<?>> commonParameterSequence = new ArrayList<>(commonPrefix);
6435         commonParameterSequence.addAll(commonSuffix);
6436         loopChecks2(step, pred, fini, commonParameterSequence);
6437 
6438         // Step 3: fill in omitted functions.
6439         for (int i = 0; i < nclauses; ++i) {
6440             Class<?> t = iterationVariableTypes.get(i);
6441             if (init.get(i) == null) {
6442                 init.set(i, empty(methodType(t, commonSuffix)));
6443             }
6444             if (step.get(i) == null) {
6445                 step.set(i, dropArgumentsToMatch(identityOrVoid(t), 0, commonParameterSequence, i));
6446             }
6447             if (pred.get(i) == null) {
6448                 pred.set(i, dropArguments0(constant(boolean.class, true), 0, commonParameterSequence));
6449             }
6450             if (fini.get(i) == null) {
6451                 fini.set(i, empty(methodType(t, commonParameterSequence)));
6452             }
6453         }
6454 
6455         // Step 4: fill in missing parameter types.
6456         // Also convert all handles to fixed-arity handles.
6457         List<MethodHandle> finit = fixArities(fillParameterTypes(init, commonSuffix));
6458         List<MethodHandle> fstep = fixArities(fillParameterTypes(step, commonParameterSequence));
6459         List<MethodHandle> fpred = fixArities(fillParameterTypes(pred, commonParameterSequence));
6460         List<MethodHandle> ffini = fixArities(fillParameterTypes(fini, commonParameterSequence));
6461 
6462         assert finit.stream().map(MethodHandle::type).map(MethodType::parameterList).
6463                 allMatch(pl -> pl.equals(commonSuffix));
6464         assert Stream.of(fstep, fpred, ffini).flatMap(List::stream).map(MethodHandle::type).map(MethodType::parameterList).
6465                 allMatch(pl -> pl.equals(commonParameterSequence));
6466 
6467         return MethodHandleImpl.makeLoop(loopReturnType, commonSuffix, finit, fstep, fpred, ffini);
6468     }
6469 
6470     private static void loopChecks0(MethodHandle[][] clauses) {
6471         if (clauses == null || clauses.length == 0) {
6472             throw newIllegalArgumentException("null or no clauses passed");
6473         }
6474         if (Stream.of(clauses).anyMatch(Objects::isNull)) {
6475             throw newIllegalArgumentException("null clauses are not allowed");
6476         }
6477         if (Stream.of(clauses).anyMatch(c -> c.length > 4)) {
6478             throw newIllegalArgumentException("All loop clauses must be represented as MethodHandle arrays with at most 4 elements.");
6479         }
6480     }
6481 
6482     private static void loopChecks1a(int i, MethodHandle in, MethodHandle st) {
6483         if (in.type().returnType() != st.type().returnType()) {
6484             throw misMatchedTypes("clause " + i + ": init and step return types", in.type().returnType(),
6485                     st.type().returnType());
6486         }
6487     }
6488 
6489     private static List<Class<?>> longestParameterList(Stream<MethodHandle> mhs, int skipSize) {
6490         final List<Class<?>> empty = List.of();
6491         final List<Class<?>> longest = mhs.filter(Objects::nonNull).
6492                 // take only those that can contribute to a common suffix because they are longer than the prefix
6493                         map(MethodHandle::type).
6494                         filter(t -> t.parameterCount() > skipSize).
6495                         map(MethodType::parameterList).
6496                         reduce((p, q) -> p.size() >= q.size() ? p : q).orElse(empty);
6497         return longest.size() == 0 ? empty : longest.subList(skipSize, longest.size());
6498     }
6499 
6500     private static List<Class<?>> longestParameterList(List<List<Class<?>>> lists) {
6501         final List<Class<?>> empty = List.of();
6502         return lists.stream().reduce((p, q) -> p.size() >= q.size() ? p : q).orElse(empty);
6503     }
6504 
6505     private static List<Class<?>> buildCommonSuffix(List<MethodHandle> init, List<MethodHandle> step, List<MethodHandle> pred, List<MethodHandle> fini, int cpSize) {
6506         final List<Class<?>> longest1 = longestParameterList(Stream.of(step, pred, fini).flatMap(List::stream), cpSize);
6507         final List<Class<?>> longest2 = longestParameterList(init.stream(), 0);
6508         return longestParameterList(Arrays.asList(longest1, longest2));
6509     }
6510 
6511     private static void loopChecks1b(List<MethodHandle> init, List<Class<?>> commonSuffix) {
6512         if (init.stream().filter(Objects::nonNull).map(MethodHandle::type).
6513                 anyMatch(t -> !t.effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, commonSuffix))) {
6514             throw newIllegalArgumentException("found non-effectively identical init parameter type lists: " + init +
6515                     " (common suffix: " + commonSuffix + ")");
6516         }
6517     }
6518 
6519     private static void loopChecks1cd(List<MethodHandle> pred, List<MethodHandle> fini, Class<?> loopReturnType) {
6520         if (fini.stream().filter(Objects::nonNull).map(MethodHandle::type).map(MethodType::returnType).
6521                 anyMatch(t -> t != loopReturnType)) {
6522             throw newIllegalArgumentException("found non-identical finalizer return types: " + fini + " (return type: " +
6523                     loopReturnType + ")");
6524         }
6525 
6526         if (!pred.stream().filter(Objects::nonNull).findFirst().isPresent()) {
6527             throw newIllegalArgumentException("no predicate found", pred);
6528         }
6529         if (pred.stream().filter(Objects::nonNull).map(MethodHandle::type).map(MethodType::returnType).
6530                 anyMatch(t -> t != boolean.class)) {
6531             throw newIllegalArgumentException("predicates must have boolean return type", pred);
6532         }
6533     }
6534 
6535     private static void loopChecks2(List<MethodHandle> step, List<MethodHandle> pred, List<MethodHandle> fini, List<Class<?>> commonParameterSequence) {
6536         if (Stream.of(step, pred, fini).flatMap(List::stream).filter(Objects::nonNull).map(MethodHandle::type).
6537                 anyMatch(t -> !t.effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, commonParameterSequence))) {
6538             throw newIllegalArgumentException("found non-effectively identical parameter type lists:\nstep: " + step +
6539                     "\npred: " + pred + "\nfini: " + fini + " (common parameter sequence: " + commonParameterSequence + ")");
6540         }
6541     }
6542 
6543     private static List<MethodHandle> fillParameterTypes(List<MethodHandle> hs, final List<Class<?>> targetParams) {
6544         return hs.stream().map(h -> {
6545             int pc = h.type().parameterCount();
6546             int tpsize = targetParams.size();
6547             return pc < tpsize ? dropArguments0(h, pc, targetParams.subList(pc, tpsize)) : h;
6548         }).collect(Collectors.toList());
6549     }
6550 
6551     private static List<MethodHandle> fixArities(List<MethodHandle> hs) {
6552         return hs.stream().map(MethodHandle::asFixedArity).collect(Collectors.toList());
6553     }
6554 
6555     /**
6556      * Constructs a {@code while} loop from an initializer, a body, and a predicate.
6557      * This is a convenience wrapper for the {@linkplain #loop(MethodHandle[][]) generic loop combinator}.
6558      * <p>
6559      * The {@code pred} handle describes the loop condition; and {@code body}, its body. The loop resulting from this
6560      * method will, in each iteration, first evaluate the predicate and then execute its body (if the predicate
6561      * evaluates to {@code true}).
6562      * The loop will terminate once the predicate evaluates to {@code false} (the body will not be executed in this case).
6563      * <p>
6564      * The {@code init} handle describes the initial value of an additional optional loop-local variable.
6565      * In each iteration, this loop-local variable, if present, will be passed to the {@code body}
6566      * and updated with the value returned from its invocation. The result of loop execution will be
6567      * the final value of the additional loop-local variable (if present).
6568      * <p>
6569      * The following rules hold for these argument handles:<ul>
6570      * <li>The {@code body} handle must not be {@code null}; its type must be of the form
6571      * {@code (V A...)V}, where {@code V} is non-{@code void}, or else {@code (A...)void}.
6572      * (In the {@code void} case, we assign the type {@code void} to the name {@code V},
6573      * and we will write {@code (V A...)V} with the understanding that a {@code void} type {@code V}
6574      * is quietly dropped from the parameter list, leaving {@code (A...)V}.)
6575      * <li>The parameter list {@code (V A...)} of the body is called the <em>internal parameter list</em>.
6576      * It will constrain the parameter lists of the other loop parts.
6577      * <li>If the iteration variable type {@code V} is dropped from the internal parameter list, the resulting shorter
6578      * list {@code (A...)} is called the <em>external parameter list</em>.
6579      * <li>The body return type {@code V}, if non-{@code void}, determines the type of an
6580      * additional state variable of the loop.
6581      * The body must both accept and return a value of this type {@code V}.
6582      * <li>If {@code init} is non-{@code null}, it must have return type {@code V}.
6583      * Its parameter list (of some <a href="MethodHandles.html#astar">form {@code (A*)}</a>) must be
6584      * <a href="MethodHandles.html#effid">effectively identical</a>
6585      * to the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
6586      * <li>If {@code init} is {@code null}, the loop variable will be initialized to its
6587      * {@linkplain #empty default value}.
6588      * <li>The {@code pred} handle must not be {@code null}.  It must have {@code boolean} as its return type.
6589      * Its parameter list (either empty or of the form {@code (V A*)}) must be
6590      * effectively identical to the internal parameter list.
6591      * </ul>
6592      * <p>
6593      * The resulting loop handle's result type and parameter signature are determined as follows:<ul>
6594      * <li>The loop handle's result type is the result type {@code V} of the body.
6595      * <li>The loop handle's parameter types are the types {@code (A...)},
6596      * from the external parameter list.
6597      * </ul>
6598      * <p>
6599      * Here is pseudocode for the resulting loop handle. In the code, {@code V}/{@code v} represent the type / value of
6600      * the sole loop variable as well as the result type of the loop; and {@code A}/{@code a}, that of the argument
6601      * passed to the loop.
6602      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6603      * V init(A...);
6604      * boolean pred(V, A...);
6605      * V body(V, A...);
6606      * V whileLoop(A... a...) {
6607      *   V v = init(a...);
6608      *   while (pred(v, a...)) {
6609      *     v = body(v, a...);
6610      *   }
6611      *   return v;
6612      * }
6613      * }</pre></blockquote>
6614      *
6615      * @apiNote Example:
6616      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6617      * // implement the zip function for lists as a loop handle
6618      * static List<String> initZip(Iterator<String> a, Iterator<String> b) { return new ArrayList<>(); }
6619      * static boolean zipPred(List<String> zip, Iterator<String> a, Iterator<String> b) { return a.hasNext() && b.hasNext(); }
6620      * static List<String> zipStep(List<String> zip, Iterator<String> a, Iterator<String> b) {
6621      *   zip.add(a.next());
6622      *   zip.add(b.next());
6623      *   return zip;
6624      * }
6625      * // assume MH_initZip, MH_zipPred, and MH_zipStep are handles to the above methods
6626      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.whileLoop(MH_initZip, MH_zipPred, MH_zipStep);
6627      * List<String> a = Arrays.asList("a", "b", "c", "d");
6628      * List<String> b = Arrays.asList("e", "f", "g", "h");
6629      * List<String> zipped = Arrays.asList("a", "e", "b", "f", "c", "g", "d", "h");
6630      * assertEquals(zipped, (List<String>) loop.invoke(a.iterator(), b.iterator()));
6631      * }</pre></blockquote>
6632      *
6633      *
6634      * @apiNote The implementation of this method can be expressed as follows:
6635      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6636      * MethodHandle whileLoop(MethodHandle init, MethodHandle pred, MethodHandle body) {
6637      *     MethodHandle fini = (body.type().returnType() == void.class
6638      *                         ? null : identity(body.type().returnType()));
6639      *     MethodHandle[]
6640      *         checkExit = { null, null, pred, fini },
6641      *         varBody   = { init, body };
6642      *     return loop(checkExit, varBody);
6643      * }
6644      * }</pre></blockquote>
6645      *
6646      * @param init optional initializer, providing the initial value of the loop variable.
6647      *             May be {@code null}, implying a default initial value.  See above for other constraints.
6648      * @param pred condition for the loop, which may not be {@code null}. Its result type must be {@code boolean}. See
6649      *             above for other constraints.
6650      * @param body body of the loop, which may not be {@code null}. It controls the loop parameters and result type.
6651      *             See above for other constraints.
6652      *
6653      * @return a method handle implementing the {@code while} loop as described by the arguments.
6654      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the rules for the arguments are violated.
6655      * @throws NullPointerException if {@code pred} or {@code body} are {@code null}.
6656      *
6657      * @see #loop(MethodHandle[][])
6658      * @see #doWhileLoop(MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
6659      * @since 9
6660      */
6661     public static MethodHandle whileLoop(MethodHandle init, MethodHandle pred, MethodHandle body) {
6662         whileLoopChecks(init, pred, body);
6663         MethodHandle fini = identityOrVoid(body.type().returnType());
6664         MethodHandle[] checkExit = { null, null, pred, fini };
6665         MethodHandle[] varBody = { init, body };
6666         return loop(checkExit, varBody);
6667     }
6668 
6669     /**
6670      * Constructs a {@code do-while} loop from an initializer, a body, and a predicate.
6671      * This is a convenience wrapper for the {@linkplain #loop(MethodHandle[][]) generic loop combinator}.
6672      * <p>
6673      * The {@code pred} handle describes the loop condition; and {@code body}, its body. The loop resulting from this
6674      * method will, in each iteration, first execute its body and then evaluate the predicate.
6675      * The loop will terminate once the predicate evaluates to {@code false} after an execution of the body.
6676      * <p>
6677      * The {@code init} handle describes the initial value of an additional optional loop-local variable.
6678      * In each iteration, this loop-local variable, if present, will be passed to the {@code body}
6679      * and updated with the value returned from its invocation. The result of loop execution will be
6680      * the final value of the additional loop-local variable (if present).
6681      * <p>
6682      * The following rules hold for these argument handles:<ul>
6683      * <li>The {@code body} handle must not be {@code null}; its type must be of the form
6684      * {@code (V A...)V}, where {@code V} is non-{@code void}, or else {@code (A...)void}.
6685      * (In the {@code void} case, we assign the type {@code void} to the name {@code V},
6686      * and we will write {@code (V A...)V} with the understanding that a {@code void} type {@code V}
6687      * is quietly dropped from the parameter list, leaving {@code (A...)V}.)
6688      * <li>The parameter list {@code (V A...)} of the body is called the <em>internal parameter list</em>.
6689      * It will constrain the parameter lists of the other loop parts.
6690      * <li>If the iteration variable type {@code V} is dropped from the internal parameter list, the resulting shorter
6691      * list {@code (A...)} is called the <em>external parameter list</em>.
6692      * <li>The body return type {@code V}, if non-{@code void}, determines the type of an
6693      * additional state variable of the loop.
6694      * The body must both accept and return a value of this type {@code V}.
6695      * <li>If {@code init} is non-{@code null}, it must have return type {@code V}.
6696      * Its parameter list (of some <a href="MethodHandles.html#astar">form {@code (A*)}</a>) must be
6697      * <a href="MethodHandles.html#effid">effectively identical</a>
6698      * to the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
6699      * <li>If {@code init} is {@code null}, the loop variable will be initialized to its
6700      * {@linkplain #empty default value}.
6701      * <li>The {@code pred} handle must not be {@code null}.  It must have {@code boolean} as its return type.
6702      * Its parameter list (either empty or of the form {@code (V A*)}) must be
6703      * effectively identical to the internal parameter list.
6704      * </ul>
6705      * <p>
6706      * The resulting loop handle's result type and parameter signature are determined as follows:<ul>
6707      * <li>The loop handle's result type is the result type {@code V} of the body.
6708      * <li>The loop handle's parameter types are the types {@code (A...)},
6709      * from the external parameter list.
6710      * </ul>
6711      * <p>
6712      * Here is pseudocode for the resulting loop handle. In the code, {@code V}/{@code v} represent the type / value of
6713      * the sole loop variable as well as the result type of the loop; and {@code A}/{@code a}, that of the argument
6714      * passed to the loop.
6715      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6716      * V init(A...);
6717      * boolean pred(V, A...);
6718      * V body(V, A...);
6719      * V doWhileLoop(A... a...) {
6720      *   V v = init(a...);
6721      *   do {
6722      *     v = body(v, a...);
6723      *   } while (pred(v, a...));
6724      *   return v;
6725      * }
6726      * }</pre></blockquote>
6727      *
6728      * @apiNote Example:
6729      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6730      * // int i = 0; while (i < limit) { ++i; } return i; => limit
6731      * static int zero(int limit) { return 0; }
6732      * static int step(int i, int limit) { return i + 1; }
6733      * static boolean pred(int i, int limit) { return i < limit; }
6734      * // assume MH_zero, MH_step, and MH_pred are handles to the above methods
6735      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.doWhileLoop(MH_zero, MH_step, MH_pred);
6736      * assertEquals(23, loop.invoke(23));
6737      * }</pre></blockquote>
6738      *
6739      *
6740      * @apiNote The implementation of this method can be expressed as follows:
6741      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6742      * MethodHandle doWhileLoop(MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body, MethodHandle pred) {
6743      *     MethodHandle fini = (body.type().returnType() == void.class
6744      *                         ? null : identity(body.type().returnType()));
6745      *     MethodHandle[] clause = { init, body, pred, fini };
6746      *     return loop(clause);
6747      * }
6748      * }</pre></blockquote>
6749      *
6750      * @param init optional initializer, providing the initial value of the loop variable.
6751      *             May be {@code null}, implying a default initial value.  See above for other constraints.
6752      * @param body body of the loop, which may not be {@code null}. It controls the loop parameters and result type.
6753      *             See above for other constraints.
6754      * @param pred condition for the loop, which may not be {@code null}. Its result type must be {@code boolean}. See
6755      *             above for other constraints.
6756      *
6757      * @return a method handle implementing the {@code while} loop as described by the arguments.
6758      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the rules for the arguments are violated.
6759      * @throws NullPointerException if {@code pred} or {@code body} are {@code null}.
6760      *
6761      * @see #loop(MethodHandle[][])
6762      * @see #whileLoop(MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
6763      * @since 9
6764      */
6765     public static MethodHandle doWhileLoop(MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body, MethodHandle pred) {
6766         whileLoopChecks(init, pred, body);
6767         MethodHandle fini = identityOrVoid(body.type().returnType());
6768         MethodHandle[] clause = {init, body, pred, fini };
6769         return loop(clause);
6770     }
6771 
6772     private static void whileLoopChecks(MethodHandle init, MethodHandle pred, MethodHandle body) {
6773         Objects.requireNonNull(pred);
6774         Objects.requireNonNull(body);
6775         MethodType bodyType = body.type();
6776         Class<?> returnType = bodyType.returnType();
6777         List<Class<?>> innerList = bodyType.parameterList();
6778         List<Class<?>> outerList = innerList;
6779         if (returnType == void.class) {
6780             // OK
6781         } else if (innerList.size() == 0 || innerList.get(0) != returnType) {
6782             // leading V argument missing => error
6783             MethodType expected = bodyType.insertParameterTypes(0, returnType);
6784             throw misMatchedTypes("body function", bodyType, expected);
6785         } else {
6786             outerList = innerList.subList(1, innerList.size());
6787         }
6788         MethodType predType = pred.type();
6789         if (predType.returnType() != boolean.class ||
6790                 !predType.effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, innerList)) {
6791             throw misMatchedTypes("loop predicate", predType, methodType(boolean.class, innerList));
6792         }
6793         if (init != null) {
6794             MethodType initType = init.type();
6795             if (initType.returnType() != returnType ||
6796                     !initType.effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, outerList)) {
6797                 throw misMatchedTypes("loop initializer", initType, methodType(returnType, outerList));
6798             }
6799         }
6800     }
6801 
6802     /**
6803      * Constructs a loop that runs a given number of iterations.
6804      * This is a convenience wrapper for the {@linkplain #loop(MethodHandle[][]) generic loop combinator}.
6805      * <p>
6806      * The number of iterations is determined by the {@code iterations} handle evaluation result.
6807      * The loop counter {@code i} is an extra loop iteration variable of type {@code int}.
6808      * It will be initialized to 0 and incremented by 1 in each iteration.
6809      * <p>
6810      * If the {@code body} handle returns a non-{@code void} type {@code V}, a leading loop iteration variable
6811      * of that type is also present.  This variable is initialized using the optional {@code init} handle,
6812      * or to the {@linkplain #empty default value} of type {@code V} if that handle is {@code null}.
6813      * <p>
6814      * In each iteration, the iteration variables are passed to an invocation of the {@code body} handle.
6815      * A non-{@code void} value returned from the body (of type {@code V}) updates the leading
6816      * iteration variable.
6817      * The result of the loop handle execution will be the final {@code V} value of that variable
6818      * (or {@code void} if there is no {@code V} variable).
6819      * <p>
6820      * The following rules hold for the argument handles:<ul>
6821      * <li>The {@code iterations} handle must not be {@code null}, and must return
6822      * the type {@code int}, referred to here as {@code I} in parameter type lists.
6823      * <li>The {@code body} handle must not be {@code null}; its type must be of the form
6824      * {@code (V I A...)V}, where {@code V} is non-{@code void}, or else {@code (I A...)void}.
6825      * (In the {@code void} case, we assign the type {@code void} to the name {@code V},
6826      * and we will write {@code (V I A...)V} with the understanding that a {@code void} type {@code V}
6827      * is quietly dropped from the parameter list, leaving {@code (I A...)V}.)
6828      * <li>The parameter list {@code (V I A...)} of the body contributes to a list
6829      * of types called the <em>internal parameter list</em>.
6830      * It will constrain the parameter lists of the other loop parts.
6831      * <li>As a special case, if the body contributes only {@code V} and {@code I} types,
6832      * with no additional {@code A} types, then the internal parameter list is extended by
6833      * the argument types {@code A...} of the {@code iterations} handle.
6834      * <li>If the iteration variable types {@code (V I)} are dropped from the internal parameter list, the resulting shorter
6835      * list {@code (A...)} is called the <em>external parameter list</em>.
6836      * <li>The body return type {@code V}, if non-{@code void}, determines the type of an
6837      * additional state variable of the loop.
6838      * The body must both accept a leading parameter and return a value of this type {@code V}.
6839      * <li>If {@code init} is non-{@code null}, it must have return type {@code V}.
6840      * Its parameter list (of some <a href="MethodHandles.html#astar">form {@code (A*)}</a>) must be
6841      * <a href="MethodHandles.html#effid">effectively identical</a>
6842      * to the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
6843      * <li>If {@code init} is {@code null}, the loop variable will be initialized to its
6844      * {@linkplain #empty default value}.
6845      * <li>The parameter list of {@code iterations} (of some form {@code (A*)}) must be
6846      * effectively identical to the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
6847      * </ul>
6848      * <p>
6849      * The resulting loop handle's result type and parameter signature are determined as follows:<ul>
6850      * <li>The loop handle's result type is the result type {@code V} of the body.
6851      * <li>The loop handle's parameter types are the types {@code (A...)},
6852      * from the external parameter list.
6853      * </ul>
6854      * <p>
6855      * Here is pseudocode for the resulting loop handle. In the code, {@code V}/{@code v} represent the type / value of
6856      * the second loop variable as well as the result type of the loop; and {@code A...}/{@code a...} represent
6857      * arguments passed to the loop.
6858      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6859      * int iterations(A...);
6860      * V init(A...);
6861      * V body(V, int, A...);
6862      * V countedLoop(A... a...) {
6863      *   int end = iterations(a...);
6864      *   V v = init(a...);
6865      *   for (int i = 0; i < end; ++i) {
6866      *     v = body(v, i, a...);
6867      *   }
6868      *   return v;
6869      * }
6870      * }</pre></blockquote>
6871      *
6872      * @apiNote Example with a fully conformant body method:
6873      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6874      * // String s = "Lambdaman!"; for (int i = 0; i < 13; ++i) { s = "na " + s; } return s;
6875      * // => a variation on a well known theme
6876      * static String step(String v, int counter, String init) { return "na " + v; }
6877      * // assume MH_step is a handle to the method above
6878      * MethodHandle fit13 = MethodHandles.constant(int.class, 13);
6879      * MethodHandle start = MethodHandles.identity(String.class);
6880      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.countedLoop(fit13, start, MH_step);
6881      * assertEquals("na na na na na na na na na na na na na Lambdaman!", loop.invoke("Lambdaman!"));
6882      * }</pre></blockquote>
6883      *
6884      * @apiNote Example with the simplest possible body method type,
6885      * and passing the number of iterations to the loop invocation:
6886      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6887      * // String s = "Lambdaman!"; for (int i = 0; i < 13; ++i) { s = "na " + s; } return s;
6888      * // => a variation on a well known theme
6889      * static String step(String v, int counter ) { return "na " + v; }
6890      * // assume MH_step is a handle to the method above
6891      * MethodHandle count = MethodHandles.dropArguments(MethodHandles.identity(int.class), 1, String.class);
6892      * MethodHandle start = MethodHandles.dropArguments(MethodHandles.identity(String.class), 0, int.class);
6893      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.countedLoop(count, start, MH_step);  // (v, i) -> "na " + v
6894      * assertEquals("na na na na na na na na na na na na na Lambdaman!", loop.invoke(13, "Lambdaman!"));
6895      * }</pre></blockquote>
6896      *
6897      * @apiNote Example that treats the number of iterations, string to append to, and string to append
6898      * as loop parameters:
6899      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6900      * // String s = "Lambdaman!", t = "na"; for (int i = 0; i < 13; ++i) { s = t + " " + s; } return s;
6901      * // => a variation on a well known theme
6902      * static String step(String v, int counter, int iterations_, String pre, String start_) { return pre + " " + v; }
6903      * // assume MH_step is a handle to the method above
6904      * MethodHandle count = MethodHandles.identity(int.class);
6905      * MethodHandle start = MethodHandles.dropArguments(MethodHandles.identity(String.class), 0, int.class, String.class);
6906      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.countedLoop(count, start, MH_step);  // (v, i, _, pre, _) -> pre + " " + v
6907      * assertEquals("na na na na na na na na na na na na na Lambdaman!", loop.invoke(13, "na", "Lambdaman!"));
6908      * }</pre></blockquote>
6909      *
6910      * @apiNote Example that illustrates the usage of {@link #dropArgumentsToMatch(MethodHandle, int, List, int)}
6911      * to enforce a loop type:
6912      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6913      * // String s = "Lambdaman!", t = "na"; for (int i = 0; i < 13; ++i) { s = t + " " + s; } return s;
6914      * // => a variation on a well known theme
6915      * static String step(String v, int counter, String pre) { return pre + " " + v; }
6916      * // assume MH_step is a handle to the method above
6917      * MethodType loopType = methodType(String.class, String.class, int.class, String.class);
6918      * MethodHandle count = MethodHandles.dropArgumentsToMatch(MethodHandles.identity(int.class),    0, loopType.parameterList(), 1);
6919      * MethodHandle start = MethodHandles.dropArgumentsToMatch(MethodHandles.identity(String.class), 0, loopType.parameterList(), 2);
6920      * MethodHandle body  = MethodHandles.dropArgumentsToMatch(MH_step,                              2, loopType.parameterList(), 0);
6921      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.countedLoop(count, start, body);  // (v, i, pre, _, _) -> pre + " " + v
6922      * assertEquals("na na na na na na na na na na na na na Lambdaman!", loop.invoke("na", 13, "Lambdaman!"));
6923      * }</pre></blockquote>
6924      *
6925      * @apiNote The implementation of this method can be expressed as follows:
6926      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6927      * MethodHandle countedLoop(MethodHandle iterations, MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body) {
6928      *     return countedLoop(empty(iterations.type()), iterations, init, body);
6929      * }
6930      * }</pre></blockquote>
6931      *
6932      * @param iterations a non-{@code null} handle to return the number of iterations this loop should run. The handle's
6933      *                   result type must be {@code int}. See above for other constraints.
6934      * @param init optional initializer, providing the initial value of the loop variable.
6935      *             May be {@code null}, implying a default initial value.  See above for other constraints.
6936      * @param body body of the loop, which may not be {@code null}.
6937      *             It controls the loop parameters and result type in the standard case (see above for details).
6938      *             It must accept its own return type (if non-void) plus an {@code int} parameter (for the counter),
6939      *             and may accept any number of additional types.
6940      *             See above for other constraints.
6941      *
6942      * @return a method handle representing the loop.
6943      * @throws NullPointerException if either of the {@code iterations} or {@code body} handles is {@code null}.
6944      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if any argument violates the rules formulated above.
6945      *
6946      * @see #countedLoop(MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
6947      * @since 9
6948      */
6949     public static MethodHandle countedLoop(MethodHandle iterations, MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body) {
6950         return countedLoop(empty(iterations.type()), iterations, init, body);
6951     }
6952 
6953     /**
6954      * Constructs a loop that counts over a range of numbers.
6955      * This is a convenience wrapper for the {@linkplain #loop(MethodHandle[][]) generic loop combinator}.
6956      * <p>
6957      * The loop counter {@code i} is a loop iteration variable of type {@code int}.
6958      * The {@code start} and {@code end} handles determine the start (inclusive) and end (exclusive)
6959      * values of the loop counter.
6960      * The loop counter will be initialized to the {@code int} value returned from the evaluation of the
6961      * {@code start} handle and run to the value returned from {@code end} (exclusively) with a step width of 1.
6962      * <p>
6963      * If the {@code body} handle returns a non-{@code void} type {@code V}, a leading loop iteration variable
6964      * of that type is also present.  This variable is initialized using the optional {@code init} handle,
6965      * or to the {@linkplain #empty default value} of type {@code V} if that handle is {@code null}.
6966      * <p>
6967      * In each iteration, the iteration variables are passed to an invocation of the {@code body} handle.
6968      * A non-{@code void} value returned from the body (of type {@code V}) updates the leading
6969      * iteration variable.
6970      * The result of the loop handle execution will be the final {@code V} value of that variable
6971      * (or {@code void} if there is no {@code V} variable).
6972      * <p>
6973      * The following rules hold for the argument handles:<ul>
6974      * <li>The {@code start} and {@code end} handles must not be {@code null}, and must both return
6975      * the common type {@code int}, referred to here as {@code I} in parameter type lists.
6976      * <li>The {@code body} handle must not be {@code null}; its type must be of the form
6977      * {@code (V I A...)V}, where {@code V} is non-{@code void}, or else {@code (I A...)void}.
6978      * (In the {@code void} case, we assign the type {@code void} to the name {@code V},
6979      * and we will write {@code (V I A...)V} with the understanding that a {@code void} type {@code V}
6980      * is quietly dropped from the parameter list, leaving {@code (I A...)V}.)
6981      * <li>The parameter list {@code (V I A...)} of the body contributes to a list
6982      * of types called the <em>internal parameter list</em>.
6983      * It will constrain the parameter lists of the other loop parts.
6984      * <li>As a special case, if the body contributes only {@code V} and {@code I} types,
6985      * with no additional {@code A} types, then the internal parameter list is extended by
6986      * the argument types {@code A...} of the {@code end} handle.
6987      * <li>If the iteration variable types {@code (V I)} are dropped from the internal parameter list, the resulting shorter
6988      * list {@code (A...)} is called the <em>external parameter list</em>.
6989      * <li>The body return type {@code V}, if non-{@code void}, determines the type of an
6990      * additional state variable of the loop.
6991      * The body must both accept a leading parameter and return a value of this type {@code V}.
6992      * <li>If {@code init} is non-{@code null}, it must have return type {@code V}.
6993      * Its parameter list (of some <a href="MethodHandles.html#astar">form {@code (A*)}</a>) must be
6994      * <a href="MethodHandles.html#effid">effectively identical</a>
6995      * to the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
6996      * <li>If {@code init} is {@code null}, the loop variable will be initialized to its
6997      * {@linkplain #empty default value}.
6998      * <li>The parameter list of {@code start} (of some form {@code (A*)}) must be
6999      * effectively identical to the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
7000      * <li>Likewise, the parameter list of {@code end} must be effectively identical
7001      * to the external parameter list.
7002      * </ul>
7003      * <p>
7004      * The resulting loop handle's result type and parameter signature are determined as follows:<ul>
7005      * <li>The loop handle's result type is the result type {@code V} of the body.
7006      * <li>The loop handle's parameter types are the types {@code (A...)},
7007      * from the external parameter list.
7008      * </ul>
7009      * <p>
7010      * Here is pseudocode for the resulting loop handle. In the code, {@code V}/{@code v} represent the type / value of
7011      * the second loop variable as well as the result type of the loop; and {@code A...}/{@code a...} represent
7012      * arguments passed to the loop.
7013      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
7014      * int start(A...);
7015      * int end(A...);
7016      * V init(A...);
7017      * V body(V, int, A...);
7018      * V countedLoop(A... a...) {
7019      *   int e = end(a...);
7020      *   int s = start(a...);
7021      *   V v = init(a...);
7022      *   for (int i = s; i < e; ++i) {
7023      *     v = body(v, i, a...);
7024      *   }
7025      *   return v;
7026      * }
7027      * }</pre></blockquote>
7028      *
7029      * @apiNote The implementation of this method can be expressed as follows:
7030      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
7031      * MethodHandle countedLoop(MethodHandle start, MethodHandle end, MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body) {
7032      *     MethodHandle returnVar = dropArguments(identity(init.type().returnType()), 0, int.class, int.class);
7033      *     // assume MH_increment and MH_predicate are handles to implementation-internal methods with
7034      *     // the following semantics:
7035      *     // MH_increment: (int limit, int counter) -> counter + 1
7036      *     // MH_predicate: (int limit, int counter) -> counter < limit
7037      *     Class<?> counterType = start.type().returnType();  // int
7038      *     Class<?> returnType = body.type().returnType();
7039      *     MethodHandle incr = MH_increment, pred = MH_predicate, retv = null;
7040      *     if (returnType != void.class) {  // ignore the V variable
7041      *         incr = dropArguments(incr, 1, returnType);  // (limit, v, i) => (limit, i)
7042      *         pred = dropArguments(pred, 1, returnType);  // ditto
7043      *         retv = dropArguments(identity(returnType), 0, counterType); // ignore limit
7044      *     }
7045      *     body = dropArguments(body, 0, counterType);  // ignore the limit variable
7046      *     MethodHandle[]
7047      *         loopLimit  = { end, null, pred, retv }, // limit = end(); i < limit || return v
7048      *         bodyClause = { init, body },            // v = init(); v = body(v, i)
7049      *         indexVar   = { start, incr };           // i = start(); i = i + 1
7050      *     return loop(loopLimit, bodyClause, indexVar);
7051      * }
7052      * }</pre></blockquote>
7053      *
7054      * @param start a non-{@code null} handle to return the start value of the loop counter, which must be {@code int}.
7055      *              See above for other constraints.
7056      * @param end a non-{@code null} handle to return the end value of the loop counter (the loop will run to
7057      *            {@code end-1}). The result type must be {@code int}. See above for other constraints.
7058      * @param init optional initializer, providing the initial value of the loop variable.
7059      *             May be {@code null}, implying a default initial value.  See above for other constraints.
7060      * @param body body of the loop, which may not be {@code null}.
7061      *             It controls the loop parameters and result type in the standard case (see above for details).
7062      *             It must accept its own return type (if non-void) plus an {@code int} parameter (for the counter),
7063      *             and may accept any number of additional types.
7064      *             See above for other constraints.
7065      *
7066      * @return a method handle representing the loop.
7067      * @throws NullPointerException if any of the {@code start}, {@code end}, or {@code body} handles is {@code null}.
7068      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if any argument violates the rules formulated above.
7069      *
7070      * @see #countedLoop(MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
7071      * @since 9
7072      */
7073     public static MethodHandle countedLoop(MethodHandle start, MethodHandle end, MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body) {
7074         countedLoopChecks(start, end, init, body);
7075         Class<?> counterType = start.type().returnType();  // int, but who's counting?
7076         Class<?> limitType   = end.type().returnType();    // yes, int again
7077         Class<?> returnType  = body.type().returnType();
7078         MethodHandle incr = MethodHandleImpl.getConstantHandle(MethodHandleImpl.MH_countedLoopStep);
7079         MethodHandle pred = MethodHandleImpl.getConstantHandle(MethodHandleImpl.MH_countedLoopPred);
7080         MethodHandle retv = null;
7081         if (returnType != void.class) {
7082             incr = dropArguments(incr, 1, returnType);  // (limit, v, i) => (limit, i)
7083             pred = dropArguments(pred, 1, returnType);  // ditto
7084             retv = dropArguments(identity(returnType), 0, counterType);
7085         }
7086         body = dropArguments(body, 0, counterType);  // ignore the limit variable
7087         MethodHandle[]
7088             loopLimit  = { end, null, pred, retv }, // limit = end(); i < limit || return v
7089             bodyClause = { init, body },            // v = init(); v = body(v, i)
7090             indexVar   = { start, incr };           // i = start(); i = i + 1
7091         return loop(loopLimit, bodyClause, indexVar);
7092     }
7093 
7094     private static void countedLoopChecks(MethodHandle start, MethodHandle end, MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body) {
7095         Objects.requireNonNull(start);
7096         Objects.requireNonNull(end);
7097         Objects.requireNonNull(body);
7098         Class<?> counterType = start.type().returnType();
7099         if (counterType != int.class) {
7100             MethodType expected = start.type().changeReturnType(int.class);
7101             throw misMatchedTypes("start function", start.type(), expected);
7102         } else if (end.type().returnType() != counterType) {
7103             MethodType expected = end.type().changeReturnType(counterType);
7104             throw misMatchedTypes("end function", end.type(), expected);
7105         }
7106         MethodType bodyType = body.type();
7107         Class<?> returnType = bodyType.returnType();
7108         List<Class<?>> innerList = bodyType.parameterList();
7109         // strip leading V value if present
7110         int vsize = (returnType == void.class ? 0 : 1);
7111         if (vsize != 0 && (innerList.size() == 0 || innerList.get(0) != returnType)) {
7112             // argument list has no "V" => error
7113             MethodType expected = bodyType.insertParameterTypes(0, returnType);
7114             throw misMatchedTypes("body function", bodyType, expected);
7115         } else if (innerList.size() <= vsize || innerList.get(vsize) != counterType) {
7116             // missing I type => error
7117             MethodType expected = bodyType.insertParameterTypes(vsize, counterType);
7118             throw misMatchedTypes("body function", bodyType, expected);
7119         }
7120         List<Class<?>> outerList = innerList.subList(vsize + 1, innerList.size());
7121         if (outerList.isEmpty()) {
7122             // special case; take lists from end handle
7123             outerList = end.type().parameterList();
7124             innerList = bodyType.insertParameterTypes(vsize + 1, outerList).parameterList();
7125         }
7126         MethodType expected = methodType(counterType, outerList);
7127         if (!start.type().effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, outerList)) {
7128             throw misMatchedTypes("start parameter types", start.type(), expected);
7129         }
7130         if (end.type() != start.type() &&
7131             !end.type().effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, outerList)) {
7132             throw misMatchedTypes("end parameter types", end.type(), expected);
7133         }
7134         if (init != null) {
7135             MethodType initType = init.type();
7136             if (initType.returnType() != returnType ||
7137                 !initType.effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, outerList)) {
7138                 throw misMatchedTypes("loop initializer", initType, methodType(returnType, outerList));
7139             }
7140         }
7141     }
7142 
7143     /**
7144      * Constructs a loop that ranges over the values produced by an {@code Iterator<T>}.
7145      * This is a convenience wrapper for the {@linkplain #loop(MethodHandle[][]) generic loop combinator}.
7146      * <p>
7147      * The iterator itself will be determined by the evaluation of the {@code iterator} handle.
7148      * Each value it produces will be stored in a loop iteration variable of type {@code T}.
7149      * <p>
7150      * If the {@code body} handle returns a non-{@code void} type {@code V}, a leading loop iteration variable
7151      * of that type is also present.  This variable is initialized using the optional {@code init} handle,
7152      * or to the {@linkplain #empty default value} of type {@code V} if that handle is {@code null}.
7153      * <p>
7154      * In each iteration, the iteration variables are passed to an invocation of the {@code body} handle.
7155      * A non-{@code void} value returned from the body (of type {@code V}) updates the leading
7156      * iteration variable.
7157      * The result of the loop handle execution will be the final {@code V} value of that variable
7158      * (or {@code void} if there is no {@code V} variable).
7159      * <p>
7160      * The following rules hold for the argument handles:<ul>
7161      * <li>The {@code body} handle must not be {@code null}; its type must be of the form
7162      * {@code (V T A...)V}, where {@code V} is non-{@code void}, or else {@code (T A...)void}.
7163      * (In the {@code void} case, we assign the type {@code void} to the name {@code V},
7164      * and we will write {@code (V T A...)V} with the understanding that a {@code void} type {@code V}
7165      * is quietly dropped from the parameter list, leaving {@code (T A...)V}.)
7166      * <li>The parameter list {@code (V T A...)} of the body contributes to a list
7167      * of types called the <em>internal parameter list</em>.
7168      * It will constrain the parameter lists of the other loop parts.
7169      * <li>As a special case, if the body contributes only {@code V} and {@code T} types,
7170      * with no additional {@code A} types, then the internal parameter list is extended by
7171      * the argument types {@code A...} of the {@code iterator} handle; if it is {@code null} the
7172      * single type {@code Iterable} is added and constitutes the {@code A...} list.
7173      * <li>If the iteration variable types {@code (V T)} are dropped from the internal parameter list, the resulting shorter
7174      * list {@code (A...)} is called the <em>external parameter list</em>.
7175      * <li>The body return type {@code V}, if non-{@code void}, determines the type of an
7176      * additional state variable of the loop.
7177      * The body must both accept a leading parameter and return a value of this type {@code V}.
7178      * <li>If {@code init} is non-{@code null}, it must have return type {@code V}.
7179      * Its parameter list (of some <a href="MethodHandles.html#astar">form {@code (A*)}</a>) must be
7180      * <a href="MethodHandles.html#effid">effectively identical</a>
7181      * to the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
7182      * <li>If {@code init} is {@code null}, the loop variable will be initialized to its
7183      * {@linkplain #empty default value}.
7184      * <li>If the {@code iterator} handle is non-{@code null}, it must have the return
7185      * type {@code java.util.Iterator} or a subtype thereof.
7186      * The iterator it produces when the loop is executed will be assumed
7187      * to yield values which can be converted to type {@code T}.
7188      * <li>The parameter list of an {@code iterator} that is non-{@code null} (of some form {@code (A*)}) must be
7189      * effectively identical to the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
7190      * <li>If {@code iterator} is {@code null} it defaults to a method handle which behaves
7191      * like {@link java.lang.Iterable#iterator()}.  In that case, the internal parameter list
7192      * {@code (V T A...)} must have at least one {@code A} type, and the default iterator
7193      * handle parameter is adjusted to accept the leading {@code A} type, as if by
7194      * the {@link MethodHandle#asType asType} conversion method.
7195      * The leading {@code A} type must be {@code Iterable} or a subtype thereof.
7196      * This conversion step, done at loop construction time, must not throw a {@code WrongMethodTypeException}.
7197      * </ul>
7198      * <p>
7199      * The type {@code T} may be either a primitive or reference.
7200      * Since type {@code Iterator<T>} is erased in the method handle representation to the raw type {@code Iterator},
7201      * the {@code iteratedLoop} combinator adjusts the leading argument type for {@code body} to {@code Object}
7202      * as if by the {@link MethodHandle#asType asType} conversion method.
7203      * Therefore, if an iterator of the wrong type appears as the loop is executed, runtime exceptions may occur
7204      * as the result of dynamic conversions performed by {@link MethodHandle#asType(MethodType)}.
7205      * <p>
7206      * The resulting loop handle's result type and parameter signature are determined as follows:<ul>
7207      * <li>The loop handle's result type is the result type {@code V} of the body.
7208      * <li>The loop handle's parameter types are the types {@code (A...)},
7209      * from the external parameter list.
7210      * </ul>
7211      * <p>
7212      * Here is pseudocode for the resulting loop handle. In the code, {@code V}/{@code v} represent the type / value of
7213      * the loop variable as well as the result type of the loop; {@code T}/{@code t}, that of the elements of the
7214      * structure the loop iterates over, and {@code A...}/{@code a...} represent arguments passed to the loop.
7215      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
7216      * Iterator<T> iterator(A...);  // defaults to Iterable::iterator
7217      * V init(A...);
7218      * V body(V,T,A...);
7219      * V iteratedLoop(A... a...) {
7220      *   Iterator<T> it = iterator(a...);
7221      *   V v = init(a...);
7222      *   while (it.hasNext()) {
7223      *     T t = it.next();
7224      *     v = body(v, t, a...);
7225      *   }
7226      *   return v;
7227      * }
7228      * }</pre></blockquote>
7229      *
7230      * @apiNote Example:
7231      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
7232      * // get an iterator from a list
7233      * static List<String> reverseStep(List<String> r, String e) {
7234      *   r.add(0, e);
7235      *   return r;
7236      * }
7237      * static List<String> newArrayList() { return new ArrayList<>(); }
7238      * // assume MH_reverseStep and MH_newArrayList are handles to the above methods
7239      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.iteratedLoop(null, MH_newArrayList, MH_reverseStep);
7240      * List<String> list = Arrays.asList("a", "b", "c", "d", "e");
7241      * List<String> reversedList = Arrays.asList("e", "d", "c", "b", "a");
7242      * assertEquals(reversedList, (List<String>) loop.invoke(list));
7243      * }</pre></blockquote>
7244      *
7245      * @apiNote The implementation of this method can be expressed approximately as follows:
7246      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
7247      * MethodHandle iteratedLoop(MethodHandle iterator, MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body) {
7248      *     // assume MH_next, MH_hasNext, MH_startIter are handles to methods of Iterator/Iterable
7249      *     Class<?> returnType = body.type().returnType();
7250      *     Class<?> ttype = body.type().parameterType(returnType == void.class ? 0 : 1);
7251      *     MethodHandle nextVal = MH_next.asType(MH_next.type().changeReturnType(ttype));
7252      *     MethodHandle retv = null, step = body, startIter = iterator;
7253      *     if (returnType != void.class) {
7254      *         // the simple thing first:  in (I V A...), drop the I to get V
7255      *         retv = dropArguments(identity(returnType), 0, Iterator.class);
7256      *         // body type signature (V T A...), internal loop types (I V A...)
7257      *         step = swapArguments(body, 0, 1);  // swap V <-> T
7258      *     }
7259      *     if (startIter == null)  startIter = MH_getIter;
7260      *     MethodHandle[]
7261      *         iterVar    = { startIter, null, MH_hasNext, retv }, // it = iterator; while (it.hasNext())
7262      *         bodyClause = { init, filterArguments(step, 0, nextVal) };  // v = body(v, t, a)
7263      *     return loop(iterVar, bodyClause);
7264      * }
7265      * }</pre></blockquote>
7266      *
7267      * @param iterator an optional handle to return the iterator to start the loop.
7268      *                 If non-{@code null}, the handle must return {@link java.util.Iterator} or a subtype.
7269      *                 See above for other constraints.
7270      * @param init optional initializer, providing the initial value of the loop variable.
7271      *             May be {@code null}, implying a default initial value.  See above for other constraints.
7272      * @param body body of the loop, which may not be {@code null}.
7273      *             It controls the loop parameters and result type in the standard case (see above for details).
7274      *             It must accept its own return type (if non-void) plus a {@code T} parameter (for the iterated values),
7275      *             and may accept any number of additional types.
7276      *             See above for other constraints.
7277      *
7278      * @return a method handle embodying the iteration loop functionality.
7279      * @throws NullPointerException if the {@code body} handle is {@code null}.
7280      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if any argument violates the above requirements.
7281      *
7282      * @since 9
7283      */
7284     public static MethodHandle iteratedLoop(MethodHandle iterator, MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body) {
7285         Class<?> iterableType = iteratedLoopChecks(iterator, init, body);
7286         Class<?> returnType = body.type().returnType();
7287         MethodHandle hasNext = MethodHandleImpl.getConstantHandle(MethodHandleImpl.MH_iteratePred);
7288         MethodHandle nextRaw = MethodHandleImpl.getConstantHandle(MethodHandleImpl.MH_iterateNext);
7289         MethodHandle startIter;
7290         MethodHandle nextVal;
7291         {
7292             MethodType iteratorType;
7293             if (iterator == null) {
7294                 // derive argument type from body, if available, else use Iterable
