7295                 startIter = MethodHandleImpl.getConstantHandle(MethodHandleImpl.MH_initIterator);
7296                 iteratorType = startIter.type().changeParameterType(0, iterableType);
7297             } else {
7298                 // force return type to the internal iterator class
7299                 iteratorType = iterator.type().changeReturnType(Iterator.class);
7300                 startIter = iterator;
7301             }
7302             Class<?> ttype = body.type().parameterType(returnType == void.class ? 0 : 1);
7303             MethodType nextValType = nextRaw.type().changeReturnType(ttype);
7304 
7305             // perform the asType transforms under an exception transformer, as per spec.:
7306             try {
7307                 startIter = startIter.asType(iteratorType);
7308                 nextVal = nextRaw.asType(nextValType);
7309             } catch (WrongMethodTypeException ex) {
7310                 throw new IllegalArgumentException(ex);
7311             }
7312         }
7313 
7314         MethodHandle retv = null, step = body;
7315         if (returnType != void.class) {
7316             // the simple thing first:  in (I V A...), drop the I to get V
7317             retv = dropArguments(identity(returnType), 0, Iterator.class);
7318             // body type signature (V T A...), internal loop types (I V A...)
7319             step = swapArguments(body, 0, 1);  // swap V <-> T
7320         }
7321 
7322         MethodHandle[]
7323             iterVar    = { startIter, null, hasNext, retv },
7324             bodyClause = { init, filterArgument(step, 0, nextVal) };
7325         return loop(iterVar, bodyClause);
7326     }
7327 
7328     private static Class<?> iteratedLoopChecks(MethodHandle iterator, MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body) {
7329         Objects.requireNonNull(body);
7330         MethodType bodyType = body.type();
7331         Class<?> returnType = bodyType.returnType();
7332         List<Class<?>> internalParamList = bodyType.parameterList();
7333         // strip leading V value if present
7334         int vsize = (returnType == void.class ? 0 : 1);
7335         if (vsize != 0 && (internalParamList.size() == 0 || internalParamList.get(0) != returnType)) {
7336             // argument list has no "V" => error
7337             MethodType expected = bodyType.insertParameterTypes(0, returnType);
7338             throw misMatchedTypes("body function", bodyType, expected);
7339         } else if (internalParamList.size() <= vsize) {
7340             // missing T type => error
7341             MethodType expected = bodyType.insertParameterTypes(vsize, Object.class);
7342             throw misMatchedTypes("body function", bodyType, expected);
7343         }
7344         List<Class<?>> externalParamList = internalParamList.subList(vsize + 1, internalParamList.size());
7345         Class<?> iterableType = null;
7346         if (iterator != null) {
7347             // special case; if the body handle only declares V and T then
7348             // the external parameter list is obtained from iterator handle
7349             if (externalParamList.isEmpty()) {
7350                 externalParamList = iterator.type().parameterList();
7351             }
7352             MethodType itype = iterator.type();
7353             if (!Iterator.class.isAssignableFrom(itype.returnType())) {
7354                 throw newIllegalArgumentException("iteratedLoop first argument must have Iterator return type");
7355             }
7356             if (!itype.effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, externalParamList)) {
7357                 MethodType expected = methodType(itype.returnType(), externalParamList);
7358                 throw misMatchedTypes("iterator parameters", itype, expected);
7359             }
7360         } else {
7361             if (externalParamList.isEmpty()) {
7362                 // special case; if the iterator handle is null and the body handle
7363                 // only declares V and T then the external parameter list consists
7364                 // of Iterable
7365                 externalParamList = Arrays.asList(Iterable.class);
7366                 iterableType = Iterable.class;
7367             } else {
7368                 // special case; if the iterator handle is null and the external
7369                 // parameter list is not empty then the first parameter must be
7370                 // assignable to Iterable
7371                 iterableType = externalParamList.get(0);
7372                 if (!Iterable.class.isAssignableFrom(iterableType)) {
7373                     throw newIllegalArgumentException(
7374                             "inferred first loop argument must inherit from Iterable: " + iterableType);
7375                 }
7376             }
7377         }
7378         if (init != null) {
7379             MethodType initType = init.type();
7380             if (initType.returnType() != returnType ||
7381                     !initType.effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, externalParamList)) {
7382                 throw misMatchedTypes("loop initializer", initType, methodType(returnType, externalParamList));
7383             }
7384         }
7385         return iterableType;  // help the caller a bit
7386     }
7387 
7388     /*non-public*/
7389     static MethodHandle swapArguments(MethodHandle mh, int i, int j) {
7390         // there should be a better way to uncross my wires
7391         int arity = mh.type().parameterCount();
7392         int[] order = new int[arity];
7393         for (int k = 0; k < arity; k++)  order[k] = k;
7394         order[i] = j; order[j] = i;
7395         Class<?>[] types = mh.type().parameterArray();
7396         Class<?> ti = types[i]; types[i] = types[j]; types[j] = ti;
7397         MethodType swapType = methodType(mh.type().returnType(), types);
7398         return permuteArguments(mh, swapType, order);
7399     }
7400 
7401     /**
7402      * Makes a method handle that adapts a {@code target} method handle by wrapping it in a {@code try-finally} block.
7403      * Another method handle, {@code cleanup}, represents the functionality of the {@code finally} block. Any exception
7404      * thrown during the execution of the {@code target} handle will be passed to the {@code cleanup} handle. The
7405      * exception will be rethrown, unless {@code cleanup} handle throws an exception first.  The
7406      * value returned from the {@code cleanup} handle's execution will be the result of the execution of the
7407      * {@code try-finally} handle.
7408      * <p>
7409      * The {@code cleanup} handle will be passed one or two additional leading arguments.
7410      * The first is the exception thrown during the
7411      * execution of the {@code target} handle, or {@code null} if no exception was thrown.
7412      * The second is the result of the execution of the {@code target} handle, or, if it throws an exception,
7413      * a {@code null}, zero, or {@code false} value of the required type is supplied as a placeholder.
7414      * The second argument is not present if the {@code target} handle has a {@code void} return type.
7415      * (Note that, except for argument type conversions, combinators represent {@code void} values in parameter lists
7416      * by omitting the corresponding paradoxical arguments, not by inserting {@code null} or zero values.)
7417      * <p>
7418      * The {@code target} and {@code cleanup} handles must have the same corresponding argument and return types, except
7419      * that the {@code cleanup} handle may omit trailing arguments. Also, the {@code cleanup} handle must have one or
7420      * two extra leading parameters:<ul>
7421      * <li>a {@code Throwable}, which will carry the exception thrown by the {@code target} handle (if any); and
7422      * <li>a parameter of the same type as the return type of both {@code target} and {@code cleanup}, which will carry
7423      * the result from the execution of the {@code target} handle.
7424      * This parameter is not present if the {@code target} returns {@code void}.
7425      * </ul>
7426      * <p>
7427      * The pseudocode for the resulting adapter looks as follows. In the code, {@code V} represents the result type of
7428      * the {@code try/finally} construct; {@code A}/{@code a}, the types and values of arguments to the resulting
7429      * handle consumed by the cleanup; and {@code B}/{@code b}, those of arguments to the resulting handle discarded by
7430      * the cleanup.
7431      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
7432      * V target(A..., B...);
7433      * V cleanup(Throwable, V, A...);
7434      * V adapter(A... a, B... b) {
7435      *   V result = (zero value for V);
7436      *   Throwable throwable = null;
7437      *   try {
7438      *     result = target(a..., b...);
7439      *   } catch (Throwable t) {
7440      *     throwable = t;
7441      *     throw t;
7442      *   } finally {
7443      *     result = cleanup(throwable, result, a...);
7444      *   }
7445      *   return result;
7446      * }
7447      * }</pre></blockquote>
7448      * <p>
7449      * Note that the saved arguments ({@code a...} in the pseudocode) cannot
7450      * be modified by execution of the target, and so are passed unchanged
7451      * from the caller to the cleanup, if it is invoked.
7452      * <p>
7453      * The target and cleanup must return the same type, even if the cleanup
7454      * always throws.
7455      * To create such a throwing cleanup, compose the cleanup logic
7456      * with {@link #throwException throwException},
7457      * in order to create a method handle of the correct return type.
7458      * <p>
7459      * Note that {@code tryFinally} never converts exceptions into normal returns.
7460      * In rare cases where exceptions must be converted in that way, first wrap
7461      * the target with {@link #catchException(MethodHandle, Class, MethodHandle)}
7462      * to capture an outgoing exception, and then wrap with {@code tryFinally}.
7463      * <p>
7464      * It is recommended that the first parameter type of {@code cleanup} be
7465      * declared {@code Throwable} rather than a narrower subtype.  This ensures
7466      * {@code cleanup} will always be invoked with whatever exception that
7467      * {@code target} throws.  Declaring a narrower type may result in a
7468      * {@code ClassCastException} being thrown by the {@code try-finally}
7469      * handle if the type of the exception thrown by {@code target} is not
7470      * assignable to the first parameter type of {@code cleanup}.  Note that
7471      * various exception types of {@code VirtualMachineError},
7472      * {@code LinkageError}, and {@code RuntimeException} can in principle be
7473      * thrown by almost any kind of Java code, and a finally clause that
7474      * catches (say) only {@code IOException} would mask any of the others
7475      * behind a {@code ClassCastException}.
7476      *
7477      * @param target the handle whose execution is to be wrapped in a {@code try} block.
7478      * @param cleanup the handle that is invoked in the finally block.
7479      *
7480      * @return a method handle embodying the {@code try-finally} block composed of the two arguments.
7481      * @throws NullPointerException if any argument is null
7482      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if {@code cleanup} does not accept
7483      *          the required leading arguments, or if the method handle types do
7484      *          not match in their return types and their
7485      *          corresponding trailing parameters
7486      *
7487      * @see MethodHandles#catchException(MethodHandle, Class, MethodHandle)
7488      * @since 9
7489      */
7490     public static MethodHandle tryFinally(MethodHandle target, MethodHandle cleanup) {
7491         List<Class<?>> targetParamTypes = target.type().parameterList();
7492         Class<?> rtype = target.type().returnType();
7493 
7494         tryFinallyChecks(target, cleanup);
7495 
7496         // Match parameter lists: if the cleanup has a shorter parameter list than the target, add ignored arguments.
7497         // The cleanup parameter list (minus the leading Throwable and result parameters) must be a sublist of the
7498         // target parameter list.
7499         cleanup = dropArgumentsToMatch(cleanup, (rtype == void.class ? 1 : 2), targetParamTypes, 0);
7500 
7501         // Ensure that the intrinsic type checks the instance thrown by the
7502         // target against the first parameter of cleanup
7503         cleanup = cleanup.asType(cleanup.type().changeParameterType(0, Throwable.class));
7504 
7505         // Use asFixedArity() to avoid unnecessary boxing of last argument for VarargsCollector case.
7506         return MethodHandleImpl.makeTryFinally(target.asFixedArity(), cleanup.asFixedArity(), rtype, targetParamTypes);
7507     }
7508 
7509     private static void tryFinallyChecks(MethodHandle target, MethodHandle cleanup) {
7510         Class<?> rtype = target.type().returnType();
7511         if (rtype != cleanup.type().returnType()) {
7512             throw misMatchedTypes("target and return types", cleanup.type().returnType(), rtype);
7513         }
7514         MethodType cleanupType = cleanup.type();
7515         if (!Throwable.class.isAssignableFrom(cleanupType.parameterType(0))) {
7516             throw misMatchedTypes("cleanup first argument and Throwable", cleanup.type(), Throwable.class);
7517         }
7518         if (rtype != void.class && cleanupType.parameterType(1) != rtype) {
7519             throw misMatchedTypes("cleanup second argument and target return type", cleanup.type(), rtype);
7520         }
7521         // The cleanup parameter list (minus the leading Throwable and result parameters) must be a sublist of the
7522         // target parameter list.
7523         int cleanupArgIndex = rtype == void.class ? 1 : 2;
7524         if (!cleanupType.effectivelyIdenticalParameters(cleanupArgIndex, target.type().parameterList())) {
7525             throw misMatchedTypes("cleanup parameters after (Throwable,result) and target parameter list prefix",
7526                     cleanup.type(), target.type());
7527         }
7528     }
7529 
7530 }
